1201 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jennings v. Wessely Energy Corp.


No. 9491


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


720 S.W.2d 811; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 13072



September 9, 1986, Decided  
September 9, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1986, Reported at: 720 S.W.2d 811 at 818.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 115th Judicial District Court of Upshur County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant heirs challenged the order of the 115th Judicial District Court of Upshur County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, oil and gas lease holder and other heirs, as to appellants' claims of an interest in certain property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant heirs sought review of an order, which granted summary judgment to appellees, oil and gas lease holder and other heirs. Appellants claimed an existing interest in the land. In 1954, a deed in the chain of title of appellees was executed and purported to transfer an interest in the property, which would have divested appellants of the property. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1299 (1925) (repealed 1963) required that a husband join a wife in the conveyance of her separate property and that the instrument be acknowledged by the wife privately and apart from her husband. The deed at issue did not comply with this statute. Appellees claimed that the defect in the deed was of no consequence because art. 1299 was subsequently declared unconstitutional and thereby void. The court reversed. The law in effect at the time of the transaction governed, and the trial court was not able to treat the unconstitutional statute as though it never existed. The court held that the doctrine of after-acquired title (estoppel by deed) did not apply because the deed did not convey any future interest to anyone, thus, appellants were not estopped from claiming one.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted summary judgment to appellees, oil and gas lease holder and other heirs, as to appellants' claims of an interest in certain property, and remanded for trial. The law in effect at the time the grantor gave a deed to appellants governed the transaction and, the subsequent repeal of the applicable law did not allow the trial court to treat the unconstitutional statute as if it never existed.

 

1202 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Corpus Christi Taxpayer's Asso. v. Corpus Christi


No. 13-86-023-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


716 S.W.2d 578; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8357



August 29, 1986, Decided  
August 29, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 148th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a summary judgment by the 148th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), entered in favor of appellee city in appellants' action for injunctive and declaratory relief, which contested the validity of the data used and the method by which appellee calculated the effective tax rate under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 26.04 (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers brought an action against appellee city for injunctive and declaratory relief, contesting the validity of the data used and the method by which appellee calculated the effective tax rate and the constitutionality of the state tax code. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee. The court affirmed, holding that appellee complied with the provisions of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 26.04 (1982) in calculating the effective and adopted tax rates. The court found nothing in the record to refute the presumption that there was a valid levy and assessment of appellants' tax liability, made by a legally constituted taxing authority, and that all conditions precedent to the levy and assessment were performed. The court found appellants' claim that appellee overestimated and misrepresented the tax levy was based on hindsight. Because the actual rate of taxation was based on the estimated effective tax amounts, it was virtually impossible for the estimated rate to equal the actual rate. Appellants' constitutional claim was not properly before the court because appellants provided no argument or authority to support their claim on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment, entered in favor of appellee city in an action by appellant taxpayers challenging the validity of the effective tax rate calculated by appellee. The court held that appellee complied with the statutory provisions in calculating the effective tax rate, and that appellants' claims were based upon hindsight.

 

1203 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moffett v. State


Nos. 05-85-01128-CR, 05-85-01129-CR, No.01-86-00446-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


716 S.W.2d 558; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8659



August 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the trial court, Dallas County (Texas), for investing in the manufacturing of a controlled substance, amphetamine, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.052(a)(2). Appellant also challenged a conviction for possession of cocaine. Appellee state contended that the court lacked jurisdiction over these appeals because appellant's notice was untimely.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant for investing in the manufacturing of a controlled substance, amphetamine, in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.052(a)(2) (1986) and for possession of cocaine. Officers had observed appellant buying for cash, large quantities of chemicals and equipment used for drug manufacture. A search of his home revealed a laboratory. On appeal, appellee state contended that the court lacked jurisdiction because the notice of appeal was untimely pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.08(b) (1986). The court disagreed, finding that appellant in his motion for new trial, alternatively gave notice of appeal in the event the motion was overruled. Even assuming the notice of appeal was premature, it was effective to confer jurisdiction on the court. Appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the jury's verdict that he invested in the manufacture of amphetamine. The court held appellant violated § 4.052(a)(2) even though he spent his own money in purchasing chemicals and equipment. From the evidence a jury could find he knew or believed the funds spent were intended for the manufacture of drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court had jurisdiction because appellant in his notice for a new trial alternatively gave notice of appeal in the event the motion was overruled. The statute under which appellant was convicted for investing in drug manufacture was properly applied to him even though he had used his own funds in the purchase of chemicals and equipment.

 

1204 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hunt County Tax Appraisal Dist. v. Rubbermaid, Inc.


No. 05-85-01258-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


719 S.W.2d 215; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9066



August 15, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 13, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF HUNT COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax appraisal district sought review of a judgement by the District Court of Hunt County, Texas in favor of appellee taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxpayer contended the tax roll assessment on the value of its land for three years. An appraisal indicated that the amount was far above market value. The court determined that for the first two years, appellant had paid its taxes based on the increased amount, could not show it did so under duress, and was therefore precluded from any form of reimbursement for the alleged overage. The court found that as to the last year appellant was entitled to judgment in its favor. The court determined that the methods used by the appraiser were sound and that the results were legally acceptable. The court fund that appellee was entitled to attorney fees for the last year because appellee prevailed on appeal. The court reversed and rendered a take nothing judgment as to the first two years, ruled in favor of appellee as to the last year and remanded for further findings as to fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered a take nothing judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer for two of the years and affirmed as to one of the years in question, having determined that the taxes were voluntarily paid in two of the years, and that the reassessed value was correct for the other year.

 

1205 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


GAMEZ v. STATE


No. 01-85-0833-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8280



August 14, 1986 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 424,494


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of voluntary manslaughter from the 182nd District Court, Harris County, Texas. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in refusing to charge the jury on involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arguing with a woman and had slapped her when the victim hit him from behind. Appellant reached into his pocket, removed his knife, and lunged at the victim. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred by refusing to charge the jury with the lesser-included offense of involuntary manslaughter because he did not intend to kill the victim or injure him severely. The court held that appellant was not entitled to a charge on involuntary manslaughter because there was no evidence that appellant could only be guilty of involuntary manslaughter. The court held that appellant was not prejudiced by the court's charge to the jury on the law governing parole and good conduct time pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b). Appellant alleged that the instruction violated Tex. Const. art. II, § I and Tex. Const. art. IV, § 2. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(b) was constitutional and did not invade the province of the executive branch of the government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of voluntary manslaughter. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to charge the jury on the lesser-included offense of involuntary manslaughter because there was no evidence that appellant did not intentionally lunge at the victim with a knife. The court held that appellant was not prejudiced by the jury instruction on parole and that the instruction was constitutional.

 

1206 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rose v. State


No. 05-85-00849-CR, No. 01-86-00446-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


716 S.W.2d 162; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8654



August 13, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 23, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of a district court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of securities fraud.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of securities fraud. The court held that the indictment was not time-barred because the earlier three-year limitation period had not expired prior to the passage of a five-year limitation amendment. The fact that appellant had filed the deed and statement with the county did not give constructive notice of the loan negating an intent to commit fraud because the doctrine of constructive notice, as applied to real property records, was inapplicable in criminal securities fraud cases. The statutory definition of fraud was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad because the statute gave fair notice that the existence of a mortgage was a material fact which had to be disclosed. The expert witness's opinion testimony was admissible in light of the complex nature of the financial transactions. The extraneous offense evidence was admissible because the jury was entitled to know all of the relevant circumstances surrounding the charged offense, the offenses were a part of a continuing episode of conduct, and any error was harmless because the evidence did not contribute to the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of securities fraud because appellant failed to establish reversible error on the part of the trial court.

 

1207 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Willis v. State


No. 05-85-00569-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


724 S.W.2d 87; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 9458



August 11, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Motion for Rehearing December 30, 1986. Rehearing Denied December 31, 1986, Reported at: 724 S.W.2d 87 at 92.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his theft conviction from the District Court, Dallas County, Texas, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §31.03. Appellant alleged that the statute was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in refusing appellant's requested instruction on his good faith purchase defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, owner of a jewelry store, purchased items of jewelry and other valuables for far less than market value from a juvenile. Appellant recorded the transactions, but never asked the juvenile for identification, warranty of ownership, or where he obtained the merchandise. Appellant failed to comply with the provisions of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3). The juvenile was arrested for theft and appellant was indicted for third-degree felony theft pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03. Appellant alleged that the presumption of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3) that a retailer was dealing with stolen property if he failed to comply with the provisions violated his constitutional due process rights. The court held that the presumption was not unconstitutional and that the jury had reasonably concluded that appellant's failure to keep records was because he knew that the property was stolen. The court held that the trial court erred in refusing to charge the jury on the affirmative defense of a good faith purchase of the goods.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's theft conviction and remanded for a new trial because the trial court erred in refusing to charge the jury on the affirmative defense of appellant's good faith purchase of stolen goods. The court held that the statutory presumption that a purchaser of used goods knew that the goods were stolen if he failed to comply with the recording provisions of law did not violate appellant's constitutional right to due process.

 

1208 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Miguez v. State


No. B14-85-403-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


715 S.W.2d 795; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8177



August 7, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 174th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Cause No. 407,818.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 174th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for murder. Appellant contended that the state failed to prove the corpus delecti and therefore, his motion for an instructed verdict should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his murder conviction, arguing that the court erred in refusing to grant his motion for an instructed verdict based on the state's failure to prove the corpus delecti. Appellant was originally charged and convicted of kidnapping the victim. Later, he was convicted of murder after her decomposed remains were found. The court noted that the corpus delecti in a murder prosecution included two elements: (1) the body of the deceased must have been found and identified; (2) the death of the deceased must have been shown to have been caused by the criminal act of another. The court noted that due to the time-gap between commission of the offense and recovery of the body, the identity of the deceased had to be proved by circumstantial evidence. The judgment was affirmed because the cumulative evidence presented by the medical examiner and the victim's son sufficiently established the identity of the deceased, and appellant confessed that he had kidnapped the victim with the intent to inflict bodily harm.


OUTCOME: Appellant's murder conviction was affirmed, and the court found that sufficient evidence was presented by the state to prove the corpus delecti and to connect appellant with the murder of the victim. The court found that cumulative evidence by the victim's son and the medical examiner sufficiently identified her, and appellant's testimony also could have been interpreted in support of a conviction.

 

1209 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Sloan v. Douglass


No. 2-85-095-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


713 S.W.2d 436; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8169



August 7, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 236TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision of the 236th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which denied their postjudgment application for turnover under former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3827a, contending that the trial court erred in finding that, where the employer has agreed to pay the employee income earned in one year, in another year, the future receipts of income are exempt as current wages under Tex. Const. art. XVI § 28.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged a decision of the trial court which denied their postjudgment application for turnover, contending that, despite the fact that the income was earned for services performed during one year, the payment procedure between appellee and his employer called for deferred payments, together with interest in future years, therefore the income stream was not current income, and the exemptions of Tex. Const. art. XVI § 28 did not apply. On appeal, the court examined the controlling state statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3827a, which allowed garnishment of wages, but was in conflict with the constitutional provisions, which should be liberally construed. The court resolved the conflict by applying the controlling constitutional language, rejecting appellants' argument for postjudgment turnover under the applicable property code, Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.001(a). The court held that current wages were not capped, and affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's postjudgment application for turnover.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court denying appellants' postjudgment application for turnover, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the exemption provisions the Texas Constitution controlled as to the definition and amounts of current income for exemption from collection under Texas statute.

 

1210 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Times Herald Printing Co. v. Jones


No. 05-85-00301-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


717 S.W.2d 933; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8939



August 5, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper sought reversal of a judgment of the District Court, Dallas County (Texas) which sealed the records of a civil suit in which the parties to the suit settled without trial, conditioning their settlement upon the sealing of the records. Appellant argued that the sealing order abridge its rights guaranteed under Tex. Const. art. 1, § 8 and violated U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: In the action below, an individual sued a physician seeking damages. The parties to the suit reached a settlement agreement and the lower court entered an agreed final judgment providing that the records of the case be sealed from public access and disclosure. Appellant newspaper sought reversal of the judgment sealing the records, arguing that the judgment abridged its rights under Tex. Const. art. 1, § 8, and violated U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that Tex. Const. art. I, § 8 did not provide greater rights of access to judicial records than U.S. Const. amend. I. As such, the court held that the limited right of access to criminal trials afforded by U.S. Const. amend. I did not mandate the opening of judicial records in a civil suit. Therefore, once the confidentiality order was entered by the lower court and relied on by the parties, the lower court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to unseal the records where appellant failed to show some extraordinary circumstances or compelling need for the records. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment sealing the records in a civil suit, holding that the limited right of access to criminal trials under U.S. Const. did not mandate access of judicial records in a civil suit and once the sealing order was entered and relied upon by the parties, it was not an abuse of discretion to refuse to unseal the records where appellant newspaper did not show extraordinary circumstances or compelling need for the records.

 

1211 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


GILLIAM v. TEXAS


NO. 01-85-01035-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8123



July 31, 1986, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 435,510


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction, from the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), arguing that the jury instruction permitting consideration of the existence of parole violated the separation of powers because the issue of parole was within the purview of the Board of Pardons and Paroles.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction, contending that the jury instruction given by the lower court, authorizing the jury only to consider and discuss the existence of parole and good conduct time, effectively violated the constitutional separation of powers doctrine because parole was a matter within the jurisdiction of the Board of Pardons and Paroles. On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that the constitutionality of a statute may not be raised on appeal unless the issue was first raised in the lower court. The court further held that as there was no objection by appellant's counsel to the portion of the charge urged as a basis for appeal, the argument was waived. The court also found, however, that the jury instruction, that tracked the language of Tex. Crim. P. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) (1985), was valid as it properly reduced or eliminated the amount of misinformation about parole and good conduct time that could be disseminated during jury deliberations.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed as appellant's objection to the jury instruction in question was not preserved for review, and because the instruction properly reduced the amount of misinformation about parole that could be disseminated to the jury.

 

1212 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Nicot-Bardeguez v. Fashing


No. 08-86-00135-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


718 S.W.2d 36; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8064



July 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from AN ORIGINAL PROCEEDING IN MANDAMUS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator wife sought mandamus relief to require respondent judge of the County Court at Law No. 2, El Paso (Texas) to sign a judgment in a divorce proceeding initially referred to a court-appointed master.


OVERVIEW: Relator wife's divorce proceeding was referred to a court-appointed master. The master entered what purported to be a judgment of divorce bearing his signature only. The clerk of the court refused to accept the judgment because it only bore the signature of the master. Relator then filed a motion to enter judgment, which was denied by respondent judge solely on the basis that the master's signature was a sufficient ministerial satisfaction of entry of judgment pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1918b, § 4(b). On review, the court found the last sentence of § 4(b) unconstitutionally ambiguous. Without the offending sentence, the other provisions consistently referred to the master's authority to recommend the judgment to be made in the case and did not express authority to enter judgment. The court held that relator was entitled to an entry of judgment by respondent as the referring judge. Confident that respondent would abide by its decision, the court stated that a writ of mandamus would issue only if respondent failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court held that relator wife was entitled to an entry of judgment by respondent judge because the master's authority was limited to recommending the judgment to be made in the case. The court stated that a writ of mandamus would issue only if respondent failed to abide by the court's decision.

 

1213 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Feinman v. State


No. 01-85-00528-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


717 S.W.2d 106; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8029



July 17, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 10th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 125,882, I. A. Lerner, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a declaratory judgment entered by the 10th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which interpreted the Open Beaches Act (Act), Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. §§ 61.001 et seq., in favor of appellee state. Appellants had brought a declaratory action against appellee, and appellee had filed a counterclaim seeking to have the Act interpreted in its favor.


OVERVIEW: After a hurricane, appellant property owners were notified by the state that their properties were in violation of the Open Beaches Act (Act), Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. §§ 61.001 et seq., (1978 and 1986), because all or a portion of their properties were seaward of the post-hurricane vegetation line. Appellants brought a declaratory judgment suit, requesting the lower court to enter a judgment interpreting the Act in their favor. The state filed a counterclaim, requesting that the lower court declare that the public had an easement over all land located seaward of the natural line of vegetation, and that this easement shifted with the movement of the natural line of vegetation and the mean low tide line. The lower court entered judgment in the state's favor. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The court held that the vegetation line was not stationary and that a rolling easement was implicit in the Act. The court found more than sufficient evidence to support an easement based on implied dedication and that such easement shifted.


OUTCOME: The declaratory judgment in favor of appellee state in appellant property owner's action seeking an interpretation of the Open Beaches Act (Act) was affirmed. Appellant's were in violation of the Act following a hurricane, because a public easement existed based upon an implied dedication, and that that easement was subject to shift.

 

1214 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Earls v. State


No. 04-85-00372-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


715 S.W.2d 731; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8505



July 16, 1986, Decided  
July 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 175th District Court of Bexas County, Trial Court NO. 85-CR-685A, Honorable Phil Chavarria, Judge Presiding, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 175th District Court of Bexas County (Texas) convicting him of aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon as a repeat offender. Defendant argued the court erred in permitting "hearsay by inference" testimony, that a detective talked with two persons in Louisiana, and based on that conversation, issued a warrant for the arrest of defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted by a jury of aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon as a repeat offender. The trial court found the enhancement allegation to be true and assessed punishment at life imprisonment. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in permitting the state, in its opening statement to the jury, to relate that a detective talked with two persons in Louisiana, and based on that conversation, issued a warrant for the arrest of defendant. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that the alleged "hearsay by inference" testimony was properly admitted. The court reasoned that the trial court limited the detective's testimony to a statement that he had a conversation and did not permit him to relate either side of the conversation. The court also ruled that since the arrest of the defendant was not a material issue unless raised by the defendant, any attempt by the state to offer evidence relevant to such issue could have been barred by proper objection by the defense as to relevance. However, because the basis of defendant's objection was hearsay, and the trial judge appropriately restricted the testimony, no error was shown.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery with a deadly weapon as a repeat offender. The court ruled that the detective's testimony was properly admitted because the trial court limited the testimony to a statement that he had a conversation and did not permit him to relate either side of the conversation.

 

1215 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Kelly


No. 07-85-0086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


713 S.W.2d 399; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8021



July 11, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; 181ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 23,096-B; HONORABLE GEORGE E. DOWLEN, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the 181st Judicial District Court, Potter County (Texas), which denied defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus to bar his retrial for the offense of delivery of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of delivery of a controlled substance. That conviction was reversed. The state then again charged defendant with delivery of a controlled substance. Defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus, asserting that through prosecutorial misconduct, the state concealed evidence favorable to him. A witness had revealed to the state that the drugs defendant gave him had fill added. The state did not reveal this information to defendant. Defendant contended that the misconduct operated as a double jeopardy bar to retrial. The trial court denied the writ, and the court of appeals affirmed. Generally, there was no double jeopardy bar to retrial except on a finding of insufficiency of the evidence. However, prosecutorial misconduct could be a bar where the state intended to provoke the defendant into requesting a mistrial. The state did not withhold the information concerning the fill to provoke defendant. Even without the fill, the weight of the narcotic was enough to convict defendant. The court of appeals was bound by the clearly erroneous standard and could not find that the trial court's determination was in error.


OUTCOME: Denial of defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus following his indictment for delivery of a controlled substance after the reversal of his conviction for delivery was affirmed. Double jeopardy could bar retrial where prosecutorial misconduct provoked a defendant into requesting a mistrial. The withholding of information that a container of narcotics contained fill was motivated by a desire to convict, not provoke, defendant.

 

1216 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cuadra v. State


No. B14-85-326-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


715 S.W.2d 723; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7867



July 3, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court at Law, Brazos County, Trial Court No. 1244-84.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the County Court at Law, Brazos County (Texas), which convicted defendant of the misdemeanor offense of tampering with evidence and assessed a fine and one year probation as punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a cadet officer and ordered two cadets to perform exercises from a written list; one cadet died and when an officer telephoned defendant and asked for the list, defendant destroyed the list. Defendant was convicted of the misdemeanor offense of tampering with evidence and assessed a fine and one year probation as punishment. On appeal, defendant argued that the words "investigation" and "privilege" as contained in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.09 (a)(1), (b) (1974) were so inadequately defined that fair notice was not given to defendant. The court disagreed, holding that the terms of the statute were not so vague as to make persons of common intelligence guess as to their meaning. The court held that, as the list was merely an evidentiary, non-testimonial document, the privilege of self-incrimination did not attach and that it was not improper for the trial court to refuse defendant's proposed jury charges as no evidence supported the defense of privilege and the other charge misstated the law. The court held that the trial court submitted all requested instructions on intent and, thus, affirmed the trial court's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that convicted defendant of the misdemeanor offense of tampering with evidence and assessed a fine and one year probation. The court held that the terms of the statute were not so vague so as not to give defendant fair notice of the crime, the list destroyed by defendant was not covered by the privilege of self-incrimination as it was not testimonial, and the jury instructions given were proper.

 

1217 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gersh v. State


No. 05-85-00635-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


714 S.W.2d 80; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8295



June 30, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged his conviction for criminal mischief in a district court of Dallas County (Texas) and argued that a presumption contained in the criminal mischief statute was unconstitutional as applied.


OVERVIEW: Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.03 contained a presumption that, if a gas meter had been tampered with, the person in whose name the gas supply was billed did the tampering. Appellant was convicted of criminal mischief when the trial court applied the presumption and he sought review. The court found that adequate evidence existed to justify the conclusion that the offense of criminal mischief had occurred but no evidence linked appellant himself to the offense. The court held that the statutory presumption operated only against that class of persons who received economic benefit and who were billed by the utility in their own name. The connection between the proven tampering and the name of the person to whom the bill was mailed was arbitrary, lacking a basis in common experience and unconstitutional as applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction and remanded the matter to the trial court on the basis that a statutory presumption that, if a gas meter had been tampered with, the person in whose name the gas supply was billed did the tampering was unconstitutional as applied.

 

1218 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Abilene Oil Distributors, Inc. v. Abilene


No. 11-86-033-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


712 S.W.2d 644; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7951



June 26, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 350th District Court of Taylor County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convenience store owner challenged a ruling of the 350th District Court of Taylor County (Texas), which affirmed appellee Board of Adjustment's denial of appellant's request to sell alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption because the store was located less than 300 feet from a lot used for school purposes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant convenience store owner applied to appellee Board of Adjustment for a license to sell alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption; the store was located in an area zoned "heavy commercial," and a "liquor store" was permitted in an area so zoned subject to special conditions. Appellee denied the variance in accordance with the city's zoning ordinance because the store was within 300 feet of a lot used for school purposes. On review, appellant argued that the city's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional because it was in conflict with Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 109.33 (Supp. 1986), which provided a means of measurement less strict than the city's ordinance. The court affirmed the trial court's decision because Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1011j (1963), permitted a zoning ordinance which imposed "higher standards" to be inconsistent with a state statute, and the city's zoning ordinance did so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee Board of Adjustment's denial of appellant convenience store owner's application for a license to sell alcoholic beverages for off-premises consumption; it would violate the zoning ordinance because of proximity to a lot used for school purposes. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional because of conflict with a state statute when it provided a "higher standard."

 

1219 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rutledge v. Rutledge


No. 2-85-178-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


711 S.W.2d 437; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8080



June 26, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 26, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF WICHITA COUNTY


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought relief through motion for rehearing to contest the jurisdiction of the County Court at Law of Wichita County (Texas), in an action which awarded a divorce between appellant and appellee wife. The county court at law had been established as a non-district court with authority over divorce cases concurrent with that of district courts pursuant to Tex. Const. art. V § 1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband had been divorced from appellee wife by a county court at law, which had been established as a non-district court with authority over divorce cases concurrent with that of district courts pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 1970-166d (1986). After his original appeal, appellant moved for reconsideration, raising for the first time that the statute which conferred divorce jurisdiction on county courts at law conflicted with Tex. Const. art. III § 56, and Tex. Const. art. V § 8. The court reaffirmed the divorce and noted that while Tex. Const. art. III § 56, precluded the legislature from passing any local or special law granting divorce, the purpose of the provision was to ban the legislature's right to grant divorce by a special act. Because the parties were divorced by a properly authorized county court at law rather than by the legislature, there was no violation of Tex. Const. art. III § 56, and the divorce was valid.


OUTCOME: Upon reconsideration, the court again affirmed the divorce between appellant husband and appellee wife because the county court at law which issued the divorce decree had the authority to do so; the constitutional provision that precluded passage of any local or special law granting divorce did not interfere with the legislature's having conferred on the county court at law the power to grant divorces.

 

1220 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Fite v. King


No. 05-85-00820-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


718 S.W.2d 345; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8897



June 23, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 29, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which issued a take-nothing summary judgment for appellee alleged father in appellant's action to establish the paternity of her child. The trial court awarded summary judgment to appellee in appellant's original paternity action based on the statute of limitations of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01. The trial court found the second action barred by res judicata.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother first brought action to establish appellee alleged father's paternity of appellant's minor child, but the trial court granted summary judgment to appellee because the action was barred by the one-year statute of limitations contained in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01, as it existed at that time. Appellant did not challenge that judgment, and it became final. Later, appellant brought a second paternity action, and the trial court granted a take-nothing summary judgment to appellee on the basis that action was barred by the doctrine of res judicata. The court held that the fact that § 13.01, was declared unconstitutional after the judgment in the original action had become final, did not prevent application of res judicata. Appellant acquiesced in the application of the statute by not appealing from the original judgment. The court held that the proper affirmative statute of limitations defense satisfied the requirements for the rendition of a valid and final judgment. Thus, appellant's second paternity claim was barred by the doctrine of res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment rendered by the trial court to appellee alleged father in appellant mother's action to establish paternity of her minor child because it was barred by res judicata. The fact that the statute of limitations, which barred appellant's first paternity action was later declared unconstitutional did not make that judgment void ab initio so as to render it assailable as a void judgment in a collateral attack.

 

1221 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hearne v. Williams


No. 10-85-269-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


715 S.W.2d 375; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7822



June 19, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: From 82nd Judicial District Court; Robertson County, Texas; Trial Court #12,812.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the judgment of the 82nd Judicial District Court, Robertson County, Texas, rendered against it in a negligence case arising out of damage caused to plaintiff airplane owner's airplane at defendant's municipal airport.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff airplane owner brought a negligence action against defendant city, alleging that defendant's employees failed to provide proper tie ropes to tie down plaintiff's airplane at defendant's municipal airport and caused damage to plaintiff's airplane when a wind blew it over. The trial court rendered in favor of plaintiff against defendant. On appeal, defendant asserted the trial court erred in rendering judgment for plaintiff because the acts of defendant were protected from liability by the doctrine of governmental immunity and there was no waiver of the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 6252-19. The court reversed, holding that governmental immunity was not waived by defendant's city charter because the defense of governmental immunity could be waived or abolished only by a specific act of the legislature and under art. 6252-19, liability of a unit of government was limited to personal injuries or death of a person; and to property only when caused by the negligent acts of a governmental unit's employees in the operation of a motor vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment rendered against defendant city in a negligence case because defendant was protected from liability by the doctrine of governmental immunity and the alleged negligence was not within the limited waiver of immunity provided by the Texas Tort Claims Act.

 

1222 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas State Teachers Asso. v. State


No. 14,676


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


711 S.W.2d 421; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7808; 64 A.L.R.4th 631



June 13, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 17, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 384,936, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, teachers association and others, sought review from the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), that denied appellants' motion for summary judgment and granted appellees', the Central Education Agency, the State Board of Education and others, summary judgment motion, and declared Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 13.047 (1986), constitutional and denied appellants' requested injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, teachers association and others, filed suit against appellees, the Central Education Agency, the State Board of Education and others, seeking a declaratory judgment that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 13.047 (1986) was unconstitutional on its face and as implemented by appellees. Appellants sought an injunction prohibiting appellees from implementing the testing law, which would impose certain competency testing requirements on certified school teachers and administrators. Appellants asserted that teachers' certificates were statutory contracts, which could not be impaired in violation of the contract clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, or retroactive law violations of Tex. Const. Ann. art. I, § 16 (1984). The trial court denied appellants' motion for summary judgment and request for injunctive relief declaring § 13.047 constitutional. The court affirmed the judgment because it found that regulation of the teaching profession and of the public education system were valid exercises of the state's police power and nothing in § 13.047 prohibited appellees from administering the literacy and knowledge components of the examination in stages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which denied appellants', teacher's association and others, motion for summary judgment and request for injunctive relief because the court held that regulation of the teaching profession and of the public education system were valid exercises of police power and any impairment of appellants' rights which occurred was justified as an incident to the valid exercise of the state's police power.

 

1223 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


ANDERSON v. STATE


No. 01-85-00950-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7716



June 12, 1986


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 423,305


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant offender appealed a judgment from the 263rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which entered a jury conviction for compelling prostitution. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to set aside the indictment, in its charge to the jury, in denying a speedy trial, in overruling defendant's objection to the relevancy of a witness' testimony, and that defendant had ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offender was arrested and convicted by a jury for compelling prostitution. Defendant asserted the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to set aside the indictment. The court affirmed the judgment finding the indictment sufficient under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.05(a)(2) and that it was not necessary for the indictment to allege all or even any of the means used to compel prostitution. Defendant claimed the jury charge was fundamental error but the court found no objection had been leveled at trial and held reversal would only be mandated if defendant had been denied a fair and impartial trial. Defendant claimed denial of a speedy trial under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 32A.02 (1986), ineffective assistance of counsel, and that the trial court erred in overruling defendant's objection to the relevancy of a witness' testimony. The court concluded that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to dismiss because the state produced evidence at the hearing that it was then ready for trial, the record reflected that counsel throughout trial represented appellant in a reasonably effective manner, and that the witness testimony complained of was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the court found the indictment was statutorily sufficient, no objection had been preserved at trial against the charge, defendant had not been denied a fair trial, the state had not delayed the proceedings, defendant's counsel had been reasonable effective, and defendant had not suffered harm due to the complained of witness' testimony.

Casares v. State


No. 01-85-000829-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


712 S.W.2d 818; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7719



June 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 425,558.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 262nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which entered a conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of theft of a motor vehicle of a value over $ 750 and under $ 20,000. Defendant asserted that the trial court reversibly erred in failing to allow defense counsel to fully cross-examine the state's witnesses in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of theft of a motor vehicle of a value of over $ 750 and under $ 20,000. Defendant raised three points of error on appeal. First, defendant asserted that the trial court erred in failing to allow defense counsel to fully cross-examine the state's witnesses in violation of defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VI rights. The court held that defendant had failed to preserve the error by not making a bill of exceptions showing what the witnesses testimony would have been if defendant had been allowed to elicit their answers. Defendant's second and third points of error claimed that the trial court's jury instruction was unconstitutional because it was in violation of the separation of powers requirement and because it was vague. The court held the issues had not been raised at the trial court below and could not be urged for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that the trial court should have allowed defendant offender broad latitude in the examination of the witnesses; however, because defendant failed to perfect a bill of exception to show what the testimony would have been if defendant had been allowed to elicit answers, the there was nothing preserved in the record for review.

 

1225 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Carrasco v. State


No. 13-85-384-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


712 S.W.2d 623; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7721



June 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from County Court at Law No. 2 of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the County Court at Law No. 2, Hidalgo County (Texas), which convicted him of unlawful use of a criminal instrument and assessed punishment of a $ 150 fine and 20 days in jail which was probated for 1 year. Appellant challenged the validity of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 16.01(a)(1) (1986) and the sufficiency of the complaint and the information.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was searched after he was arrested for public intoxication and the police found a wire with a loop on the end, two screwdrivers, and a pair of pliers. Appellant stated that he had not burglarized any cars, but that he had planned to do so. The trial court denied appellant's motion to quash and appellant pled guilty. A police report that contained his admission that he intended to burglarize automobiles was offered and accepted into evidence without objection from appellant. Appellant was convicted of unlawful use of a criminal instrument. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The wire with a loop at the end, found on appellant's person, was specially designed or made for use in the burglary of vehicles and appellant admitted his intent to so use the wire. Because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 16.01 (1986) clearly applied to appellant's conduct, he could not successfully challenge it for vagueness. The court found that the complaint and information substantially tracked the language of § 16.01, setting forth an offense against the state in plain and intelligible words and providing appellant with notice of the nature of the charge against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of unlawful use of a criminal instrument finding that the statute upon which the prosecution was based was not vague because it clearly applied to appellant's conduct. The court also found that the complaint and the information substantially tracked the language of the statute upon which the charge was based providing appellant with notice of the nature of the charge against him.

 

1226 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Whittemore v. State


No. 09-85-254-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


712 S.W.2d 607; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8026



June 11, 1986, Decided  
June 11, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 217TH DISTRICT COURT OF ANGELINA COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the 217th District Court of Angelina County (Texas). Appellant had been convicted by a jury of aggravated sexual assault. The court assessed punishment at 50 years in the Texas Department of Corrections. Appellant asserted grounds that his right to counsel and his right to confrontation were violated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that statements made by appellant to a cellmate were not the result of "custodial interrogation" and did not violate appellant's right to counsel. The court concluded that the entering of taped testimony of a child pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. § 38.071 did not violate appellant's right to confrontation. The court reasoned that the state could prevail over a fundamental right upon a showing that the statute was necessary to the accomplishment of a compelling state interest. The court held that the state had a legitimate interest in protecting children from the emotional harm that could be endured due to legal proceedings and repeated interrogations and that § 38.071 was designed to reduce the risk of harm. The court found that it was within the trial court's discretion to admit a tape when the challenge was to its quality. The court also found that admission of a written statement did not violate appellant's right to an attorney where appellant contacted district attorney several times without the district attorney having sought a statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding that neither appellant's right to counsel nor his right to confrontation were violated in the trial court proceedings.

Gelabert v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the 262nd District Court of Harris County, Texas that entered two convictions against defendant for attempted capital murder of a police officer. The court had twice remanded the case to the trial court for appointment of counsel after defendant filed motions for self-representation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction for attempted capital murder of a police officer. Defendant requested removal of the trial counsel so that she could represent herself. The trial court granted the defendant's request. The court abated the appeal and instructed the trial court to appoint counsel to assure the effective assistance of counsel on appeal. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for attempted capital murder because defendant had not shown that, but for her counsel's error, the result of the proceeding would have been different or that she was thereby denied a fair and impartial trial.

DILLON v. STATE


No. B14-85-140-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7599



May 29, 1986


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 413,796


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgement of the 184th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted her of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the fact that defendant was charged under the aggravated robbery statute rather than the theft statute did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction to hear the case, as the theft statute was not more specific than the aggravated robbery statute. The court ruled that the means of committing the offense was more specific in the aggravated robbery statute, and that defendant was properly charged under the aggravated robbery statute. The court further held that defendant's motion to quash the indictment was properly denied because the terms "uses" and "exhibits" used in the indictment were not unconstitutional vague and in themselves gave defendant fair notice of the prohibited act. Further, the court rejected defendant's argument that the lineup identifications violated her right to counsel because defendant did not make such an objection at trial, and therefore, defendant's right to counsel argument was not preserved for review on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated robbery. The court found that the trial court properly overruled defendant's motion to quash the indictment because defendant was given fair notice of the prohibited act. Also, the court rejected defendant's argument of a violation of her right to counsel with respect to the lineup identification because she did not object at trial.

NELLUMS v. STATE


NO. 01-85-00347-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7517



May 22, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 178th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 411,331


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the 178th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of assault on a law enforcement officer. The trial court charged the jury that it could consider the presumption provided in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.03(b), which stated that because the officer was wearing a distinctive uniform, defendant was presumed to have known he was a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of deadly assault on a law enforcement officer. On appeal, the court concluded that the attire worn by the peace officer constituted a "distinctive uniform" under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.03(b) so that the trial court properly charged the jury regarding the statutory presumption that defendant knew from the uniform that the person he assaulted was a peace officer. In addition, defense counsel's failure to object to the jury charge regarding the uniform served to waive any error. The court found that the evidence was sufficient, even without the application of the statutory presumption, to establish defendant's knowledge that the person he assaulted was a peace officer. Lastly, the court found that closing remarks by the prosecutor to which defendant failed to object were not so extreme as to deprive defendant of a fair trial or so prejudicial as to constitute reversible error. The court overruled all of defendant's points of error and affirmed the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of deadly assault on a law enforcement officer, concluding that the attire worn by the officer constituted a distinctive uniform under the statutory presumption, and even without application of the presumption, sufficient evidence existed to establish defendant's knowledge that the person he assaulted was a peace officer.

 

1230 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. State


No. 13-85-037-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


713 S.W.2d 697; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7585



May 22, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 103rd District court of Cameron County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 103rd District Court, Cameron County (Texas) for involuntary manslaughter under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2) (1974) and contended that the trial court erred when it overruled his motion to dismiss the indictment on the ground that he was denied his right to a speedy trial under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2) (1974). He challenged his conviction contending that he had been denied his right to a speedy trial under the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1986). The court agreed and reversed the conviction. The court disagreed with the state's contention that the Speedy Trial Act was unconstitutional because its caption failed to give fair notice of the effect of the Act as required by Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. The caption could not be construed as failing to give fair notice to a reasonable reader of the subject and contents of the Act. It informed the reader that the law relating to speedy trial of criminal cases had been amended and added to. The court also rejected the contention that the Speedy Trial Act constituted an encroachment of the legislature on the authority of the courts. No authority was cited for this proposition. It was not an encroachment because it disposed of cases solely on the procedural ground of undue prosecutorial delay and without regard to the guilt or innocence of the accused.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter because he had been denied his right to a speedy trial.

B & B Vending Co. v. Garland


No. 12-84-0103-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


711 S.W.2d 132; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7625



May 22, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 101ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business licensee sought review of the declaratory judgment of the 101st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which was rendered in favor of appellee city in appellant's action for declaratory judgment that City of Garland, Tex., Ordinance No. 3447 conflicted with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8814 (Supp. 1986). The ordinance prohibited the location of coin-operated machines within 300 feet of residential property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant business licensee contracted with a restaurant to exhibit three video games. Appellee city's ordinance prohibited the location of coin-operated machines with 300 feet of residentially zoned property. The restaurant fell within this limitation. Appellee refused to issue a permit to appellant for video games to be exhibited at that location. Appellant sought a declaratory judgment that City of Garland, Tex., Ordinance No. 3447 conflicted with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8814 (Supp. 1986), and was therefore is unconstitutional. Appellee sought a declaratory judgment, alleging that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court ordered that appellant take nothing. The court reversed, holding that under the plain and unambiguous language of Tex. Const. art. III § 35, the statute was valid. The ordinance went beyond the statute and placed an additional restriction prohibiting the location of such machines within 300 feet of residentially zoned property. Insofar as the ordinance forbid the location of such machines within 300 feet of residentially zoned property, it was in conflict with the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and rendered a declaratory judgment for appellant business licensee. It held that the portion of the statute relating to the location and regulation of coin-operated machines was constitutional, and that appellee city's ordinance, to the extent that it purported to prohibit the location of coin-operated amusement machines within 300 feet of residentially zoned property, was void and unenforceable.

 

1232 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Matcha v. Mattox


No. 14,384


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


711 S.W.2d 95; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7799



May 21, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 354,178, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, home owners, sought review of the judgment of the 250th District Court, Travis County (Texas), which directed a verdict for appellee, attorney general, in an action to remove appellants' house from the beach on the grounds that the property line had shifted giving the public an easement and right of access to appellants' property.


OVERVIEW: After a violent hurricane, the remains of a beach house owned by appellants, home owners, were located entirely seaward of the natural line of vegetation on the beach. Appellee, attorney general, sought to enjoin appellants from repairing their house on the grounds that the public had acquired rights in the beach area where appellants' house stood. The trial court granted judgment for appellee, and the court affirmed holding that the public had acquired a right of use or an easement in the vicinity of appellants' property by custom. The court held that the doctrine of custom had been acknowledged in Texas' courts and that there was proof to support the conclusion that the public acquired an easement over appellants' property by custom. The court further held that public easements shifted with the natural movements of the beach and thus the easement now encompassed appellants' property. The court further held that the issue of the vegetation line was not an issue which could be finally adjudicated, but must always remain open to relitigation.


OUTCOME: Judgment ordering removal of appellants, home owners', beach front home affirmed because the public had acquired a right of access and easement to the property through the shifting of the vegetation line, and the issue of the vegetation line was always open to relitigation.

 

1233 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Gibson v. Marsh


No. 08-86-00071-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


710 S.W.2d 107; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12973



May 14, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 710 S.W.2d 107 at 109.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN ORIGINAL PROCEEDING IN MANDAMUS Original Opinion of April 23, 1986, Reported at: 710 S.W.2d 107.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator attorney sought a rehearing of the mandamus relief granted by the Court of Appeals of Texas, Eighth District, El Paso, to readdress the fees set by respondent trial court for relator's court-appointed representation of an indigent criminal defendant.


OVERVIEW: Relator attorney, who had been granted partial mandamus relief to have respondent trial court set a reasonable fee for relator's court-appointed representation of an indigent criminal defendant, sought a rehearing to challenged the reasonableness of the fees. Relator had been granted the mandamus relief when respondent had refused to set any fee in his case because relator had not complied with the El Paso schedule. The court found that the El Paso schedule set fees at three times the minimum fee authorized under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.05. In denying the motion for rehearing, the court concluded that the El Paso schedule was reasonable and that relator had waived the right to seek a greater amount by failing to obtain approval for such within five days of the judgment as required by art. 26.05, §2.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator attorney's motion for rehearing on his writ of mandamus because the fees set by respondent trial court in accordance with the El Paso schedule for representing an indigent criminal defendant were three times the minimum authorized by Texas law, and therefore, reasonable.

Briggs v. State


No. 05-85-00894-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


714 S.W.2d 36; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 8293



May 13, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of a chemical dispensing device under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06 (1986).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for possession of a chemical dispensing device under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06 (1986). The court reversed and remanded for dismissal of the indictment because § 46.06 was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the statute excepted small chemical dispensers from its prohibition, but it failed to give guidance as to what "small" was. The court held that its inability to define precisely the scope of the prohibition demonstrated that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.06(a)(7) was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that convicted appellant of possession of a chemical dispensing device and remanded for dismissal of the indictment because the statute was unconstitutionally vague and unenforceable as a penal sanction. The statute excepted small chemical dispensers but failed to give guidance as to what "small" was. Its inability to define precisely the scope of the prohibition demonstrated that it was unconstitutionally vague.

Ex parte Lopez


No. 04-85-00155-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


710 S.W.2d 948; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7524



April 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring and Dissenting Opinion May 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Relator's Application for Writ of Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator husband filed a writ of habeas corpus seeking an order directing the district court (Texas) to release him from custody, where he was being held in contempt for failure to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: Relator husband was held in contempt for failing to pay child support and was committed to jail for 30 days and until the arrearages and costs were paid. He sought a writ of habeas corpus directing his discharge. The court granted the writ and ordered relator discharged. The court found that the imprisonment for 30 days was punitive and, thus, a criminal proceeding. The court concluded that because indigent relator was not represented by counsel, and did not intentionally and intelligently waive his right to assistance of counsel, the trial court violated relator's U.S. Const. amend. VI right by imposing imprisonment. The court found that the support arrearages and court costs were civil contempt, but were also punitive in nature because relator did not have the ability to pay to purge the contempt. The court held that relator was not entitled to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court granted relator husband's writ of habeas corpus and ordered relator discharged. The court held that relator was denied his Sixth Amendment right to counsel in the contempt proceedings and he was not entitled to a jury trial.

 

1236 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mustard v. State


No. 05-85-00723-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


711 S.W.2d 71; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7766



April 29, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of a Texas trial court, which convicted him of bribery of a deputy marshal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant asked a deputy marshal a question that suggested that appellant wanted information that would permit appellant to make unauthorized changes to records in the city's computers. The deputy reported this to his supervisors, and the police guided him in providing appellant access codes to the computers in exchange for money. Appellant was arrested at the scene of the exchange and convicted of bribery. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that there was sufficient evidence of the elements of bribery under Tex. Penal Code § 36.02, that Dallas, Tex., Rev. Ordinances ch. 33A, § 7.4(1)(4), having to do with city employees' disclosure of information, was not void for vagueness, and that the caption of the bill enacting Tex. Penal Code § 36.02(b) was not fatally defective. The court further held that although the trial court erred in failing to quash the indictment for insufficient notice of the offense, the error did not prejudice appellant, that appellant was given notice of what he would be called upon to defend against, that appellant was not entrapped as a matter of law, and that the codes were not available under the Open Records Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of bribery was affirmed because there was sufficient evidence of the elements of the offense, a statute establishing duties of the deputy marshal whom appellant bribed was not void for vagueness, and appellant was not entrapped as a matter of law.

Breeze v. Breeze


No. 2-85-196-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


707 S.W.2d 298; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12805



April 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 324th District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a judgment from the 324th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted a divorce from appellee wife, divided the property pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.63 (1986), and made findings of fact and conclusions of law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband challenged the trial court's division of property in a divorce action that was instituted by appellee wife. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dividing the estate. The court held that the trial court did not impermissibly consider sex as a factor in its division of the community estate, and that appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.63 (1986). Appellant offered no proof that the trial court discriminated against him because he was male. The court also held that appellant lacked standing to raise an equal protection claim under U.S. Const. amends. V or XIV. The court held that there was sufficient cause for appellant to prosecute his appeal and that it was not done only for delay. Appellee was not entitled to recover attorney's fees as damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment that divided the property between appellant husband and appellee wife was affirmed. The trial court did not impermissibly consider sex as a factor in its division of the community estate. Appellee was not entitled to recover attorney's fees because there was sufficient cause for appellant to prosecute his appeal.

Pequeno v. State


No. 01-84-00397-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


710 S.W.2d 709; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12827



April 24, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 380,678, Patricia Lykos, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to confinement following his guilty plea for aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of true to the state's allegation that he violated his probation, which he was placed on for an aggravated assault conviction, after he continued to contact the complainant, from whom he was prohibited from having any contact. The trial court revoked defendant's probation and sentenced him to prison. Defendant appealed and alleged that the trial court erred because the probation condition was unreasonable, that the terms of his probation violated his constitutional right to travel, and that his punishment was cruel and unusual. The court affirmed and held that because the only way to achieve the essential objective of defendant's probation was to prohibit his contact with the complainant, the condition was not unreasonable or ambiguous. The revocation of probation was based solely on the finding that defendant had contacted the complainant, therefore, a ruling on any alleged violation of the travel restriction was unnecessary. Because the punishment assessed by the trial court was within the limits prescribed by Tex. Penal Code Ann § 22.02(c) (Supp. 1986) for third degree felonies under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.34 (1974), it was not cruel and unusual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's revocation of defendant's probation after he violated probation conditions. The court held that the probation condition that defendant restrain from contacting the complainant was reasonable and unambiguous, that his plea of true to the violations was sufficient to support the revocation, and that the punishment was not cruel and unusual.
