Gibson v. Marsh


No. 08-86-00071-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


710 S.W.2d 107; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12765



April 23, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 14, 1986, Reported at: 710 S.W.2d 107 at 109.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM AN ORIGINAL PROCEEDING IN MANDAMUS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator attorney sought mandamus relief to compel respondent judge to set a reasonable fee as compensation for relator's trial representation of an indigent criminal defendant.


OVERVIEW: Relator attorney sought mandamus relief to compel respondent judge to set a reasonable fee as compensation for relator's trial representation of an indigent criminal defendant. The trial lasted four days for which relator submitted a voucher for pay far greater than that permitted under state or county maximum fees. The trial court rejected relator's voucher, and relator sought mandamus relief alleging that unless forced service was accompanied by reasonable compensation, the appointment was involuntary servitude, prohibited by U.S. Const. amend. XIII. The court granted relator's petition to the extent that respondent was required to set a reasonable fee for relator's appointed service. All other relief sought was denied. The court found no basis for requiring an attorney to submit a voucher limited to the fees set by the state or the county district judges and to use an excessive claim as an excuse to delay setting a fee. Relator submitted a voucher, which while apparently exceeding the county fee schedule was nonetheless adequate for respondent to set a reasonable fee.


OUTCOME: Relator attorney's petition for mandamus relief was granted in part and denied in part because respondent judge should have set a reasonable fee for relator's appointed service for representing an indigent criminal defendant.

 

1240 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Schismatic & Purported Casa Linda Presbyterian Church v. Grace Union Presbytery, Inc.


No. 05-85-00599-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


710 S.W.2d 700; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7725



April 18, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from A district Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, withdrawing church members, sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which held that title to the church's real and personal property vested in appellees, church members who remained loyal to the parent church.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, withdrawing church members, challenged the trial court's finding that title to church property vested in appellees, remaining members loyal to the parent church. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that the trial court's judgment based on the deference rule did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I and amend. XIV. The court rejected appellants' argument that a U.S. Supreme Court case required that the court apply the neutral principles of law theory to determine ownership of church property; rather the states had the option of which theory to use. Under the deference rule, which was the precedent for the state, the court deferred to the parent church's identity of the loyal members as the representatives of the local church. An erroneous finding of fact and legal conclusion did not alter the trial court's judgment where the judgment was supported by other findings. The trial court's error in decreeing title in the church as a corporate entity was reformed by the appellate court to reflect the actual party.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that decreed appellees, loyal church members, the owners of the church's property, based on the deference rule, which was held to be the controlling precedent. Under this rule, the trial court deferred to the judgment of the parent church as to the identity of the rightful owners of the property.

PALMER v. STATE


No. A14-85-226-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12685



April 17, 1986 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law of Brazos County, Cause No. 275-85


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the County Criminal Court at Law of Brazos County (Texas), which convicted him of the offense of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1. Appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient to convict him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of driving while intoxicated. The trial court denied appellant's motion to quash the information on the grounds that the definition of intoxication under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701 1-1 was unconstitutionally vague to provide notice. The trial court also denied appellant's motion to quash the complaint and information because they were both file stamped at the same time, and the trial court denied appellant's motion to set aside the information under the Speedy Trial Act (Act), Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, because the state failed to comply with the procedural dictates. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that appellant's actions, of stumbling out of the vehicle, the failure of two field sobriety tests, and appellant's comment to the officer that he was drunk, were sufficient evidence. The court found that appellant presented no evidence that he was not tried within the time limit established by the Act and overruled his point of error. The court found that because appellant was convicted on his physical actions, the definition of intoxication and notice were inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which convicted appellant of the offense of driving while intoxicated because the record reflected that appellant was convicted on evidence that went directly to his impaired physical and mental faculties, and not to any specific blood alcohol level, so that appellant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally vague in its definition of intoxication was useless.

Grand Prairie Hospital Authority v. Tarrant Appraisal Dist.


No. 02-85-00180-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


707 S.W.2d 281; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12646



April 17, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 153rd district court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital authority challenged the order of the 153rd District Court, Tarrant County, Texas, which granted appellee taxing authorities' pleas to jurisdiction, and dismissed appellant's action seeking a declaratory judgment that its property was exempt from taxation based on Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4437e, § 16.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital authority filed an action against appellee taxing authorities seeking a declaratory judgment that its property was exempt from taxation as a matter of law. The lower court granted appellee's pleas to jurisdiction and dismissed the action without prejudice. Appellant challenged the judgment, and the court affirmed. The court held that under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4437e, § 16, appellant's property must have been held only for public purpose in order to be tax exempt. The court found that appellant's property was not used exclusively for the use and benefit of the public as private doctors were leasing part of the property for their own commercial enterprise. Therefore, the court ruled that, as appellant's property was not exempt as a matter of law, appellant was required to exhaust its administrative remedies before seeking judicial review. Because appellant did not exhaust administrative remedies, the lower court did not err in dismissing the claim for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant hospital authority's declaratory judgment action against appellee taxing authorities as the trial court lacked jurisdiction because appellant's property was not used exclusively for public purposes and they did not exhaust administrative remedies before seeking judicial review.

Texas Employment Comm'n v. Camarena


Nos. 14479, 14,532


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


710 S.W.2d 665; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7632



April 16, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied June 3, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT NOS. 369,808-A and 369,808, HONORABLE HARLEY CLARK, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants commission and officials appealed from the judgment of the 201st District Court of Travis County (Texas) enjoining enforcement of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221b-17(g)(5)(B) (1971), upon declaring unconstitutional the statute's exclusion of agricultural labor from unemployment compensation coverage. Plaintiffs union and workers cross-appealed an order denying, on sovereign immunity grounds, motions for attorneys' fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Texas Unemployment Compensation Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221b-17(g)(5)(B) (1971), agricultural workers were not eligible for unemployment compensation benefits. In a challenge by plaintiffs union and workers, the trial court enjoined defendants commission and officials from enforcing the exclusion upon declaring it unconstitutional. Plaintiffs' motion for attorneys' fees and court costs was denied, however, on sovereign immunity grounds. Defendants and plaintiffs appealed. Meanwhile, an amendment to the Act took effect to provide coverage for agricultural workers. In reversing and remanding with instructions to dismiss the main judgment, the court ruled that plaintiffs' claims were moot given the amendment that eliminated the exclusion complained of. In affirming the order denying plaintiffs' motion for attorneys' fees, the court ruled that the statute relied on by plaintiffs, the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 37.009 (1986), did not provide a waiver of the state's immunity from monetary liability. On the other hand, costs were not subject to governmental immunity, so the denial of costs was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment against defendants was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to dismiss because, pending appeal, a legislative amendment to the statute took effect to remove the agricultural labor exception, thereby mooting plaintiffs' suit. The denial of fees was affirmed because the state had not legislatively waived its immunity from liability. The denial of costs was reversed because governmental immunity did not apply to costs.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Taylor County.

On appeal, appellant asserted that § 1.04(2) was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain. The court affirmed the conviction. Thus, appellant's public exposure of her vagina was a clear violation of § 1.04(2) and not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecent exposure of person on premises where beer was sold because appellant did not have to guess at the meaning of this statutory prohibition and her indecent conduct was a clear violation of the law.

Lopez v. State


Appeal No. 04-85-00212-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


709 S.W.2d 744; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 7529



April 9, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 341st District Court of Webb County, Trial Court No. 19,442, Honorable Elma Teresa Salinas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 341st District Court of Webb County (Texas), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2) (1974), assessed punishment, and recommended that the term be probated. The trial court imposed a special condition of probation that required appellant to serve 120 days in confinement pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12B, § 6b(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2) (1974). The jury assessed punishment and recommended that the term be probated but did not probate the fine. The trial court imposed a special condition of probation that required appellant to serve 120 days in confinement pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12B, § 6b(c). The court affirmed and held that the 120-day confinement condition of probation did not violate appellant's constitutional rights to due process or equal protection of the law. The court held that appellant failed to show that the statute was ambiguous or that the mandatory language of the statute created suspect classifications. The court held that the trial court had the power and authority to require appellant to serve 120 days in a penal institution as a condition of the probation recommended by the jury. The court held that the fine was not required to have been probated because the jury specifically recommended that the fine not be probated. The mandatory confinement did not constitute double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of involuntary manslaughter by reason of intoxication and, pursuant to statute, imposed a condition of probation that he serve 120 days in confinement. Condition of probation did not violate appellant's constitutional rights to due process, equal protection of the law, or double jeopardy. Probation of fine was not required because the jury specifically recommended that it not be.

Tobin Landscape & Constr. Co. v. Bramlett

1248 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Corpus Christi Independent School Dist. v. Padilla


No. 13-85-487-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


709 S.W.2d 700; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12508



March 27, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 24, 1986, Reported at: 709 S.W.2d 700 at 709.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district and appellant superintendent sought review of a judgment from the 347th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which granted a motion by appellee school employees for summary judgment and which issued injunctive relief. Appellees had filed suit after appellant school district denied their request for review by the board of trustees of an adverse decision on appellees' grievances.


OVERVIEW: Appellee school employees filed grievances after their work assignments were changed. Appellant superintendent denied appellees' grievances, and appellant school district denied appellees' request for review before the board of trustees. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment and issued injunctive relief. The court reversed. Appellees were not denied their rights under Tex. Const. art. I, § 27 to file grievances with the proper authority. Article I, § 27 did not impose an affirmative duty on the government to provide a grievance procedure; the government only had to "consider" the grievance. Although appellees were barred from seeking review by the board, they were provided access to the board through an open forum at the end of each board meeting. Appellant school district's policy also did not violate Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5154c, § 6 (1971). This statute only required that public employees have access to those in a position of authority to present their grievances; it did not require that presentation of grievances be made to the board. The board was empowered to delegate its authority to appellant superintendent to remedy appellees' grievances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee school employees, dissolved the injunction, and rendered summary judgment in favor of appellant school district and appellant superintendent. Appellant school district's policy that foreclosed review by the board of trustees of adverse grievance determinations did not violate appellees' constitutional or statutory rights.

Dahl v. State


No. 3-85-080-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


707 S.W.2d 694; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12775



March 26, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 76,553, HONORABLE MACE B. THURMAN, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 147th District Court, Travis County (Texas), where he had pled guilty and was convicted of driving while intoxicated, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to driving while intoxicated, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1 (1983). He brought three grounds of error: the definition of "intoxication" in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(a)(2)(B) (1983) was impermissibly vague in violation of U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19; article. 6701l-1 (1983) violated due process because it was vague; and the indictment should have alleged the manner and means by which appellant "operated" a motor vehicle. The court affirmed. The court held that a statute may have been challenged for vagueness either on its face or as applied in a particular case. Appellant's Intoxilyzer reading was .21. Under any interpretation of the statute, he was intoxicated, as the highest reading that appellant contended would be necessary to demonstrate intoxication based on a breath test was .21. Therefore, the statute could not have been void as applied to appellant. The notice required by due process was "fair notice." The statute gave adequate notice of the proscribed conduct. The allegation that appellant "operated" a motor vehicle was adequate to put appellant on notice of the charge against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because the charging statute was not void as it was applied to appellant. The fact that appellant "operated" a motor vehicle was adequate notice of the charge against him. Appellant was given fair notice that his conduct, in driving after drinking, would have violated the law.

 

1251 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Leal v. Mather


No. C14-86-00138-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


709 S.W.2d 269; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12551



March 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring Opinion March 20, 1986.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator judge filed a petition for writ of mandamus challenging the sufficiency of the petition filed by the real party in interest, a candidate, under the Texas Election Code. Relator claimed that only 247 petition signatures were valid instead of the requisite 250 required under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 172.024(c-1).


OVERVIEW: The real party in interest, a candidate, filed an application to be placed on the primary ballot for the position of criminal court judge. Relator judge challenged the sufficiency of the petition, claiming it had only 247 valid signatures instead of the requisite 250. Specifically, he challenged the validity of thirteen signatures. In reviewing relator's petition for writ of mandamus, the court addressed the first three signatures challenged by relator as invalid due to an incomplete signing as to the date. The court overruled that challenge, holding that in view of all the circumstances, the signature dates could not mean anything other than January 22, 1986. In so holding, the court noted that the preceding signatures reflected a January 22, 1986 completion date, the person circulating the petition swore by affidavit to the circulation of the petition in on January 21 and 22, 1986, and the petition form showed an issuance date of 1/86. Having overruled these challenges, at least 250 valid signatures appeared on the petition and the validity of the remaining challenged signatures were not addressed.


OUTCOME: Relator judge's petition for writ of mandamus was denied as the date of signing of three signatures, though incomplete, could not mean anything but January 22, 1986. As these signatures were valid, the petition had sufficient valid signatures to meet the requirements of the Texas Election Code.

 

1252 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McGlothlin v. State


No. 2-84-276-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


705 S.W.2d 851; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12752



March 13, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 97TH DISTRICT COURT OF MONTAGUE COUNTY



DISPOSITION:  Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 97th District Court of Montague County (Texas), which convicted appellant, after a jury trial, of possession of amphetamine over 400 grams under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.042(d)(2) (Vernon Supp. 1986), and sentenced him to 25 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of possession of amphetamine over 400 grams and was sentenced to 25 years confinement. On review, appellant complained generally of an illegal search and seizure, insufficient evidence to support the jury verdict, error in the jury charge, jury misconduct, and prosecutorial misconduct. The appellate court affirmed. While there was some conflicting evidence as to whether appellant invited the officers inside, such consent was not necessary in light of undisputed evidence that the officers did not conduct a physical search of the premises. The officers went inside merely to prevent evidence from being destroyed, for a short period of time, and with a good faith belief that a warrant was being obtained. No search was instigated prior to the issuance of the search warrant. The trial court did not commit reversible error in overruling appellant's motion to suppress. The evidence showed that appellant exercised care, custody, control, and management over the contraband, and that he knew the amphetamine was contraband. The court concluded that appellant was not denied a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting appellant for possession of amphetamine over 400 grams and sentencing him to 25 years confinement was affirmed. The trial court did not commit reversible error in overruling appellant's motion to suppress. The officers went inside appellant's residence to prevent evidence from being destroyed and with a good faith belief that a warrant was being obtained. No search was instigated prior to the issuance of the search warrant.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for selling an obscene magazine, summarily ruling that the state's obscenity statutes were not unconstitutional, that the magazine was clearly obscene within the statutory definition, and that the material was both factually and constitutionally obscene.

Floyd v. Willacy County Hospital Dist.


No. 13-85-375-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


706 S.W.2d 731; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12291



February 27, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 20, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 197th District Court of Willacy County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Legal survivors of the deceased appealed from the 197th District Court of Willacy County (Texas) which granted summary judgment to appellee county hospital, and others, in a wrongful death action. Appellants had filed suit against appellee hospital, appellee physician, appellee nurse, and appellee health care entity.


OVERVIEW: Legal survivors appealed from the trial court, which granted summary judgment to appellee hospital, appellee physician, appellee nurse, and appellee health care entity, in appellants' wrongful death action. Appellants claimed that their constitutional rights under the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 3a, were violated by the hospital because the hospital categorized patients into two different classes: those who were regular patients of the hospital's staff doctors; and, those who were not regular patients of the hospital's staff doctors. The deceased's vital signs were never taken. The court failed to see how it could be determined that the deceased was not suffering from a "true emergency or life threatening situation," or "a condition which was obviously a matter of life or death," without at least checking his vital signs. The court found that appellants might be able to establish that the very determination of what was a "true emergency" was made in such an arbitrary and capricious manner as to be unconstitutional. The hospital's plea of sovereign immunity was not enough to show that it was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for appellee hospital, appellee physician, appellee nurse, and appellee health care entity, was affirmed in part and reversed in part. Appellee hospital had not advanced any summary judgment proof identifying a rational basis for the classification allegedly created by its policy. Summary judgment granted to appellee hospital as to the allegation of a violation of equal protection was reversed and remanded for trial.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas) convicting him of execution of a document by deception.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of securing execution of a document by deception and sentenced to five years in prison. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash the indictment because the term "deception" did not give him adequate notice of the offense with which he was charged. OUTCOME: The order convicting appellant of execution of a document by deception was reversed and remanded because the term "deception" in the indictment did not give appellant adequate notice of the offense with which he was charged.

1257 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Daniel v. State


No. 2-84-304-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


704 S.W.2d 952; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12250



February 26, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 4 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Criminal District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted appellant of engaging in organized criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for engaging in organized criminal conduct, arguing that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 18.20 (1986), permitting the use of wiretaps, violated his rights under Tex. Const. art. I, § 9. The court held that the statute was constitutional and that since the offense for which appellant was convicted was within the ambit of 18. U.S.C.S. § 2516, appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute as applied to other offenses. Appellant claimed error in the refusal to charge the jury that they must all agree on the same overt act. The court held that the jury could be charged disjunctively and a general verdict of guilty was proper. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.01(b) on conspiracy did not require that two persons work together to commit the same act, only that two persons each perform one overt act. The admission of tapes of wiretapped conversations was proper where all copies were not sealed because only the tapes admitted into court and played were required to be sealed. State was not required to prove "unlawful manufacture" count alleged in the indictment where that count was not charged. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for engaging in organized criminal activity. Statute permitting wiretaps was constitutional as applied to appellant, admission of tapes of wiretapped conversations was proper even though unsealed copies were also made, and state did not have to prove count that was alleged in the indictment but not charged.

Texas Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation v. Texas State Employees Union


No. 14,460


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


708 S.W.2d 498; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12887



February 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied April 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 356,361-A, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Texas Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation (agency), challenged an order of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), that declared appellant's regulations regarding its employees submission to polygraph tests invalid and enjoined their enforcement in a suit by appellees, the Texas State Employees Union and agency employees.


OVERVIEW: The regulations of appellant, the Texas Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation (agency), provided that its employees could be required to take a polygraph in agency investigations of alleged employee misconduct. In a suit by appellees, Texas State Employees Union and agency employees, the trial court declared the regulations invalid and enjoined their enforcement. The court reversed. The court found that the state had an important and substantial interest in the safety and order of the mental-health system and that appellant's employees had common law rights of privacy and freedom from unreasonable employment conditions. The court held that an employee could not be required to submit to a polygraph unless the agency first determined that it was reasonable in view of the intrusion, the public interest at stake, and the existence of reasonable alternatives. The determination had to be made by a neutral agency official unrelated to the investigation and after notice to the employee and an opportunity for the employee to protest. The court imputed the reasonableness requirement to the regulations and held them valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order declaring that the regulations enacted by appellant, the Texas Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation (agency), were invalid. The court imputed to the regulations an antecedent reasonableness determination. The court remanded for a determination of the contention of appellees, Texas State Employees Union and agency employees, that the regulations were invalid on other grounds.

One 1979 Jeep v. State


No. 2-85-087-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


702 S.W.2d 781; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12071



February 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners challenged judgment of the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which ordered forfeiture of appellants' vehicle under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. R. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.03(a) (Supp. 1986), alleging the statute was unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. III, § 38, that the state failed to prove actual delivery or unlawful use of the vehicle, and that the amount seized was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owners challenged the forfeiture of their vehicle, which was ordered pursuant to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. R. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.03(a) (Supp. 1986). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held the statute was not unconstitutional and not violative of Tex. Const. art. III, § 38 because the caption to the article gave reasonable notice of the changes contained in the amended statute. The court found there was sufficient evidence for forfeiture of the vehicle because Tex. R. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.03(a) (Supp. 1986) did not require the state to prove actual delivery. Hence, because a controlled substance existed within the confines of the moving vehicle with appellants' knowledge, the vehicle was subject to forfeiture. Also, § 5.03(a) unambiguously provided for forfeiture when a vehicle was used or intended to be used to transport a controlled substance regardless of the quantity of the controlled substance and appellants' admission to the police that there was marijuana remaining in her vehicle after several sale were made evidenced the vehicle was used to transport and facilitate the sale of marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the forfeiture of appellant owners' vehicle and held that the statute was not unconstitutional, that the evidence was sufficient to support forfeiture by appellee state because it was not required to prove actual delivery of a controlled substance, that appellants' admissions proved the vehicle was used to transport a controlled substance, and that the statute provided for forfeiture regardless of the quantity involved.

 

1260 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Washington v. Walker County


No. 01-85-0543-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


708 S.W.2d 493; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12098



February 6, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 20, 1986, Reported at: 708 S.W.2d 493 at 497.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 12th District Court of Walker County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 14,590, Erwin G. Ernest, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney, who was also a state legislator, challenged the judgment of the 12th District Court of Walker County, Texas, which denied appellant's petition for a writ of mandamus to order appellees, the county and state, to perform the ministerial act of paying appellant for attorney's fee for appellant's representation of an indigent defendant, alleging such payment was not unconstitutional or prohibited under Tex. Const. art. III, § 18.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney, who was also a legislator, was appointed to represent an indigent defendant. After the trial, the trial court certified the amount of attorney's fee to be paid by appellees, the county and state, to appellant. Appellee state forwarded a check to appellee county, which refused to issue the check to appellant. The trial court denied appellant's petition for a writ of mandamus to order appellees to perform the ministerial act of payment. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court and held payment was not constitutionally prohibited because appellant's appointment as counsel was not an interest in a contract prohibited under Tex. Const. art. III, § 18, hence, payment was a ministerial act, and appellant was entitled to the fees. An attorney's representation of an indigent defendant was not a contract between the attorney and the state or county merely because of the incidental benefit of attorney's fee. Further, payment of the state funds forwarded to and held by appellee county was not payment of a debt or obligation prohibited under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.055 because it was to satisfy appellee state's obligation under the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of appellant attorney's petition for a writ of mandamus and held payment of attorney's fee by appellees, the state and county, to appellant for representing an indigent defendant was not unconstitutional because appellant's appointment as counsel was not an interest in a contract prohibited under the state constitution. Hence, payment of the fee was a ministerial act and appellant was entitled to the attorney's fee.

Schumaker v. State


Nos. 13-85-110-CR, 13-85-111-CR, 13-85-112-CR, 13-85-113-CR

January 30, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the County Court at Law of Bee County, Texas.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions from the County Court at Law of Bee County (Texas), for harassment, criminal mischief, assault, and driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of harassment, criminal mischief, assault, and driving while intoxicated, and challenged the lower court's judgment. The court reversed the lower court and remanded the case. The court held that appellant's aunt, whose testimony was at issue, was a character witness, not a reputation witness and it was error to permit a witness who had testified on personal knowledge or as to character to be cross-examined with questions allowed only to a reputation witness, the "have you heard" questions. The court held that the lower court's charge for harassment mixed two subsections and was reversible error and it was also error for the trial court to refuse to admit appellant's testimony about his intent in making the phone calls as intent was an essential element of that offense. OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's judgment, and held that it was error to permit a witness who had testified on personal knowledge or as to character to be cross-examined with questions allowed only to a reputation witness, the "have you heard" questions and for the trial court to refuse to admit appellant's testimony about his intent in making the phone calls as intent was an essential element of harassment.

Polk v. State


No. 05-85-00491-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


704 S.W.2d 929; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12407



January 30, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reversal of the decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with a violation of the Safety Responsibility Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701H (1977 & Supp. 1986). The complaint was defective because it did not state a date for the offense. However, appellant was arrested because of it and was told he was a suspect in a murder case. Appellant was taken directly to the police station, not to a magistrate, and he confessed. The confession was introduced at the murder trial. The conviction was reversed and remanded to the trial court because the appellate court found that the warrant under which appellant was arrested was invalid because it was based on a defective complaint. It followed that the arrest based on the invalid warrant was illegal. The voluntary confession was obtained pursuant to the illegal arrest and should not have been introduced because appellee state did not meet the burden of determining that the taint of the illegal arrest was purged. There was no event or circumstance that occurred or manifested itself so significantly as to intervene to attenuate the taint of the illegal arrest. The appellate court found no good faith exception applicable under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court, which convicted appellant of murder. The court found that the complaint that charged appellant with a violation of the Safety Responsibility Act was defective, that the warrant was invalid because it was based on a defective complaint, and that the arrest based on the invalid warrant was illegal. The confession was inadmissible because it was obtained pursuant to the illegal arrest.

Johnson v. State


No. 05-85-00318-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


706 S.W.2d 120; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12477



January 23, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: From County Criminal Court Number Eight of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgement of the County Criminal Court Number Eight, Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of desecration of a venerated object.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of desecration of a venerated object, the United States flag, during a protest. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. In doing so, the court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.09 did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I because the relevant terms of the offense, "deface," "damage, " and "physically mistreat" were not vague, but were well understood terms, and that § 42.09 was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not prohibit legitimate protest activities. The court found that § 42.09 did not violate defendant's rights to free speech under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV. The court found that appellant's act of burning the flag constituted symbolic speech requiring scrutiny under U.S. Const. amend. I because appellant intended to convey a particularized message that was very likely to be understood by those who viewed it. However, infringement of defendant's constitutional rights to free speech was justified because the act of burning the flag was so inherently inflammatory that the state could have acted to prevent breaches of the public peace, and to protect the flag as a symbol of national unity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of desecration of a venerated object because the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, and the state advanced substantial interests that justified infringement of appellant's rights to free speech.

Martin v. State


No. C14-85-009-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


704 S.W.2d 892; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11903



January 16, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 122nd District Court of Galveston County, Trial Cause No. 84CR0207.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated robbery in the 122nd District Court of Galveston County (Texas), on the basis that Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 7.01(c), 7.02(a)(2) (Vernon 1974), unconstitutionally provided for criminal responsibility for another's acts, that he did not know co-defendant intended to commit robbery, and that his requested jury instruction should have been given.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant sought reversal of his conviction for aggravated robbery, alleging that although he was with co-defendant, he did not know co-defendant intended to rob the store and he did not participate in the robbery. Appellant asserted that there was no identification of co-defendant, and no evidence of ownership of the money taken in the robbery or that the victims were in fear of imminent bodily injury or death. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that identity was established when the co-defendant testified about the robbery, and that the store manager's testimony established both ownership of the money and the victims' fear of imminent bodily injury or death. The court also held that the statutes providing for criminal responsibility for aiding or soliciting another person's crime, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 7.01(c), 7.02(a)(2) (Vernon 1974), were not unconstitutional. Further, the denial of appellant's requested jury instruction was not error, as it was not a complete instruction on the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery, holding that the statutes providing for criminal responsibility for another's acts were not unconstitutional, that sufficient evidence supported the conviction, and that the denial of appellant's requested jury instruction was not error as the instruction was not comprehensive.

 

1265 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


JUNCO PONCE v. STATE


No. 01-85-0140-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11906



January 16, 1986


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District court of Harris County Trial Court Cause No. 417585


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which imposed conditions of probation that he must make restitution to the county and serve 30 days in the county jail after a jury had found defendant guilty of murder, had assessed his punishment at 10 years confinement, and had recommended probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in imposing conditions of probation that required restitution to the county and for defendant to serve 30 days in the county jail after a jury had recommended probation following defendant being found guilty of murder and an assessment of punishment at 10 years confinement. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, and held that although the trial court was required to grant jury recommended probation, it was authorized to set the conditions of probation pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 6. The court ruled that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 was not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite with regard to the conditions of probation imposed upon defendant, and that nothing in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 § 6(a)(8) required the county to be a victim of a crime in order for reparations to be authorized. The court also held that a fundamental error did not exist from the trial court not instructing the jury on the trial court's power to order 30 days detention in a penal institution, because it was unlikely that the jury would have reduced the amount of confinement time assessed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that required defendant to serve 30 days in the county jail and pay restitution to the county, because the trial court was authorized to set conditions of probation, the county did not need to be victim of crime to receive restitution, and the controlling statute was not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite.

DAVIS v. STATE


No. 01-84-0744-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11907



January 16, 1986


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 412323.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 177th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault upon a child younger than 14 years old. Defendant contended that the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional because it did not require proof that defendant knew the victim's age, and that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated sexual assault upon a girl who was younger than 14 years of age on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional because it did not require proof that defendant knew the victim's age and that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence. The court affirmed the conviction because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22-011 (1985) imposed strict liability when the victim was younger than 14 years old and, therefore, the state did not need to allege or prove that defendant knew the victim's age. The court treated the contention that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence as a claim that the evidence was insufficient and found there was sufficient evidence that a sexual act occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because defendant's knowledge of the victim's age was not an element of the offense of aggravated sexual assault that the state was required to prove and, viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, the evidence was sufficient to find the defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1267 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Prejean v. State


No. 01-85-00197-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


704 S.W.2d 119; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11938



January 16, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 337th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 405,239.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a conviction for arson under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02(a)(4) (1986) in the 337th District Court of Harris County, Texas. Defendant contended that there was insufficient evidence to convict him because he did not intend to commit arson, he had intended to commit suicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of arson under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02(a)(4) (1986). Defendant challenged the conviction, arguing that there was insufficient evidence that he had the intent to commit arson because he initially intended to commit suicide when he lit the fires, that the lesser-included offense of criminal mischief should have been included in the charge to the jury, and that he was denied his right to a speedy trial. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that although "intent" or "purpose" was not synonymous with "motive," the intent to commit suicide was closely akin under the facts to a motive for a purposeful act of arson and that defendant purposefully lit the fires. Criminal mischief was also properly not included in the jury instruction because it required proof of the value of the property damaged or destroyed. The court further held that defendant was not denied his right to a speedy trial because he did not prove that he was prejudiced in any way and that all re-settings of the trial were mutual.


OUTCOME: Defendant's arson conviction was affirmed by the court, holding that defendant had purposefully laid and set the fires, and it was his conscious desire to set the apartment on fire, even if the ultimate result he originally intended to accomplish was suicide. The court also held that it was proper for the state not to instruct the jury on the lesser offense of criminal mischief and that defendant had received a speedy trial.

 

1268 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Oliver v. State


Nos. 2-81-248-CR, 2-81-249-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


701 S.W.2d 696; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11901



January 15, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 2 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 2 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted her of two charges of unlawfully practicing dentistry, where appellant contended that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4551a(5) (Supp. 1986) was unconstitutionally vague because the terms "fit" and "adjust" were not defined in the statute and were vague and ambiguous.


OVERVIEW: Following her convictions for unlawfully practicing dentistry, appellant sought review. After the court of appeals reversed and remanded the two causes against appellant, the state sought discretionary review to the court of criminal appeals. Thereafter, the high court reversed and remanded the two causes back to the court of appeals. On remand, the court affirmed the convictions. The court addressed the issue of whether Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4551a (5) (Supp. 1986), was unconstitutional because the terms "fit" and "adjust" were not defined in the statute and were vague and ambiguous. The court noted that for a law to be valid and enforceable it must be sufficiently definite that the law's terms and provisions could be known, understood, and applied; however, a statute would not be rendered unconstitutionally vague merely because the words or terms were not specially defined. The court found that although experts might disagree whether a certain procedure constituted "fitting" or "adjusting," both terms were common everyday words understood by ordinary men and, therefore, when read as a whole, art. 4551a(5) was sufficiently clear as to give adequate notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for unlawfully practicing dentistry. The court ruled that the applicable statute was not unconstitutionally vague, because a statute was not rendered unconstitutional simply because its terms were not specially defined. The court found that the terms in question were common terms, which were understood by ordinary men and, thus, the statute was sufficiently clear so as to give notice.

 

1269 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Solis v. State


No. 13-85-224-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


704 S.W.2d 883; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 11890



January 9, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 92nd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 92nd District Court, Hidalgo County, Texas, which convicted him of attempted capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted capital murder. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that the language of the indictment was sufficient to charge attempted capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.01 (1985). The court found that no evidence came in as a result of an invalid arrest warrant, and the invalid warrant did not preclude evidence of appellant's attempted murder of officer executing it. The court held that once appellant used force against the officer, the arrest warrant became immaterial because appellant was resisting arrest. The court held that the criminal attempt statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 15.01(a) (1986) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant because the act of shooting a police officer was unquestionably more than mere preparation. The court refused to second-guess the decision made by the grand jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of attempted capital murder. The language of the indictment was sufficient to charge attempted capital murder. An invalid warrant did not preclude evidence of appellant's attempted murder of the officer executing it. Once appellant used force against the officer, the arrest warrant was immaterial because appellant was resisting arrest. Criminal attempt statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

1270 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Irion v. State


No. 3-84-233-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


703 S.W.2d 362; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12005



January 8, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF TRAVIS COUNTY NO. 238-171, HONORABLE STEVE RUSSELL, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Court at Law, Travis County, Texas, which convicted her of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the statutory definition of "intoxicated" was not unconstitutionally vague because the Court of Criminal Appeals had previously held the definition constitutional. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction because the opinion testimony of the arresting officer alone was sufficient to prove the element of intoxication. The court held that the absence of a videotape required by 1983 Tex. Gen. Laws 303, § 24 did not require acquittal for insufficiency of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of driving while intoxicated because the statutory definition of "intoxicated" was not unconstitutionally vague. The evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction because the opinion testimony of the arresting officer alone was sufficient to prove the element of intoxication. The absence of a statutorily required videotape did not require acquittal for insufficiency of the evidence.

 

1271 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Chitwood v. State


Nos. 05-85-00208-CR, 05-85-00209-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


703 S.W.2d 360; 1986 Tex. App. LEXIS 12406



January 2, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of a District Court, Dallas County (Texas), that found that he waived his right to complain of the prosecution's use of a video tape of a child under Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 38.071, §2 at a trial held before the statute was deemed unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court on appeal was whether by failing to object, defendant waived his right to complain that the prosecution's use of a videotape of a child under Tex. Crim. P. Code art. 38.071, § 2 was improper because the statute allowing such use was later declared unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that aside from the apparent tactical aspects of defendant's failure to object, defendant had sufficient notice of the existence of a viable attack upon the constitutionality of art. 38.071, § 2 at the time of his initial appeal. The court also noted that the constitutional claim was not so novel that its legal basis was not reasonably available to counsel. The court held that defendant had waived his objection to the new and obviously questionable statute by failing to object to it at trial. The court stated that the right to confrontation was too fundamental for defendant to affirmatively permit the introduction of a video tape and then later claim that this right had been violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment that found defendant waived his right to complain of the prosecution's use of a videotape of a child was affirmed because defendant failed to object to the admission of the videotape at trial even though the statute under which it was admitted was new and constitutionally questionable.

 

1272 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas Attorney Gen. on behalf of Ford v. Daurbigny


No. 01-85-0617-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


702 S.W.2d 298; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12573



December 19, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 308th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 84-58425.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, mother of a minor child, sought review of a decision by the 308th District Court of Harris County (Texas) which granted summary judgment to respondent, alleged father of the child, in a paternity action.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, petitioner, mother of a minor child, contended that the trial judge erred in granting summary judgment because a prior dismissal without prejudice for want of prosecution was not a bar to reprosecution; laches was inapplicable as a matter of law or, alternatively, had not been established; and the court applied the wrong period of limitations, and limitations had not run. The court agreed with petitioner's arguments. The court held that respondent, alleged father of the child, failed to meet his burden to establish each necessary element of the affirmative defense of laches as a matter of law. Therefore, the court held that respondent failed to establish his right to summary judgment by establishing all of the elements of any one or more of his defenses as a matter of law. The court also held that, as a matter of law, limitations did not bar the prosecution of the lawsuit. Accordingly, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had granted summary judgment to respondent, alleged father of a minor child, in a paternity action. The court held that respondent failed to establish his right to summary judgment by establishing all of the elements of any one or more of his defenses as a matter of law. The court also held that limitations did not bar prosecution of the lawsuit.

 

1273 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Valero Transmission Co. v. Hays Consol. Independent School Dist.


No. 14,474


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


704 S.W.2d 857; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12908



December 18, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied March 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. 2,654, HONORABLE CHARLES R. RAMSAY, JUDGE


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the 22nd District Court of Hays County, Texas, in favor of appellee school district, which required appellant to pay ad valorem taxes, penalties and interest. Appellant argued that administrative review by the appraisal review board was not its exclusive remedy to protest ad valorem tax assessments and that appellee could not institute a collection suit while appellant's protest was still pending.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer disputed the ad valorem tax assessment made by appellee school district, and filed a protest with the Appraisal Review Board (Board). Appellant did not pay the disputed taxes, so appellee filed suit. Appellant counterclaimed, and alleged that the assessment was unfair. The trial court found for appellee and denied appellant's counterclaim because appellant had not exhausted its administrative remedies since the tax protest was unresolved. Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment, and argued that the administrative remedy was not exclusive and that appellee could not collect the disputed taxes until the protest had been resolved. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that pursuant to Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.01, it was mandatory for the administrative review process to be exhausted before appellant could obtain judicial review. The court held that pursuant to Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.09, appellant could not raise the issues involved in its tax protest as a counterclaim to the collection suit. The court held that appellee was not required to wait until the protest was completed to file suit to collect the past due taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, and held that appellant taxpayer could not obtain judicial review directly or through a counterclaim until the administrative review by the Appraisal Review Board (Board) was complete. The court also held that appellee school district was not required to wait for the Board's decision on appellant's protest before it could file suit to collect past due taxes.

 

1274 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Texas Alcoholic Beverage Com. v. Wishnow


No. A14-85-163CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS


704 S.W.2d 425; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12744



December 12, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 157th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 85-00115.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission sought review of the judgment of the 157th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, which reversed the cancellation of appellee club owner's alcoholic beverage permits because Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(6) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission cancelled appellee club owner's alcoholic beverage permits for violations of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 11.61(b)(7),(13),(14) (1978) and Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(6) (1985), but was reversed when appellee challenged the administrative order in the trial court. The trial court reversed the cancellations because appellee's criminal conviction for violation of § 104.01(6) had been overturned where the criminal appeals court held § 104.01(6) unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's findings and held that § 104.01(6) was penal in nature and, therefore, the civil courts could interfere to prevent irreparable injury to appellee's vested property rights. The court found that appellant's underlying order was not reasonably supported by substantial evidence, even though some violations did exist, because the penalty was too severe for the totality of the alleged violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's reversal of appellant Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission's cancellation of liquor permits for appellee club owner because the civil court was permitted to utilize the criminal appellate court's finding that the statute involved was unconstitutionally vague.

 

1275 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Reinsmith v. State


No. C14-85-255-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


703 S.W.2d 315; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 8990



December 12, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Law No. 5 of Harris County, Trial Court No. 768,407.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court of Law No. 5 of Harris County, Texas, which applied the definition in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(a)(2)(B) defining "intoxication" as having 0.10 percent or more alcohol concentration and found defendant guilty of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with driving while intoxicated. The jury found that defendant had a blood alcohol level equal to or greater than 0.10 and convicted defendant under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(a)(2) (Supp. 1985). Defendant challenged the conviction and claimed that art. 67011-1(a)(2) created an irrebuttable presumption of intoxication and that the statute was unconstitutional because notice of the new definition was not given in its caption, predetermined his guilt, shifted the burden of proof and deprived him of a fair trial and due process of law. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and found that art. 67011-1(a)(2) was not unconstitutional and did not create a presumption at all, much less an irrebuttable one, but was a separate, independent, additional way in which the crime of driving while intoxicated could be committed and that defendant's blood alcohol level was an ultimate fact that still had to be proved at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because the definition of intoxication as having a blood alcohol level of 0.10 or more did not create a presumption of guilt but was, instead, an independent way to prove the crime and a fact that was required to be determined in trial, and the statute setting for the definition was not unconstitutional.

 

1276 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bedford v. State


No. C14-84-734-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


703 S.W.2d 775; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 8991



December 12, 1985, Decided  
 December 12, 1985, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 305,871


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of attempted murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted murder and his punishment was assessed at life imprisonment. He sought review of the conviction. On review the court affirmed. The court held that the state's argument that the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A (1985), violated several provisions of the Texas Constitution was improper. The court held that the statute was in compliance with the Texas Constitution because it gave fair notice of its subject matter and it did not constitute an impermissible encroachment on the functions of the judiciary. The court further held that appellant had not been denied a speedy trial, because the state exercised due diligence in proceeding to trial once it knew of his whereabouts. Further, the state was ready for trial within the 120-day time limitation that was set forth under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A (1985). The court also held that the trial court did not err when it admitted evidence of appellant's prior acts of misconduct, because such evidence was admissible to show appellant's state of mind at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed, because the appellant had not been deprived of his right to a speedy trial, and the lower court did not err when it admitted evidence of his prior acts of misconduct.

 

1277 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Weaver v. State


No. 2-85-004-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


700 S.W.2d 776; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12771



December 11, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Criminal Court No. 1 of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 1 of Tarrant County, Texas, which found that a videotape recording of defendant was not required in order to prosecute defendant for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1, § 24 and that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-5, § 3(g) (Supp. 1984), was an unconstitutional failure to give adequate notice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated. The jury found him guilty and the court assessed punishment. Defendant challenged his conviction and claimed that the trial court erred in not dismissing the indictment because the police failed to videotape defendant after he was arrested as required by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-1, § 24 and that defendant's failure to submit a specimen for testing was a violation of his due process rights because the caption of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701L-5, § 3(g) (Supp. 1984), did not comply with the notice requirements of Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. The court affirmed the conviction and found that the consequence of violating § 24, was not dismissal of the indictment, but that defendant could bring the lack of a videotape to the jury's attention, which defendant failed to do. The court further found that the caption of § 3(g) was sufficient, and not unconstitutional, to apprise any interested person of the effect of an accused's refusal to have a chemical test performed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because the state was not required to have a videotape of defendant after he was arrested in order to prosecute the crime, but the failure to have such a tape meant that defendant could raise the issue of lack of a tape recording at trial, which defendant failed to do. The court held that defendant had notice of the consequences of refusing to give a specimen sample.
