Dallas v. Union Tower Corp.


No. 05-83-01145-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


703 S.W.2d 275; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12862



December 5, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and school district sought the review of the order of the trial court (Texas), which entered a judgment for appellee building owner in appellee's suit to recover excessive property taxes. The lower court denied appellant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Appellee building owner filed suit against appellant city and school district to recover property taxes paid by appellee, which appellee claimed were excessive. The lower court entered a judgment for appellee, and denied appellant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The court, on appeal, affirmed the order of the lower court holding that appellant had assessed appellee's property at below 100 % of its value, which violated Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7174 (1925). The court also held that the record showed that appellee's property was also assessed at a higher rate than that of other property within appellant's taxing jurisdiction and that these unequal assessments were done without references to whether they were done pursuant to an adopted plan as was required under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court, which awarded a judgment to appellee building owner in appellee's suit to recover excessive property taxes, which were paid to appellant city and school district; appellee's property was assessed at an unreasonably higher tax rate than other tax payers' property.

 

1279 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Horn v. State


No. 2-85-018-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


699 S.W.2d 714; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12454



November 27, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 297th Judicial District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 297th Judicial District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated robbery after appellant, who had been Mirandized, made a written confession to the crime. Enhanced by two prior felony convictions, appellant's punishment was assessed by the jury at 99 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was arrested for aggravated robbery and Mirandized, appellant confessed. Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery, and appellant's punishment, enhanced by prior felonies, was set at 99 years confinement. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found that appellant had been unable to complain of the confession's voluntariness because appellant had introduced the confession. Similarly, the court found that the confession had been admissible regardless of discrepancies in complying with the confession statute under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 2 (1979) because the discrepancies had not affected the correctness of Miranda warnings provided in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 15.17 (Supp. 1985). The court also found that the statement was admissible because the trial court's dictation of findings into the record was sufficient to satisfy Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 6 (1979). Finally, the court found that an enhancement count, containing the date, court, and cause number of the felony, had presented proper notice and that the trial court had not been required to submit appellant's instruction during punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment convicting appellant of aggravated robbery because the voluntariness of a confession introduced by appellant could not be questioned, nor was it inadmissible based on statutory discrepancies not affecting the Miranda warnings' correctness. Also, dictation of findings into the record was sufficient, enhancement recitals had provided proper notice, and requested instruction was not required during punishment.

 

1280 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Budd v. State


No. 09-85-159-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


701 S.W.2d 65; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12674



November 27, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 258TH DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JACINTO COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the 258th District Court of San Jacinto County (Texas) convicting him of the manufacture of less than 28 grams of a controlled substance. Defendant received an eight-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the manufacture of more than 400 grams of a controlled substance. Defendant pleaded guilty to the manufacture of less than 28 grams of the controlled substance and was sentenced to eight years. Defendant sought review, alleging that he was not admonished by the trial court as to the correct sentence range. The court affirmed, holding that the indictment properly alleged an offense under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03 (1976). The court held that defendant knew he would receive an eight year sentence, which was at the lower end of the sentencing range. Defendant had received numerous admonitions from the trial court. The court ruled that defendant's plea was knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that he knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently pleaded guilty without duress or coercion because he pleaded guilty to an offense where an eight year sentence was possible; thus, he knew he would receive an eight-year sentence.

 

1281 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bond v. State


No. 09-85-064 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


700 S.W.2d 36; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12689



November 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 163rd District Court of Orange County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 163rd District Court of Orange County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 50 years. Appellant contended that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.46 was unconstitutional in its application to his case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of aggravated robbery and received a 50-year sentence. Appellant contended that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.46, regarding the use of a conviction for enhancement purposes, was unconstitutional as applied to his case. June 7, 1979, was the effective date of § 12.46. Appellant argued that because the enhancement allegation had its basis in a June 13, 1978, conviction, § 12.46, as applied to him, was an ex post facto law, and that § 12.46 inflicted a greater punishment than the law provided when the June 13, 1978, felony was committed. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and the sentence, holding that on November 8, 1983, the date of the principal offense, § 12.46 was fully effective and that appellant received a fair and impartial trial. The court stated that the reason that a conviction which occurred before the statute was enacted may be used for enhancement was that the statute providing for a greater penalty upon a subsequent conviction did not seek to punish the offender for the original crime a second time, but rather, the repetition of criminal conduct aggravated guilt and justified heavier penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence by the trial court. The court held that on November 8, 1983, the date of the principal offense, § 12.46 was fully effective and that appellant received a fair and impartial trial.

 

1282 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Rhea v. State


No. 6-84-112-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


705 S.W.2d 165; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12400



November 19, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 102nd Judicial District Court of Red River County, Texas.



DISPOSITION:  We reverse the trial court's judgment and remand the cause to that court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 102nd Judicial District Court of Red River County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child, claiming that the admission of the child's videotaped statement violated Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the aggravated sexual assault of his two-year old child based on the child's videotaped statement. Reversing the conviction, the court held that the child was not a competent witness because the child's testimony indicated that she did not possess sufficient intellect to relate transactions about which she was questioned when placed under oath as a witness and was unable to understand the obligation of an oath. Due to her incompetence, the court held that the admission of the child's videotaped statement violated the requirement in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2(a)(8) that the child be available to testify. The court found that, excluding the videotape, scarcely any evidence remained to support the verdict and without that evidence a rational trier of fact could not have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child because the child was not competent to testify as a witness and, therefore, the trial court erred in admitting the videotaped testimony of the child without which there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction.

 

1283 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. Seagoville


No. 05-83-00813-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


700 S.W.2d 953; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12867



November 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought a motion for rehearing to review a summary judgment granted by a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), in favor of appellees, a city, the mayor and municipal judge of the city, and two clerks of the municipal court. Appellant had brought suit against appellees for violation of his civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. 1983, pertaining to an arrest and incarceration on traffic offenses of which he was later acquitted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimant alleged that he was falsely imprisoned by appellee city and municipal court judge, when appellee clerks of the municipal court signed and filed complaints against him for failure to appear in court for traffic violations. Appellant contended in his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action that his arrest and incarceration resulted from his criticism of appellee city's administration and violated his constitutional right to free speech. The district court granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and appellant challenged the order. On review, the court reversed the summary judgment in favor of appellee city because the doctrine of sovereign immunity was not an absolute bar to a § 1983 action. Furthermore, the court found that the notice requirement of the Texas Tort Claims Act was not applicable, as appellant was not entitled to file suit under the act for false imprisonment. The court found that appellant's pleading was deficient, but appellee city did not assert it in its motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed summary judgment for appellees judge and clerks of the municipal court, as they had judicial immunity while acting within the course of their duties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment in favor of appellee city, because sovereign immunity was not an absolute bar to a civil rights action for constitutional deprivations inflicted on appellant claimant pursuant to a governmental decision, and the notice requirement of the Torts Claims Act did not apply to appellant's action. The court upheld summary judgments for appellees judge and clerks of the court, because they were judicially immune.

 

1284 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Cochran v. State


No. B14-84-856-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12364



November 14, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Cause No. 405,410


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment by the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated kidnapping pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 20.04 (1974) after he offered a woman a ride home but deceived her by taking her to another place and placed a knife to her back before police intervened.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted in the trial court of aggravated kidnapping pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 20.04 (1974). Appellant challenged his conviction, but the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found appellant guilty of aggravated kidnapping because the fact that the victim initially got into appellant's car voluntarily did not matter because appellant intended to deceive her and in fact took her to a place other than her home. The court held that the fact that appellant had held a knife to victim's back for only a few seconds before police intervened sufficiently "terrorized" the victim to aggravate the kidnapping and even momentary restraint constituted kidnapping. Finally, the court found that appellant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel because he had the burden to prove the deficiency and failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting appellant of aggravated kidnapping because the victim voluntarily entered his car for a ride home, but appellant took her to another location by deception and aggravated the kidnapping by holding a knife to her back momentarily before police intervened.

 

1285 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


De Mangin v. State


No. 01-85-0106-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


700 S.W.2d 329; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12385



November 14, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 794469.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7 of Harris County, Texas, which convicted appellant pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (1977) of driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended that a senate bill amending that statute violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (1977) and challenged his conviction, contending that a senate bill amending that statute violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that the conviction of did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 as a result of a senate bill's caption, which failed to refer to that statute specifically. The court stated that amended statutes only needed to be referred to generally, not specifically, where they were amended and the senate bill caption did not violate the Texas Constitution. The court held that appellant was not denied his right to assistance of counsel where he was pressured to take a blood alcohol test before given time to locate a lawyer because this stage of the process was not constitutionally protected and the state was merely gathering evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting appellant of driving while intoxicated because there was no constitutional requirement that he have an opportunity to consult an attorney before a blood-alcohol test was administered, as that was not a critical stage in the process and the state was merely gathering evidence.

 

1286 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ball


No. 05-85-00857-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


703 S.W.2d 727; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12861



November 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Collin County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the take-nothing-judgment by a district court in Collin County (Texas), in an enforcement action on behalf of the License & Weight Service of the Department of Public Safety against appellee. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in its interpretation of the applicable statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state had sought civil penalties and a permanent injunction for asserted violations of the Texas Motor Carrier Act. The ultimate issue rested on whether appellee was subject to the provisions and penalties of the Motor Carrier Act. Appellant questioned which exemption, under §16(j) or § 1a(1)(a) of the Motor Carrier Act, applied. The court held that the legislature intended the second paragraph of § 16(j) to function as an exemption to the whole Act and not to be merely applicable to the provision incorrectly placed in the Penal Code. Appellant also argued that the trial court gave an improper instruction. The court held that the issue submitted by the trial court phrased in terms of §16(j) was correct and that appellant had not shown that it was harmed by the submission of issue number one since the court also gave the qualifying instruction phrased in terms of §1a(1)(a). The court affirmed and found that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury findings.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the trial court properly interpreted the statute and there was sufficient evidence to support the findings.

Moallen v. State


No. 01-83-0004-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


699 S.W.2d 926; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12292



November 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 184th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 366,305.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction in the 184th District Court of Harris County (Texas), entered upon her plea of no contest to credit card abuse.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that her conviction for credit card abuse, entered upon her no contest plea, was improper because the indictment was fundamentally defective. The reviewing court upheld the conviction. The indictment sufficiently tracked the statutory language, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.31(b)(2) (1974). The state was not required to allege what appellant intended to obtain through the use of the credit card because, generally, only the perpetrator would know that fact. The state was not required to name the victim because it did not necessarily need to be a victim for there to be a violation of the law.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction, entered upon her plea of no contest to credit card abuse, was affirmed because the indictment properly tracked the statutory language.

 

1288 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Newman v. State


No. 01-85-0210-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


700 S.W.2d 307; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12337



November 7, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 183rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 414,903.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for aggravated sexual abuse entered by the 183rd District Court of Harris County (Texas). Appellant alleged ten points of error, including insufficient evidence, improper denial of his challenges for cause to veniremen, improper use of videotaped testimony pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 38.07 and 38.071, and improper jury argument.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual abuse, he challenged the trial court's decision. The court affirmed and overruled appellant's 10 points of error. First, the evidence was sufficient because an outcry witness and a physician corroborated complainant's videotaped testimony. Second, appellant failed to request additional challenges for cause after he exercised all of his peremptory challenges. Third, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 35.16(b)(3), the state could inquire whether a juror was biased against any phase of the law on which the state relied for conviction. Fourth, although argument of other crimes was not proper, it was cured by a charge to the jury. Fifth, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2(b), appellant's right to confrontation was not violated by introduction of videotaped testimony because he had an opportunity to cross-examine complainant and chose not to call her to the stand. Sixth, because a witness's ability to take an oath is a question of law, no jury charge on the issue was required. And finally, testimony of an outcry witness was properly admitted pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.07.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual abuse holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, appellant failed to preserve his denial of challenges to veniremen, complainant's videotaped testimony was both properly introduced and did not violate appellant's right to confrontation because he waived his right to cross-examination, and the state's improper closing argument was cured by a jury instruction.

 

1289 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ismail v. Ismail


No. 01-84-00737-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


702 S.W.2d 216; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12350



November 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 308th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 82-00787.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of a divorce judgment from the 308th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which divided certain property, including real property located in Egypt, pursuant to Texas' quasi-community property statute, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.63(b) (1985); awarded attorney's fees to appellee migrant spouse; and entered sanctions against appellant.


OVERVIEW: In a divorce action between two Egyptian citizens, the trial court granted the parties a divorce and divided certain property, including real property located in Egypt. On review, appellant husband contended, among other things, that the trial court erred: (1) in applying the Texas quasi-community property statute, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.63(b) (1985), (2) in awarding excessive attorney's fees to the appellee, and (3) in entering sanctions against the appellant. The court found that appellant's contacts with the state, when coupled with the state's interest in protecting appellee migrant spouse, warranted the application of state law to the division of the property located within the state. Therefore, there was no error in refusing to apply Egyptian law in this case. Further, there was no abuse of discretion in entering sanctions against appellant because, by his own admission, he failed to comply with the trial court's ordered discovery request. However, the court concluded that the evidence was insufficient to support an award of attorney's fees and, therefore, remanded that issue. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment, which awarded appellee migrant spouse attorney's fees, was reversed, severed, and remanded to the trial court for a hearing because the evidence was insufficient to support the award. However, the remainder of the judgment was affirmed because the trial court properly applied Texas' quasi-community property statute and did not abuse its discretion in its division of the property.

 

1290 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. State


No. 10-84-152-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


699 S.W.2d 695; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12470



November 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 54th Judicial District Court McLennan County, Texas; Trial Court # 84-125-C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the 54th District Court of McLennan County (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of the murder of a security guard, following denial of his motions for discharge under the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, removal for cause of a prospective juror, and mistrial for alleged improper cross-examination of defendant by the prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the murder of a security guard. After it said it was ready for trial, the state moved for a continuance due to the absence of a material witness. It sought another continuance when a prosecutor chose to attend a seminar. Another delay was caused by the trial judge's vacation. Defendant's motion for discharge under the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, was denied and, during jury selection, a defense challenge for cause was overruled. After defendant testified at trial that he had never been convicted of a felony, the prosecutor cross-examined him by emphasizing that he was never "convicted" of a felony. Defendant's objection was sustained and the jury was instructed to disregard, but his motion for mistrial was denied. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that the state met the time limitations of the Speedy Trial Act, but even if it had not, there was no violation because the Act violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35, by having an insufficient caption. Error regarding the juror challenge was not preserved and any impropriety by the prosecutor was cured by the instruction to disregard.


OUTCOME: The murder conviction was affirmed because the record showed that the state was ready for trial within the time limitations of the Speedy Trial Act; even if the time limit were not met, the Act was invalid, in that its caption was insufficient under the state constitution; defendant failed to preserve error as to his challenge to a prospective juror; and any error from questioning by the prosecutor was cured by a jury instruction to disregard.

 

1291 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Allen


No. 05-85-00180-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


699 S.W.2d 886; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12890



 November 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 699 S.W.2d 886 at 894.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas. Original Opinion of August 30, 1985, Reported at: 699 S.W.2d 886.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant sought leave for an order allowing him to file a motion for rehearing in a district court of Dallas County, Texas, where his application for a writ of habeas corpus seeking to avoid extradition was denied, contending that the amendments to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 44.38 constituted an ex post facto law in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order denying applicant's writ of habeas corpus to avoid extradition was affirmed by the court, and applicant tendered his motion for rehearing to the clerk of this court for filing. The clerk initially accepted the motion but returned the motion to applicant. Applicant asserted that the refusal to allow him a motion for rehearing was an ex post facto application of Tex. Crim. Proc. Code art. 44.38, which abolished the right to a motion for rehearing in extradition appeals when the order approving extradition has been affirmed, violated Tex. Const. art 1, § 16 because he was entitled to the benefit of the rules in effect at the time he commenced his appeal. The court disagreed, holding that because there was no express legislative intent to the contrary, the amendments to Tex. Crim. Proc. art. 44.38 applied from the effective date of the legislation. And since applicant right to a rehearing would have come into existence the date this court decided appellant's case, which was after the amendments' effective date, the amendments applied to applicant, were not retroactive, and did not violate the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws.


OUTCOME: The court denied the applicant's request for a writ of mandamus, holding that the subject amendments to the Texas Code of Criminal Procedure did not violate the Texas Constitution since the decision was not delivered until after the amendments' effective date, that the applicant took no action before that date that could be affected by the amendments so that the amendments applied to applicant and were not retroactive.

 

1292 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. State


No. 05-84-00005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


700 S.W.2d 289; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12858



November 1, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a County Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from a County Court of Dallas County (Texas), which revoked his probation by admitting evidence taken during a roadblock.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped at a roadblock, where the officer noticed the smell of alcohol, did field sobriety tests, and arrested him for driving while intoxicated. The trial court ruled that the roadblock was legal and the evidence was therefore admissible. After being found guilty on the charge, the state moved to revoke his probation on a prior charge, using the same evidence. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, appellant argued the evidence should have been suppressed because it was taken illegally. The court ruled that evidence obtained as a result of an illegal seizure was not admissible in the probation hearing. However, it also ruled that the roadblock was justified because the police had set up the roadblock for the sole purpose of checking driver's licenses. Thus, the roadblock was legal under Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art 6687b, § 13 (Supp. 1985). Although the trial court failed to make findings of fact on the sole purpose for the roadblock, a different result was not compelled and the verdict was sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which revoked appellant's probation because the roadblock, set up for the purpose of checking driver's licenses, was legal and evidence obtained at the roadblock could be used in his revocation hearing.

 

1293 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Dallas County Appraisal Dist. v. L.D. Brinkman & Co.


No. 05-84-01270-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


701 S.W.2d 20; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12873



October 31, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants Dallas County Appraisal District and its chief appraiser sought review from a District Court of Dallas County (Texas) in which the court determined that certain property held in warehouses by appellee businesses was not subject to ad valorem taxation in the state of Texas pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.01 because the property would be shipped out of state within 175 days.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, Dallas County Appraisal District and its chief appraiser contended that all of the inventory of appellee businesses that was in their warehouses on the first day of January, was subject to taxation. One appellee had presold 10 percent of its property to out-of-state customers and appellee the second appellee had not presold any of its property. Appellees' goods were not in interstate transit. The trial court excluded inventory which appellees shipped out within 175 days of its arrival in the state and deducted that portion of the inventory found to be in the state temporarily from the tax. The court reversed holding that goods were located within the state for longer than a temporary period if, under federal law, they were in the state on more than a transitory basis. Goods were not in interstate transit where there was an interruption in the continuity of transit. The court held that where goods were brought from out of state to a central depot and separated into those presold in other states, owners had detained all the goods for business and profits purposes and were within the tax jurisdiction of the state.


OUTCOME: The trial court reversed the determination because appellees' property was in the state for longer than a temporary period and was therefore subject to taxation by the state.

 

1294 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


State v. One 1980 Pontiac


No. 2-84-262-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


695 S.W.2d 821; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12116



 October 30, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 213th District Court of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review from the 213th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), in which forfeiture of appellee car and marihuana were denied under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 §§ 5.03(a)(5), 5.07(d) (1985). Appellant contended the evidence established conclusively the vehicle was subject to forfeiture.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state sought writ of sequestration (forfeiture), for appellee car and drugs alleging car was used to transport and facilitate the transport, possession and concealment of appellee marihuana. At the forfeiture hearing it was established by appellee owner of appellee car that she and her boyfriend left the house to pick up friends and go to dinner and she had one bag of marihuana in her purse and her boyfriend one bag in his boot. They were also smoking while in the car. Appellee owner pled guilty and received a fine of $ 50 and $ 82 court costs. The trial court denied the forfeiture. The court reversed holding that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.03(a) as amended, gave rise to the forfeiture without proving that appellee car facilitated the offense. Car was subject to forfeiture where a controlled substance existed within the confines of the moving vehicle with owner's knowledge, even if the controlled substance was in a purse or on a person.


OUTCOME: The court reversed denial of the forfeiture because the vehicle was used in transporting the marihuana from appellee's home to where they picked up friends, to a restaurant, and in the trip home. The caption to H.B. 1191 gave reasonable notice of changes in the amended statute. Delivery of a controlled substance was no longer needed to forfeit a motor vehicle.

Galvan v. State


Nos. 3-84-257-CR, 3-84-258-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


699 S.W.2d 663; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12409



October 30, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 04/15/1987
Subsequent appeal at, Appeal dismissed by Galvan v. State, 2014 Tex. App. LEXIS 7397 (Tex. App. Austin, July 9, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Williamson County, 26th Judicial District No. 83,002-K, Honorable John R. Carter, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the 26th Judicial District Court of Williamson County (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, which found them guilty of the offense of injury to a child in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 (1985), and assessed punishment at 50 years incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were found guilty of the offense of injury to a child. On review, appellant argued that (1) the indictment was duplicitous; (2) the trial court erred in allowing a certain witness to testify as an expert; (3) the evidence was insufficient to support their conviction; and (4) the jury charge was erroneous. The court found that the rationale for the duplicity rule was not offended by indictment because appellants could readily ascertain that they were charged with causing serious bodily harm to their child by failing to provide him with the food and medical care that the law required them to provide. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the state's witness qualified as an expert. Further, the court concluded that a rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the offense of injury to a child had been proved beyond a reasonable doubt by the state. Finally, appellants' complaint with regard to the jury charge was not properly before the court because they were raised for the first time in the supplemental brief. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for the offense of injury to a child was affirmed because the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that appellants had the conscious objective or desire to cause serious bodily injury to their child by omitting to provide food and medical care.

 

1297 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Young, Wilkinson & Roberts v. Abilene


No. 11-85-123-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


704 S.W.2d 380; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12164



October 17, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Taylor County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant sought review of a decision from the trial court, Taylor County (Texas), denying plaintiff's application for a liquor license because plaintiff's restaurant did not meet the requirements of defendant City of Abilene's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff restaurant challenged the trial court's refusal to approve plaintiff's application for a license to sell alcoholic beverages at plaintiff's place of business, which was located in an area zoned "heavy commercial" within defendant city's boundaries. Defendant's board of adjustment had denied plaintiff's request for a variance from the requirements of Abilene, Tex., Zoning Ordinance § 23-306.5.H(13)(b), which barred on-premise consumption of alcohol within 300 feet of any residential lot. The trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court held that home rule cities such as defendant had authority to regulate the sale of intoxicating beverages. Defendant's zoning ordinance was not inconsistent with Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 109.33 (1985), which limited the availability of alcoholic beverages to establishments more than 300 feet from churches, schools, and hospitals but made no mention of residential lots. The ordinance was not inconsistent with the state statute because defendant's zoning powers could not be limited by state liquor laws. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision upholding the constitutionality of defendant city's zoning ordinance. A state law governing the serving of on-premise alcoholic beverages did not restrict defendant from promulgating a less-permissive ordinance because state liquor statutes had no effect on the zoning powers of home-rule cities such as defendant. Plaintiff restaurant's application for a zoning variance was properly denied.

Malloy v. Blau


No. 07-84-0170-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


698 S.W.2d 255; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12158



October 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Lipscomb County; 31ST Judicial District; No. 2031; Honorable Grainger W. McIlhany, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, heirs of a mineral rights owner, challenged the judgment from the 31st District Court of Lipscomb County (Texas) that granted the motion of appellees, assignees of a surface rights owner, for summary judgment on appellants' action to set aside an old judgment divesting them of their rights. Appellants claimed that the failure of the original plaintiff to use due diligence to find devisee's address made service by publication invalid.


OVERVIEW: The father of appellants, his heirs, purchased the mineral rights in a tract of land after the predecessor of appellees, its assignees, waived priority of its vendor's lien in favor of the father. After the father died, the predecessor filed a trespass to try title suit against the father's unknown heirs, and obtained service by publication and a judgment that divested appellants of their mineral rights. Years later appellants sued to set aside the judgment, and the trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that because appellants produced evidence showing that the address of appellants' mother, their fathers' devisee, was easily ascertainable at the time the predecessor filed its suit, appellants raised issues of material fact on whether the predecessor had failed in its common law duty to use due diligence in attempting to find the devisee's address, and whether the predecessor's acts in failing to use due diligence or present material evidence to the trial court constituted fraud or wrongful acts that would entitled appellants to relief from judgment. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the motion of appellees, successors of a surface rights owner, for summary judgment on the action of appellants, heirs of a mineral rights owner, to set aside an old judgment divesting them of their rights. The court held that issues of fact remained on whether original plaintiff obtained service by publication by its failure to use due diligence to find a devisee's address, and whether the failure was fraud.

Preston v. State


No. A14-84-858-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


699 S.W.2d 307; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7362



October 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 398,769.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction, by the 228th District Court of Harris County (Texas), of conspiracy to deliver cocaine, contending that the caption of the 1983 amendment to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976), violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35, because it failed to provide reasonable readers with notice that the amendment incorporated Tex. Penal Code tit. 4 into the provisions of the Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of conspiracy to deliver cocaine in excess of 400 grams and sought review, contending that the caption of the 1983 amendment to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 ( 1976), violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35 because it failed to provide reasonable readers with notice that the amendment incorporated Tex. Penal Code tit. 4 into the provisions of the Act. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. It held that the caption to the Act was not unconstitutional where it specifically stated its general purpose and proposed content, the subject of the amending act was germane to and not too remote from the subject of the original Act, and no new matter was included in the amendatory act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that the caption to the amending act was not unconstitutional where it specifically stated its general purpose and proposed content and it included no new subject matter not germane to the original Texas Controlled Substances Act.

 

1300 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Padilla v. State


No. 08-85-00018-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


697 S.W.2d 525; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7333



October 2, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 327th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, (TC# 37,334).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the 327th District Court, El Paso County (Texas), revoking defendant's probation following repeated incidents of public intoxication. Defendant alleged that the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that he was intoxicated to a point of presenting a danger to himself and that the recent amendments to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02 were unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. III, § 35.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to arson of a vehicle and the trial court imposed probation. Following two incidents of public intoxication, the court revoked probation and sentenced defendant to imprisonment. On appeal from a revocation of probation, the court held that the prosecution's evidence was sufficient to support a finding that defendant was intoxicated to a point of presenting a danger to himself. The court noted that he was staggering drunk and on the verge of falling and that he was vulnerable to criminal conduct. The court found it was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to conclude that he posed an additional danger if he drove away in his vehicle while intoxicated. The court held that the amendments to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.02 to include the burning of one's own vehicle in the definition of arson did not violate Tex. Const. art. III, § 35, as the caption to the amending legislation gave fair notice of the change. The court noted that the caption specifically stated the proposed changes and that the legislation only partially changed the existing code sections and did not amend existing penalties.


OUTCOME: The order revoking defendant's probation was affirmed as the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of intoxication to a point of presenting a danger to himself and the recent amendments to the penal code adding burning of ones' own vehicle to the definition of arson were constitutional as the legislative caption preceding the amendments gave fair notice of the change.

Helms v. Texas Alcoholic Beverage, Com.


No. 13-85-010-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


700 S.W.2d 607; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12155



September 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 7, 1985, Reported at: 700 S.W.2d 607 at 614.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 267th District Court of Victoria County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tavern owner challenged an order of the 267th District Court of Victoria County (Texas), affirming the denial of an on-premises beer and wine permit, pursuant to Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 61.42.


OVERVIEW: Appellee licensing commission denied an application by individual appellant for an on-premises beer and wine retailer's permit on the ground that the place or manner in which appellant might conduct his business would adversely affect the general welfare, health, peace, morals, safety, and sense of decency of the people of the area, contrary to the provisions of the Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 61.42. The permit was denied following a hearing in which property owners living in the immediate area, church members, members of the board of a nearby public school, the mayor, chief of police, and the sheriff opposed the grant of the permit. On appeal, the court determined that the location of the proposed licensed premises was adjacent to a church where civic and social activities were held, and also to a low-income housing project as well as a school. It held that the granting of the permit at the proposed licensed premises would result in an adverse change in the character of the neighborhood. It affirmed the denial of the permit.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. Appellant tavern owner was properly denied an on-premises wine and beer permit, because the location of appellant's premises would adversely affect the general welfare, health, peace, morals, safety, and sense of decency of the people of the area.

 

1302 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. Houston Gulf Coast Bldg.


No. 01-85-0649-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


697 S.W.2d 850; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7275



September 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 152nd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 85-38608. Jack O'Neill, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the 152nd District Court of Harris County (Texas) that issued an injunction, pursuant to appellee trade council's request, that prohibited appellant from enacting an ordinance that would set average wage rates to be paid workers on public works.


OVERVIEW: Members of appellee trade council worked for appellant city on public works projects. Pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5159a, appellant is authorized to determine general prevailing wage rates. Appellant proposed an ordinance that would set prevailing wage rates based upon a survey of wages. Appellee opposed such ordinance contending that art. 5159a did not define prevailing wage, so the term should mean the predominant wage rate. Appellee filed an action for injunctive relief that sought to enjoin appellant from adopting the ordinance. The trial court issued a temporary injunction. On appeal, the court dissolved the injunction. The trial court exceeded its judicial authority issuing the temporary injunction. The ordinance was still in the proposal stages, so that the trial court did not have the authority to predetermine the validity of the ordinance. The legislative process had not yet been completed, yet the trial court interfered with such process.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the injunction because the trial court did not have the authority to enjoin appellant city from enacting the ordinance. The ordinance had not been adopted and was still in the legislative process. The trial court could not interfere in such process based on separation of power principles.

 

1303 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Mansfield v. Port Lavaca


No. 13-84-349-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


698 S.W.2d 429; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7321



September 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 267th District Court of Calhoun County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the decision by the 267th District Court of Calhoun County(Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee city on appellants' action for declaratory judgment to set aside the sale of appellee's land.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city contracted to convey land to appellee dock companies. Appellants brought an action for declaratory judgment to set aside the sale of patent land. The trial court granted judgment against appellants. Appellants contended that appellee city could not sell the lands because they were owned by the public school fund. The court found the point to be without merit because the lands were not owned by the state when it was sold to appellee city. The court rejected appellants' arguments that the land was a public park subject to regulation as it was never designated as a park. Contrary to appellants' contention, no valid referendum was presented to the city council. The court found no violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5421c-12, which concerned notice requirements prior to the sale of political subdivision's land. The court found that the trial court correctly refused to grant leave to amend appellants' affidavits and exhibits because their request was not timely. The court also found that the grant of land to appellee city was not unconstitutional. Finally, the court did agree that there were material fact issues which precluded summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision and rejected multiple arguments asserted by appellants. The court held that the lands were not owned by the state, the land was not a public park, no referendum was presented, notice requirements were not violated, no constitutional violations occurred, and there were no fact issues preventing summary judgment.

 

1304 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. State


No. 2-84-044-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


696 S.W.2d 288; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7254



September 25, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a Criminal District Court No. 3 of Tarrant County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Criminal District Court No. 3 of Tarrant County (Texas) for burglary by committing and attempting to commit theft under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary by committing and attempting to commit theft under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1974). The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court committed reversible error in not granting appellant's motion to set aside the indictment for violation of the Texas Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 32A.01, 02 when the indictment was issued a year after he was charged. The court held that merely requesting the issuance of a bench warrant to procure a defendant's presence at trial within 120 days did not constitute due diligence with the meaning of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02, §§ 4(5), (9). The court held that there was no exceptional circumstances exception to take the case out of the Texas Speedy Trial Act because prosecutor could have verified whether the bench warrant had been issued. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 32A.01, 02 were not unconstitutional due a defective caption because the caption to the Speedy Trial Act succinctly provided fair notice to a reasonable reader of the subject and content of the bill.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction, holding that the trial court committed reversible error in not granting appellant's motion to set aside the indictment for violation of the Texas Speedy Trial Act because requesting the issuance of a bench warrant was not sufficient to procure appellant's presence at trial and did not constitute due diligence on prosecutor's part.

 

1305 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Honc v. State


No. 13-84-289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


698 S.W.2d 218; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7270



September 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 10, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 107th District Court of Cameron County, Texas, Tr. Ct. No. 84-CR-177-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision by the 107th District Court of Cameron County (Texas), which convicted him of sexual assault, indecency with a child, and injury to a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere to charges of sexual assault, indecency with a child, and injury to a child, all of which were contained in one indictment. The trial court assessed punishment at ten years. The appellate court reversed and remanded for reassessment of the punishment. The appellate court reasoned that sexual assault did not become an offense until after the date it was alleged that appellant committed the crime. As a result, the count of sexual assault was reversed. The court did find sufficient evidence to find that appellant penetrated the victim's vagina with his hand, and intent to arouse or gratify sexual desire was inferred from the circumstances. Likewise, intent to gratify sexual desire was inferred by appellant's conduct in touching the breasts of victim. There was no evidence in the record to support appellant's allegation that the victim was 14 years old at the time the conduct occurred. Language in the indictment that specified the instrument used to inflict injuries upon the victim, was surplus and state did not have to prove the use of that instrument. The court remanded for sentencing on the counts except for the sexual assault count.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for sexual assault because the crime was not an offense at the time it was committed. The court found that evidence supported the other convictions, but remanded for sentencing because sentencing had been imposed for all three crimes together at trial.

 

1306 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of Unnamed Baby McLean


No. 2-84-141-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


697 S.W.2d 479; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7235



September 17, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 89TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the judgment of the 89th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), which, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.21 (Vernon Supp. 1985), denied appellant's petition for voluntary legitimation and managing conservatorship of his and appellee mother's biological child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father challenged the trial court judgment denying his cross-action petition for voluntary legitimation and managing conservatorship of his and appellee mother's biological child in the prospective adoptive parents' action to terminate appellant and appellee's parent-child relationships. The trial court appointed the child welfare unit of Wichita County Family Court Services (CWU) managing conservator of the child. The court affirmed. It was within the trial court's discretion to determine appellant's fitness to assume parental responsibility, and in light of appellee and CWU's testimony against appellant's fitness, the trial court's finding that the best interest of the child was served by denying appellant's petition was not clearly erroneous. The requirement of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.21 (Vernon Supp. 1985) that appellee show that legitimation was in the child's best interest did not violate due process and equal protection because the statute's gender-based distinction substantially relates to the important state objective of promoting illegitimate children's best interests. For the same reason, § 13.21 did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, sec. 3A.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment denying appellant father's petition for voluntary legitimation and managing conservatorship of his and appellee mother's biological child. The trial court's finding that it was in the child's best interest to deny appellant's petition was not clearly erroneous. Statutory requirements that appellant show that legitimation was in the child's best interest did not violate due process or equal protection.

 

1307 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. White Motor Credit Corp.


No. 05-84-00032-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


708 S.W.2d 465; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12912



September 16, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 21, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a borrower and guarantor, sought reversal of an order of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which granted judgment on a jury verdict to appellee lender in its action on a defaulted truck installment sales contract. Appellees filed a counterclaim based on usury under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-8.01 and art. 5069-8.02 (Vernon 1983), but the jury found the usury to be the result of an unintentional and bona fide error.


OVERVIEW: Appellant creditor sought judgment on a defaulted truck installment sales contract, and its initial and first amended pleading erroneously included unearned interest and charges, without credits. Appellees, a debtor and guarantor, filed a counterclaim based on usury under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5069-8.01 and art. 5069-8.02 (Vernon 1983), but the jury found the usury to be the result of an unintentional and bona fide error and the trial court followed the jury verdict and gave judgment to appellee. The court reversed judgment against appellant debtor and remanded, and held that appellee's own pleadings established usury because they were an attempt to "collect" interest, and that although a bona fide error was a defense to usury, it was only available by showing not only that bona fide error existed but also that the error was made notwithstanding the maintenance of procedures adopted to avoid the error. Appellee had its financial person review the pleadings for form, not content, so it had not shown the second element. Usury was not a defense for a guarantor, however, unless the guaranty agreement so provided, so the judgment against appellant guarantor was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against appellant borrower based on the usury defense and remanded, because appellee lender had not shown that it had and followed established procedures intended to avoid errors, so the claim of bona fide error was not available against usury, which was established by appellee's pleadings. The court affirmed judgment against appellant guarantor because usury was a personal defense of an obligor.

 

1308 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Tolbert v. State


No. 01-84-00690-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


697 S.W.2d 795; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7195



September 12, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 21st District Court of Burleson County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 9517.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 21st District Court of Burleson County (Texas), which convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child younger than age 14, on grounds that the admission of the complainant's videotape testimony under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (1985) violated appellant's U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confrontation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child younger than age 14 and assessed a punishment of 40 years confinement. At the trial, appellant filed a motion to suppress a videotape interview of the complainant on grounds that the videotape had to be taken before the proceeding began under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071 (1985). The trial court denied the motion and admitted the videotape. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the trial court. The court held that the state was not required to allege that the complainant was under age 12 in the indictment. The age requirement was satisfied because the complainant testified to being 11 years old. The provisions of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (1985), were not prima facie violative of the U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confrontation. Appellant did not have to be permitted to cross-examine the complainant simultaneously with the taking of the videotape statement. The court held that the right to confrontation was satisfied if the witness was subjected to full and effective cross-examination at the trial. Appellant was not denied due process by the admission of the videotape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant of aggravated sexual assault of a child younger than 14 years old because the admission of the complainant's videotape testimony did not violate appellant's Sixth Amendment right to cross-examination and the right to confrontation was satisfied if the witness was subjected to full and effective cross-examination at trial.

Ex parte Allen


No. 05-85-00180-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


699 S.W.2d 886; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12875



August 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 699 S.W.2d 886 at 894.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a ruling of a district court in Dallas County (Texas), which denied his application for writ of habeas corpus by which he sought to avoid extradition to Tennessee to face charges of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant faced extradition to Tennessee where he had been charged with armed robbery; he agreed in writing, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 1.14, to waive his right to have the matter of extradition heard by a district judge. Extradition was ordered, and appellant applied to the trial court for habeas corpus relief, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial because the governor's warrant appellant claimed could not stand on an alleged unreliable identification affidavit was not requisite to the warrant's validity. The court found that the demanding state's governor's warrant and attached documents were sufficient proof that appellant was in the demanding state on the date of the offense and overruled his point that the extradition proceeding held before a magistrate was tantamount to a trial on the merits because the hearing did not involve a ruling on any issue of law or fact, the decision on which could result in dismissal of the case. The court ruled that appellant's right to confrontation was not violated by introduction of the governor's warrant and supporting papers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus, which was filed after appellant was ordered extradited to Tennessee. The court ruled that the hearing was not tantamount to a trial on the merits because the hearing did not involve an issue of law or fact, the decision on which could result in dismissal of the case.

 

1310 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bellamy v. State


No. 12-82-0052-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


747 S.W.2d 384; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12067



August 29, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 145th District Court of Nacogdoches County, Texas


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a ruling of the 145th District Court of Nacogdoches County, Texas, which convicted him of theft and assessed his punishment at five years' confinement, probated for five years, and a fine of $ 5000.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a dealer of secondhand personal property, bought some items from sellers; he did not obtain the information required by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3) (1985), when he paid $ 25 or more for such property. A dealer not in compliance with § 31.03(c)(3) was presumed to know that the property was stolen. Appellant was arrested for theft, found guilty, and given a probated sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that § 31.03(c)(3) did not deprive appellant of due process in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV by shifting the burden of proof from the state to appellant because the presumption did not undermine the jury's responsibilities; the jury was instructed to decide first beyond a reasonable doubt if the property was stolen then to consider all the evidence to determine if appellant knew the property was stolen. The court found that the magistrate who issued the warrant and then had accompanied the officers to the arrest scene had behaved improperly, but ruled that he was merely an observer. The court held that the affidavit's statement which named two accomplices rather than the actual seller was not false because the whole group was involved in the sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for theft and upheld the constitutionality of the presumption that a dealer in secondhand property who failed to collect specified information from a seller was presumed to know that the property was stolen because the jury was instructed to first determine beyond a reasonable doubt if the property was stolen and then to consider all the evidence to decide appellant's guilt.

 

1311 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. Safeco Ins. Co.


No. 05-84-01079-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


696 S.W.2d 678; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7366



August 23, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant customer sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which denied appellant's recovery on a bond secured by appellee surety, in appellant's successful underlying action against an alarm systems installer who filed the bond as required by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb), § 40(a).


OVERVIEW: In the underlying action, appellant customer sued an alarm systems installer for breach of a contract to install a burglar alarm system in appellant's place of business. The trial court entered judgment for appellant, and awarded treble damages and attorney's fees under the Deceptive Trade Practices Act. Appellant then filed an action against appellee surety, seeking to satisfy his judgment from the surety bond filed by the installer as required by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb), § 40(a). The trial court denied appellant's recovery on the bond, and appellant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the bond required by § 40(a) was not a performance bond, but a fidelity bond given to protect the employer or user of the services from abuses arising out of confidential information possessed by the licensee. If the bond were a performance bond, appellee's breach of contract would constitute a violation of the act for which appellee would be subject to penal sanctions. The court refused to attribute to the legislature an intent to impose a penal sanction upon the simple breach of a private contract.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant customer's recovery on the bond against appellee surety because it was a fidelity bond rather than a performance bond. The fidelity bond protected only against abuses arising out of confidential information obtained by the alarm installer, not a breach of contract.

Boulding v. State


Nos. A14-83-759-CR, C14-83-760-CR

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for two counts of sexual abuse of a child, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.10 (1974). Defendant contended that the joinder of the two separate offenses in one indictment was improper. The court held that, because the two separate offenses did not arise out of the same episode, the joinder was improper, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 21.24(a) (Supp. 1985) and Tex. The court held that joinder of the two separate offenses was improper because they did not arise out of the same episode. The court held that the portion of the statute which improperly discriminated according to the sex of the abused child was unconstitutional.

 

1313 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. State


No. 01-85-0175-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


696 S.W.2d 465; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12133



August 22, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court No. 2 of Galveston County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 74,400.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Court No. 2 of Galveston County (Texas), which convicted him of resisting arrest and sentenced him to 25 days confinement after denying his motion to dismiss for lack of a speedy trial, based on the state's argument that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 was unconstitutional, because its caption did not comply with Tex. Const. art. III, §. 35.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court denied appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of a speedy trial, based on the state's argument that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 was unconstitutional, because its caption did not comply with Tex. Const. art. III, § 35, appellant was convicted of resisting arrest and sentenced to 25 days confinement. On appeal, the court reversed and entered a judgment of acquittal, holding that art. 32A.02, as part of the Speedy Trial Act (Act), was constitutional, because it met the "fair notice" standard. The court noted that the standard applied because the Act's caption contained the participles "adding" and "amending", which conveyed to the readers the character and quality of the legislation. Further, the Act was an addition to the Code of Criminal Procedure rather than an amendment of any statute dealing with speedy trials. Therefore, the caption to the Act put the reader on notice that something entirely new could be found in the Code of Criminal Procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction of resisting arrest and entered a judgment of acquittal, holding that the Speedy Trial Act was constitutional because it met the "fair notice" standard.

Garza v. Block Distributing Co.


No. 04-83-00436-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


696 S.W.2d 259; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7320



August 21, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 37th District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 82-CI-15833, Rose Spector, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county tax assessor-collector and county judge, appealed the judgment of the 37th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted a permanent injunction restraining any effort to levy, assess, or collect any additional ad valorem taxes upon tangible personal property owned by plaintiff taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer was a wholesale liquor dealer and the bulk of its taxable property consisted of its inventory of liquor. Defendant county tax assessor-collector sent plaintiff a tax statement, showing an increased valuation of the property, along with the increase in taxes due, without notifying plaintiff of any hearing at which it could protest this unilateral imposition of an additional tax burden upon its property. Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment that the increase in valuation was invalid because of defendants' failure to give plaintiff notice prior to increasing its valuations. Plaintiff also sought, and obtained a temporary restraining order enjoining defendants from increasing the valuation on plaintiff's property. The temporary restraining order was converted into a temporary injunction. At the bench trial, it was established that plaintiff's valuation was increased without prior notice having been given. Defendants appealed, and the court agreed with the trial court, concluding that the appraisal board never acquired jurisdiction of the proposed increase in value, and, therefore, its approval thereof was a void act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff taxpayer because the county tax assessor-collector increased the valuation of the property without giving notice of a hearing at which plaintiff could protest the additional tax burden. Thus, the appraisal board never acquired jurisdiction of the proposed increase in value, and so its approval thereof was a void act.

State v. Coca Cola Bottling Co. of Southwest


No. 04-85-00032-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


697 S.W.2d 677; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12267; 1985-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P66,765



August 21, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 57th District Court of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 84-CI-15586, Honorable Fred Biery, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state of Texas sought review of a 57th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) decision that dismissed its petition that asserted appellee soft drink companies violated the Texas Free Enterprise and Antitrust Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 15.05(d).


OVERVIEW: Appellant state of Texas sought review of a decision that dismissed its petition that asserted appellees soft drink companies violated the Texas Free Enterprise and Antitrust Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 15.05 (d) (Act). The court stated the legislative history of the federal antitrust laws indicated that Congress did not reserve the exclusive regulation of mergers and acquisitions to the exclusion of the states. The court held it was evident that the Act was patterned on the Clayton Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 18 (Supp. 1985) and the act could be construed in harmony with federal judicial interpretations of comparable antitrust statutes.
