1316 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


FANNING v. STATE


No. 01-84-00423-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11978



August 15, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 176th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 383,253


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 176th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of robbery and assessed punishment at five years probation and a $ 1,200 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant along with three men came to the complainant's apartment in the middle of the night. Appellant loudly cursed and threatened the complainant, stating that she wanted to beat the complainant up due to the car accident that he allegedly caused. One of the men brandished a gun, the complainant's keys were taken, and the men beat him. The complainant thought appellant was at the wheel when they left. Appellant was convicted of robbery and sentenced to five years in prison. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that it was permissible for the jury charge to given in the disjunctive when the components were different ways of committing the same offense. The court also held that appellant's constitutional rights were not violated, and the indictment was not fundamentally defective, as the jury charge could allow appellant's conviction as a party without the indictment alleging generally that she was a party or specific facts making her party. Appellant was thus guilty as a party to the offense, because she was present at the commission of the offense and encouraged the commission of the offense by words.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's robbery conviction because it was permissible for the jury charge to given in the disjunctive when the components were different ways of committing the same offense, the jury charge could allow appellant's conviction as a party without the indictment alleging generally that she was a party, and appellant was guilty as a party as she was present and encouraged the commission.

 

1317 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Retail Merchants Asso. v. Handy Dan Hardware, Inc.


No. 01-84-0798-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


696 S.W.2d 44; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11961



August 8, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 696 S.W.2d 44 at 54.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 280th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 83-70032. Original Opinion of April 25, 1985, Reported at: 696 S.W.2d 44.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee hardware corporation sought a rehearing of the review of the judgment of the 280th District Court of Harris County (Texas), contending that the court erred by ignoring findings of fact of the trial court, that the findings were binding on the court in its review of the constitutionality of the Blue Law since they were unchallenged by appellant, merchants association, and that the court erred in reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellee hardware corporation filed a motion for rehearing an appeal, claiming that the court erred in ignoring the trial court's factual findings, that those findings were binding on the court in its review of the constitutionality of the Blue Law, that the court should have considered only its evidence and construed all inferences in its favor, and that the court erred in reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence. The court held that where a statute's constitutionality was challenged under the due process and equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions, the reviewing court was required to examine all the evidence presented to demonstrate the absence of any rational relationship between the statute's means and ends. On original submission, the court reviewed all the evidence, including that admitted by judicial notice, but absent an evaluation of witness credibility, in determining that appellee failed to meet its burden. The standards of review developed to evaluate the constitutionality of economic legislation narrowly circumscribed the powers of the appellate judiciary. The court could not encroach upon the powers of the legislature to formulate policy.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellee hardware corporation's motion for rehearing. The court held that where a statute's constitutionality was challenged under the due process and equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions, the reviewing court was required to examine all the evidence presented to demonstrate the absence of any rational relationship between the statute's means and ends.

 

1318 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Jolar Cinema of Houston, Inc. v. Houston


No. 01-85-0103-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


695 S.W.2d 353; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6916



August 1, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 333rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 84-62202.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business sought review of the judgment of the 333rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which granted appellee city a temporary injunction prohibiting appellant from providing live performances for the sexual stimulation or gratification of its customers. Also, appellee claimed that the trial court abused its discretion is failing to enjoin appellant's entire operation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city sought and obtained a temporary injunction against appellant business based on appellant's violation of Houston, Tex., Ordinance ch. 83-1812, § 28.73(B), which made it unlawful for a business with a sexual orientation to operate without first obtaining a permit from appellee. In affirming the judgment, the court found that the ordinance did not violate the U.S. Const. amend. I right to free expression guaranteed to the states by U.S. Const. XIV because it did not prohibit all such entertainment but only sought to regulate it. The court found that the standard of review was whether the trial court clearly abused its discretion in granting the injunction and that it had no authority to delve into the merits of the case. Thus the court found that appellant's claim that its business was limited to coin operated machines was not properly before it. The court also found that Tex. Rev. Civ. Code Ann. art 2372w, § 3b did not prohibit the ordinance in question. The court found no error in the injunction's limitation to live performances because no evidence had been submitted to the trial court of the materials contained on appellant's coin operated machines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the temporary injunction against appellant business because it found no clear abuse of discretion. Appellee city's ordinance requiring appellant to obtain a permit for this type of business did not violate the right of free expression because it did not prohibit all sexual entertainment but only sought to regulate such businesses through a licensing system.

 

1319 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. Wershba


No. C14-84-884-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


698 S.W.2d 369; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11946



August 1, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 190th District Court of Harris County, Trial Court No. 84-15404.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the summary judgment of the 190th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that dismissed her medical malpractice claim against appellee podiatrist on statute of limitations grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient last received medical care from appellee podiatrist on March 1, 1982, but learned of an unauthorized procedure that appellee performed on her and his failure to perform a surgical procedure on January 3, 1983. Appellant's attorney sent a statutorily required notice of claim on March 7, 1983, but she did not file her medical malpractice cause of action until April 2, 1984. When appellee's motion for summary judgment, based on the expiration of the statute of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, §10.01 was granted, appellant sought review of the dismissal. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and held that the unconstitutionality of § 10.01 was applicable only to medical malpractice actions where discovery of the alleged malpractice could not have been reasonably discovered until more than two years after the discovery. Because plaintiff discovered her alleged malpractice at least 13 months prior to filing the action, she had a reasonable opportunity to discover it and to commence the action within the time limits of the statute. The court, therefore, overruled her points of error and affirmed summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment of appellant patient's medical malpractice cause of action against appellee podiatrist on statute of limitations grounds, because the action was filed after two years from the last treatment date, and the dismissal was not an unconstitutional violation of equal protection because of her inability to avail herself of any statute of repose.

McCulloch v. Fox & Jacobs, Inc.


No. 05-83-01329-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


696 S.W.2d 918; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7147



July 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) that granted summary judgment to appellee in a tort action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's son suffered severe injuries after diving in the shallow end of a pool. Appellant alleged several negligence claims. Additionally, appellant alleged strict liability, charging that the defective design of the pool rendered it unreasonably dangerous. Appellee contended that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5536a barred all of appellee's causes of action. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee. Appellant sought review. The critical inquiry was whether appellee's role in constructing the pool was more analogous to a builder or to an owner or supplier. Appellant argued that appellee was merely a residential developer. Appellee countered that, as supervisor of the project, it was sufficiently involved in the construction process to merit the protection of the statute. The court agreed that appellee was a "person performing or furnishing construction of an improvement." Thus, the statute protected appellee from suit after ten years. The court affirmed. The summary judgment evidence established as a matter of law that article 5536a barred commencement and prosecution of each of appellant's causes of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee in appellant's tort action because the summary judgment evidence established that a statute of repose barred all of appellant's claims.

 

1321 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 05-84-00807-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


695 S.W.2d 686; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12080



June 28, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 30, 1985..


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of a District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of gambling promotion. Appellant argued that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to quash the indictment because it was impossible to tell from the face of the indictment whether the state meant to indict appellant for receiving a bet or for making a bet.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of gambling promotion by the court below. The indictment alleged that appellant received a bet from another person on the final result of a college football game, but then, in setting forth the transaction between appellant and that other person, the indictment alleges that appellant made a bet with that other person. Appellant filed a motion to quash based, in part, on insufficiency of notice. The court below denied the motion to quash. On appeal, the court found that it was impossible to tell from the face of the indictment whether the state meant to indict appellant for receiving a bet, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03(a)(2), or for making a bet, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.02(a)(1). The court found that the failure of the indictment to give appellant precise notice of the offense charged against him compelled reversal. Accordingly, the court found that the trial court had erred when it denied appellant's motion to quash. The court reversed the judgment of the court below and ordered the dismissal of the indictment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which convicted appellant of gambling promotion, was reversed and the court below was ordered to dismiss the indictment because it was impossible to tell from the face of the indictment whether the state meant to indict appellant for receiving a bet or for making a bet. The failure of the indictment to give appellant precise notice of the offense charged against him compelled reversal.

SCHWANECKE v. VASEEM ALI


No. 01-84-0664-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11762



June 27, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 127th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 79-34630


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group of individuals against abortion, sought review of an order of the 127th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which rendered summary judgment for appellees, a group of doctors, a private hospital, and the University of Texas, in appellants' claim to enjoin the performance of abortion procedures in Texas, to enjoin the expenditure of public funds for abortion, and for declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a group of individuals against abortion, filed a class action on behalf of children born following abortion attempts, unborn children, and taxpayers against appellees, a group of doctors, a private hospital, and the University of Texas, to enjoin the performance of abortion procedures in Texas, the expenditure of public funds for the procedures, declaratory relief as next friends for the classes of unborn and recently born children, and declaratory relief for the classes of Texas taxpayers. The trial court rendered summary judgment for appellees and awarded them attorney's fees. The court affirmed, holding that appellants did not have individual standing because they did not show a personal or particularized injury. Appellants also failed to provide evidence that the expenditure of public funds for abortion violated the Texas constitution or was otherwise unlawful. Because the alleged personal representatives of the class lacked personal standing, the claim on behalf of the class of Texas taxpayers also failed. Appellants failed to show an abuse of discretion in the award of attorney fees to appellees, physician, attorney general, and the University of Texas.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment to appellees, a group of doctors, a private hospital, and the University of Texas, was affirmed in a claim filed by appellants, a group of individuals against abortion, to enjoin the performance of abortions in Texas, the expenditure of public funds for abortion, and for declaratory relief because appellants did not have standing to maintain the action.

 

1323 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


TABOR v. JOE A. MCDERMOTT INC.


No. 01-85-0127-CV.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11769



June 27, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 190th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 82-3759-A


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged the order of the 190th District Court, Harris County, Texas that denied his motion to dissolve a writ of garnishment. This writ of garnishment was an interlocutory order of the trial court intended to protect funds, which might have been owed to appellee garnishor as a result of a judgment against a partnership of which appellant was a partner.


OVERVIEW: Appellee garnishor held a judgment against a partnership and applied for a writ of garnishment against a corporation asserting that the corporation was indebted to the partnership. The corporation acknowledged its debt and indicated that partnership assigned the debt to appellant individual, a partner in that partnership. The trial court denied appellant's motion to dissolve the writ of garnishment. The trial court held that appellee had a judgment against the partnership, which was outstanding, and ordered the corporation to pay into the trial court's registry all funds owed to the partnership. The court dismissed the challenge to the trial court's judgment denying appellant's motion to dissolve the writ. Garnishment proceedings were not meant to challenge the underlying judgment and the majority of appellant's motion to dissolve the garnishment related to the underlying judgment, which he was also challenging by way of a bill of review. The court held that the trial court's orders placing the funds in its registry were designed to protect the interests of the parties pending the outcome of the bill of review. These orders were interlocutory and thus not final and appealable.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant individual's challenge to denial of its motion to dissolve the writ of garnishment entered on appellee garnishor's behalf because the writ was an interlocutory order that was not final and thus not appealable. The court noted that the interlocutory order was designed to protect the parties' interest pending a writ of review brought by appellant to challenge a judgment against a partnership.

 

1324 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Leonard v. State


No. 09-84-184 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


694 S.W.2d 625; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11930



June 27, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from a trial court (Texas) after a jury convicted him of delivery of a controlled substance. After a plea of "true" to a prior conviction, his punishment was assessed at 20 years.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for delivery of a controlled substance on the basis that there was insufficient or no evidence adduced to support the jury verdict as it related to all of the elements of the offense charged, and insufficient or no evidence and a fatal variance between evidence adduced and the allegation as to "Pentazocine." The court affirmed the judgment on the basis that although the indictment included the statement that appellant delivered a controlled substance in a quantity not less than 200 grams, the 1979 Controlled Substances Act (Act) was applicable to appellant's prosecution and it did not have a weight differential scheme. As weight was not an essential element of the offense, it was not required to be proven. Relating to the allegation as to Pentazocine, the court found that despite difficulty with the pronunciation of Pentazocine throughout the trial, the jury heard testimony from a chemist and defense counsel stated that he was not challenging what the substance was. There was sufficient evidence to support the finding that appellant delivered Pentazocine, and there was no fatal variance between the indictment and what was proven.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for delivery of a controlled substance because under the 1979 Controlled Substances Act, weight was not an essential element of the offense and the state was not required to present evidence as to the weight of the substance. The court also found sufficient evidence for the jury to find what appellant delivered was Pentazocine, and that there was no fatal variance in what was alleged and proven.

 

1325 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Coody v. A.H. Robins Co.


No. 04-83-00420-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


696 S.W.2d 154; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7316; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,719; 41 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1735



June 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing overruled August 21, 1985. Writ Filed September 20, 1985. Petitioner's Motion to Dismiss Application for Writ of Error (Due to Settlement) Granted September 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 131st District Court of Bexar County; Trial Court No. 80-CI-18960; Honorable Richard J. Woods, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party appealed from an order of the 131st District Court, Bexar County, Texas, that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant manufacturer. The summary judgment that plaintiff take nothing was based on the ground that her action for injuries resulting from her use of an intrauterine device manufactured by defendant was barred by limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured party was fitted with an intrauterine device (IUD) that was manufactured by defendant manufacturer. A few months later she developed pelvic inflammatory disease (PID) caused by the IUD. Several years later plaintiff learned that defendant had been sued for its defective design of the IUD. Plaintiff 's doctor told her that her IUD was the same one that was the subject of the lawsuits. Plaintiff sued defendant alleging defective design, breach of warranty, and negligence. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant on the ground the statutes of limitations periods had expired. Plaintiff appealed, and the court affirmed. Plaintiff's actions accrued when she knew or should have known of her injury. Here, plaintiff discovered her injury at the time she was diagnosed with PID. However, she waited seven years, which was when she learned of the other lawsuits, before filing her own action. The discovery rule did not operate to toll the running of the limitations period until such time as plaintiff discovered all the elements of a cause of action. Once she learned she had been injured, the burden was on her to determine whether she should file suit.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant manufacturer on statute of limitations grounds in plaintiff injured party's product liability suit was affirmed. The applicable statute of limitations periods commenced once plaintiff knew or should have known about her injury. The period was not tolled until such time as plaintiff discovered all the elements of her causes of action.

MAGRAY v. STATE


No. 01-84-0716-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11682



June 20, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 751,936


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas, that convicted him for selling an obscene magazine. On appeal, he argued that his conviction was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV, that the evidence was insufficient to establish that the material sold was constitutionally or factually obscene, and that there was no proof that he knew the content or character of the material.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced for selling an obscene magazine. On appeal, he advanced several arguments. First, he contended that the statutes under which he was convicted, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 43.21, 43.23, were unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV. The court found this argument lacked merit in view of applicable case law. Appellant also maintained that the evidence was insufficient to establish that the material sold was either constitutionally or factually obscene. The court reviewed the magazine under the applicable standard and determined that it was both factually and constitutionally obscene. Finally, appellant maintained that there was no proof that he knew either the content or character of the material. The court found that significant circumstantial evidence presented by appellee indicated that that appellant may have had reason to know that the magazine contained sexually explicit material. However, the entirety of the evidence did not establish that appellant had knowledge of its contents and character. Accordingly, the court ordered that the judgment of the trial court reversed.


OUTCOME: The conviction for selling an obscene magazine was reversed and reformed to reflect a judgment of acquittal. Evidence presented by appellee did not establish that appellant had knowledge of the contents and character of alleged obscene magazine.

Shults v. State


No. 05-83-00482-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


696 S.W.2d 126; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12146



June 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the District Court of Dallas County (Texas), finding that items taken in four seizures by police of appellants' store were drug paraphernalia, thus the trial court ordered forfeiture of the items pursuant to the state's notice of seizure and intended forfeiture under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.05.


OVERVIEW: Police seized drug paraphernalia from appellants' store on four occasions. After the first seizure took place, the state filed an original notice of seizure and intended forfeiture under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.05. The remaining seizures took place and the state filed notices of seizure and intended forfeiture on each. The forfeiture actions were consolidated. The trial jury found that items taken in the seizures were drug paraphernalia and the trial court ordered forfeiture of the items. Appellants argued that the proceedings regarding the first two seizures were not instituted within 10 days of the seizures as required by the 10 day time limit for filing notices of seizure and intended forfeiture that was reinstated by the criminal appellate court. The state argued that the drug paraphernalia forfeiture was a civil matter, not a criminal matter, thus, the civil appellate court was not bound by the decision of the criminal appellate court. The civil appellate court reversed and remanded the action as to the first two seizures, because they were not subject to the trial court's jurisdiction for purposes of forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the case was remanded. The forfeiture of certain items seized by police from appellant's store were improperly determined to be forfeited items of drug paraphernalia, because the state's notice of seizure and intended forfeiture was not filed within 10 days after the first two seizures, thus the notices of seizure and intended forfeiture were not timely filed. However, other items seized were forfeited.

Smith v. Houston


No. C14-85-132-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


693 S.W.2d 753; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 11691



June 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 133rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Cause No. 84-20681.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision from the 133rd District Court of Harris County (Texas) that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellants' declaratory action to set aside liens placed on their property.


OVERVIEW: Appellants owned property that fronted a road. Appellee city decided to wide the road, so it assessed appellants and other property owners a fee per square feet for such widening. Appellants refused to pay the assessment, so appellee placed liens on appellants' property. Appellants filed an action for declaratory relief that sought to have the liens set aside. Appellants contended the ordinance that apportioned the assessment was void. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court reversed the decision and remanded for further proceedings. The ordinance was void because it violated Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17. Section 17 prohibited assessments for other than the benefits conferred. The ordinance made the assessments without regard to any benefits conferred to the properties. The assessments were based on whether a property did or did not have a sidewalk, rather than the benefits conferred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded for further proceedings. The ordinance under which appellee city assessed appellant's property was void because it assessed appellants for other than benefits conferred. The assessment was based on whether appellants had a sidewalk or did not have a sidewalk.

 

1331 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Chopin v. Interfirst Bank Dallas N A


No. 05-84-00487-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


694 S.W.2d 79; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6834



June 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a Probate Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, joint account survivors, challenged the judgment from a probate court of Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee executor in appellee's action to recover the non-testamentary disposition of the decedent's interest in joint bank accounts.


OVERVIEW: The decedent had set up joint accounts with appellants, joint account survivors. Appellee executor filed suit, contending that the accounts were assets of the estate. The probate court granted summary judgment to appellee. One appellant had also moved for summary judgment contending that the accounts were gifts. The court of appeals affirmed except on the issue of interest. The Probate Code, in particular Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 439(a), controlled over Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 342-706 (1973). The latter section concerned itself with the right of possession, not the ownership of funds. Under § 439(a), a joint account did not automatically create a survivorship agreement. There had to be a separate written agreement. The signature cards for the accounts merely identified to whom a bank should deliver possession. There was no mention of joint tenancy or a right of survivorship. Section 439(a) trumped any common law intervivos gift rights. The Probate Code provided the exclusive means of disposing of a joint account. However, the granting of prejudgment interest to appellee from the date of appellants' possession of the accounts was an error.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee executor in its action against appellants, joint account survivors, to recover the proceeds of bank accounts held jointly with the decedent affirmed in part. Appellees were not entitled to the proceeds of the accounts absent a written agreement evidencing the decedent's intent. Appellee did not establish by law that it was entitled to prejudgment interest, and the cause was remanded on that issue.

1333 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Desemo v. Gafford


No. 11-85-059-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


692 S.W.2d 571; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6714



June 6, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Palo Pinto County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the judgment from the trial court of Palo Pinto County (Texas), which sustained appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment in appellant's action alleging negligence in medical care and treatment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient contended that appellee doctor was negligent in his medical care and treatment of her and that his negligent acts and omissions were the proximate causes of her injuries. The trial court found in favor of appellee. Appellant challenged the judgment, contending that her claim was not barred by the applicable statute of limitations. The court rejected appellant's contentions, finding that the statute of limitations as applied was not unconstitutional. The court held that the courts were open to appellant because she had consulted with her attorney and the notice letter was sent to appellee within the limitations period, but that the suit was not filed within the additional 75 days allotted for investigation of her claim. The court found that appellant should not benefit from tolling provisions for persons with an unsound mind because the language of the statute of limitations provided that it applied to all persons regardless of legal disability. Accordingly, the court affirmed the holding of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that found in favor of appellee doctor. The court held that appellant patient's claim for negligence was barred by the statute of limitations because the statute was constitutional as applied to appellant since the courts were open to her within the limitations period but that she failed to timely file her claim.

Long v. State


No. 05-84-00181-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


694 S.W.2d 185; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6821



June 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the District Court of Dallas County (Texas) for sexual abuse of a child and sentenced to 20 years' imprisonment, contending that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right of confrontation was violated by the admission of videotaped testimony of the complaining witness under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2, (1985).


OVERVIEW: In appellant's conviction for sexual abuse of a child, the trial court held that a videotape recording of an interview of the complainant, a 12 year old child with a rape crisis therapist, was admitted into evidence pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2, (1985). The court reversed appellant's conviction and held that article 38.071, § 2 was unconstitutional because the videotape procedure denied appellant his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront a witness. Article 38.071, § 2 did not afford appellant an opportunity for face-to-face confrontation, and the statute specifically prohibited his presence at the videotaping session. The court found that limitation of appellant's right of confrontation was not essential to advance the state's compelling interest in protecting the child because neither the record or legislative history showed that the child or sex-abuse victims were emotionally disturbed, reluctant to testify, or intimidated by the accused. The court held that the child's testimony as a rebuttal witness and appellant's cross-examination was not sufficient to preserve his constitutional right or make it harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for sexual abuse of a child, holding that the statute that allowed videotaped testimony of a child to be admitted into evidence in a sexual abuse case when appellant was not present or allowed to cross-examine the child was unconstitutional and violated his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation.

 

1335 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Vinklarek v. Cane


No. 14,395


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


691 S.W.2d 108; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6972



May 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing overruled June 12, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District No. 365,651, Honorable Joe Dibrell, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the judgment of the 345th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted defendant doctor summary judgment in plaintiff's medical malpractice claim against defendant for alleged negligent care and treatment. The lower court concluded that the claim was time-barred under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1985).


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff patient suffered an infection following an oral surgery, she filed a medical malpractice suit against defendant doctor for alleged negligent care and treatment in connection with the infection. The lower court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment concluding that the claim was barred by the statute of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1985). The court, on appeal, rejected defendant's contentions that the two-year statute of limitations commenced upon the last negligent act and reversed and remanded the case. The court held, under the continuing treatment doctrine, that the statute of limitations did not commence until the last treatment for the alleged injury occurred. The court further held that there was evidence to support the conclusion that there was a fact issue regarding when plaintiff 's last date of treatment occurred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the lower court, which granted defendant doctor summary judgment in plaintiff patient's medical malpractice claim against defendant; there was a fact issue as to whether or not plaintiff's claim was barred under the statute of limitations.

Council of Co-Owners of Saida II Towers Condominium Asso. v. Texas Catastrophe Property Ins. Asso.


No. 13,970


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


696 S.W.2d 60; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12102



May 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 126TH Judicial District No. 337,150A, Honorable Charles D. Mathews, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds challenged an order from the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed their causes of action for breach of property insurance contracts written by appellee insurer under the Catastrophe Property Insurance Pool Act, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.49 (1981 & Supp. 1984).


OVERVIEW: In appellant insureds' suit for breach of property insurance contracts against appellee insurer, the trial court dismissed appellants' complaints, holding that it had not jurisdiction over the matter under the Catastrophe Property Insurance Pool Act (Act), Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.49 (1981 & Supp. 1984). On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the trial court did have jurisdiction as the Act did not confer power upon the State Board of Insurance (board) to determine common-law causes of action for breach of contract. The court held that the board had no power to make incidental findings necessary to judicial determination of such causes of action, and any act purporting to make any such determination was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of appellant insureds' breach of contract suits against appellee insurer. The trial court had jurisdiction to determine the causes of action as under the Catastrophe Property Insurance Pool Act, the State Board of Insurance had no power to determine common-law causes of action for breach of contract.

 

1337 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Powell v. State


No. 05-84-00646-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


694 S.W.2d 416; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6833



May 28, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for indecency with a child by a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which allowed the admission into evidence of a videotape of the child's testimony under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071(4)-(5) (Supp. 1985), Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, and U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court admitted into evidence a videotape of a child victim's testimony, appellant was convicted of indecency with a child. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071(4)-(5) (Supp. 1985) was unconstitutional. The court held that art. 38.071(4)-(5) violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 10 and U.S. Const. amend. VI because appellant was not afforded the right to confront and cross-examine the witness. The court held that the right to confrontation was personal to appellant, and thus also the right to cross-examination. Therefore, the state could not constitutionally force appellant to delegate entirely to his lawyer the cross-examination of an adverse witness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child. The statutory provisions which allowed the admission into evidence of videotapes of the testimony of a child sexual assault victim were unconstitutional as they deprived appellant of the right to confront and cross-examine an adverse witness.

 

1338 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


McDonald v. State


Nos. 01-83-0573-CR, 01-83-0447-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


692 S.W.2d 169; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6937



May 23, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause Nos. 381,553 and 330,325


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for engaging in organized criminal activity by the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas) under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.01 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.01 and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02 were constitutional as they reached only those persons who knowingly engaged in criminal activity. The court held that the trial court did not err in overruling appellant's motion in limine and in admitting evidence of other offenses as they were part and parcel of the offense charged. The court held that the indictment did not fail to allege an offense under § 71.01 because it did not contain a requirement that five or more persons committed the burglary. Section 71.01 only required that appellant "commit" the underlying offense and that he did so with intent to establish, maintain, or participate in a combination. The court held that is was not error to deny appellant's motion to quash as the written motion was inadequate and an oral motion expanding upon or raising a different ground from the written motion did not cure the inadequacies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for engaging in organized criminal activity. The statutes under which appellant were convicted were constitutional as they reached only those persons who knowingly engaged in criminal activity. Appellant's motion to quash was properly overruled as the written motion was inadequate and oral argument did not cure the inadequacies.

Keith v. State


No. C14-84-216CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


692 S.W.2d 921; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7106



May 23, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Cause No. 368722.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the 263rd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of involuntary manslaughter in a non-jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for involuntary manslaughter. The deceased was shot as he lay sleeping in his bed. Neighbors found the deceased lying on the sidewalk outside his apartment. During the investigation, the police found a .44 caliber revolver in a case under the mattress in the bedroom of defendant, and the bullet found in the deceased was determined to have come from that gun. The trial court convicted defendant of involuntary manslaughter. On appeal, the court was unable to determine if defendant acted recklessly in his handling of the weapon. A thorough examination of the record led the court to conclude that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction. However, the court concluded that the evidence would be sufficient to support a conviction for a lesser offense, without violating defendant's double jeopardy rights. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to conduct an independent review of all the evidence in the record and determine whether a conviction upon criminally negligent homicide should be entered. The judgment of the trial court was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter because the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction. The court remanded the case to trial court with instructions to conduct an independent review of all the evidence in the record and determine whether a conviction upon criminally negligent homicide should be entered.

MCDONALD v. STATE


No. 01-83-0572-CR.


The First Court of Appeals, Texas


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7168



May 23, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 381,552.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 209th District Court of Harris County (Texas), for engaging in organized criminal activity including automobile theft and burglaries of department stores. Appellant claimed multiple points of error.


OVERVIEW: In disputing his conviction for engaging in organized criminal activity, appellant brought multiple points of error. The court held that evidence of appellant's offenses was properly admitted and that they were not extraneous to the crime of engaging in organized criminal activity. The court held that there was no error in overruling appellant's motion in limine, and no limiting instruction was necessary. The court found that appellant's written motion to quash was inadequate and that an oral motion raising a different ground would not cure it. The court concluded that it was not error to submit the issue of whether one of the members of the combination who helped the police was an accomplice witness as a matter of fact. The court held that the officer was acting within his capacity as an undercover law enforcement agent, and the testimony of the accomplices and agents, combined with the circumstances surrounding appellant's arrest, provided more than sufficient evidence to convict him. The court concluded that testimony regarding hearsay conspiratorial conversations was properly admitted when there was no allegation of conspiracy. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Appellant's offenses were not extraneous to the crime of engaging in organized criminal activity. Testimony of accomplices and agents, combined with the circumstances of appellant's arrest, provided sufficient evidence for conviction.

The court overruled appellant's first point of error. Next, the court held that sufficient evidence supported appellant's conviction on the basis that appellant acted as a party to the transaction for drug delivery. The court overruled appellant's second point of error. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.

O'Connor v. O'Connor


No. 04-84-00039-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


694 S.W.2d 152; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6802



May 22, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 17, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 83-CI-03964 Honorable David Peeples, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of a judgment of the 224th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which partitioned his military retirement benefits, awarding appellee ex-wife 34 percent of all his future military retirement benefits and an arrearage for her share of payments received by him, in a "gap" case decided before the effective date of the Uniformed Services' Former Spouses' Protection Act, 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408.


OVERVIEW: In a partition action, the trial court partitioned appellant ex-husband's military retirement benefits, awarding appellee ex-wife 34 percent of all his future military retirement benefits and an arrearage for her share of payments received by him, in a "gap" case decided before the effective date of the Uniformed Services' Former Spouses' Protection Act (Act), 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellee was entitled to 34 percent of appellant's military retirement benefits, under 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408(c)(1), which reinstated Texas law by allowing such property to be considered community property subject to division upon divorce. The court found that the specific language of the divorce decree that the trial court has no jurisdiction over the military retirement benefits controlled over the general language of an earlier provision listing and awarding him the retirement benefits. Also, the court held that the trial court had jurisdiction over the partition of the benefits under the specific language of § 1408(c)(1) and Texas' interpretation of that language, and that the award of arrearage to appellee was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partition of appellant ex-husband's military retirement benefits to appellee ex-wife, holding that the specific language of the divorce decree that the trial court had no jurisdiction over the retirement benefits controlled over the general language awarding him the retirement benefits, that the trial court had jurisdiction to partition the benefits, and that the award of arrearage to appellee was not unconstitutional.

Daves v. State Bar of Texas


No. 07-85-0049-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


691 S.W.2d 784; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6933



May 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Lubbock County; 237 the Judicial District; No. 84-504,190; Honorable John R. McFall, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the decision of the 237th District Court, Lubbock County, Texas, which held that appellee Texas State Bar had established that appellant engaged in an act of professional misconduct and suspended appellant's license to practice law for six months.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Texas State Bar accused appellant attorney of violating Tex. Code of Prof. Resp. DR 2-101(C)(2) by advertising his services in an area of family law without a disclaimer that he was "Not certified by the Texas Board of Legal Specialization." Appellee took a summary judgment and the lower court adjudged a six-month suspension as the penalty. The judgment was reversed by the court because the penalty was improperly imposed. Although the Texas Supreme Court issued Tex. Code of Prof. Resp. DR 2-101(C)(2) without its prior approval by a majority of appellee's membership, the measure was valid because the Texas constitution of 1876 vested in the supreme court inherent authority to regulate and control the practice of law. The binding effect of that inherent authority precluded discussion of appellant's argument that the disciplinary rule was an unconstitutional infringement on protected commercial speech. While appellee's summary judgment was proper based on the admissions in appellant's pleadings, it was an abuse of discretion to impose the penalty assessed without an evidentiary hearing or consideration of the factors in R. Gov. the St. Bar of Tex., art. X, § 23(B) (1984).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment and six-month suspension against appellant attorney because, while the evidence conclusively established that the advertisement he published was an act of misconduct under the disciplinary rules of appellee Texas State Bar, it was an abuse of discretion to impose the penalty without an evidentiary hearing or consideration of the factors designed to inform disciplinary decisions.

FOX v. STATE


No. B14-84-517-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6689



May 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 338th District Court of Harris County, Texas Cause No. 404,010


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment by the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her for possession of methamphetamine, a controlled substance, and assessed punishment, enhanced by two prior convictions, at 25 years' confinement. Defendant contended that there was insufficient evidence to prove the offense charged and to prove the enhancements, and that the prior convictions were voided by a void amendment to the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of methamphetamine, a controlled substance. The court assessed punishment, enhanced by two prior convictions, at 25 years' confinement. Defendant appealed and presented three grounds of error: insufficient evidence to prove the offense charged, an improper conviction pursuant to a void statute, and insufficient evidence to prove the two enhancement allegations. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence because it found that after viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the verdict, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court further determined that where an amendment to a statute was found unconstitutional, the original statute remained in full force and effect. The court concluded that the language of defendant's indictment was sufficient to state an offense under the original controlled substances act, and that penitentiary records were proof of defendant's prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for possession of methamphetamine because, when viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The amendment to the controlled substances act was unconstitutional but the original statute remained in full force, and penitentiary records were used as proof of prior convictions.

Showery v. State


No. 08-83-00373-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


690 S.W.2d 689; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6612



May 8, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 41st District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC#37172-41)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of a judgment from the 41st District Court of El Paso County (Texas), entered upon a jury verdict, which found him guilty of the murder of a newborn infant in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(1) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician sought review of a conviction under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(1) (1974), for an alleged affirmative act of murder directed against a newborn infant. The state's theory was that appellant performed an abortion by which the fetus was withdrawn alive, and that appellant then caused the death of the newborn by exercising various means of suffocation. Appellant, among other things, challenged the constitutionality of the prosecution due to the incorporation of an overboard definition of "born alive." The court agreed with appellant's contention that the murder statute could not constitutionally apply to a nonviable fetus. However, appellant's criminally challenged conduct occurred after the removal of the fetus. If at that point of extraction the victim exhibited the statutory or comparable signs of life and was alive at the time of his alleged acts, he was susceptible to conviction for murder. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to show that the victim was alive at the time of appellant's alleged conduct. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed. Based upon the evidence of fetal development, the signs of life observed by the eyewitnesses, and the conduct of appellant physician, the jury was justified in concluding that the child was born alive and was alive until such life was intentionally and knowingly taken by the conduct of appellant.

 

1348 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Bean v. State


No. 08-84-00108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


691 S.W.2d 773; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6931



May 8, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal form 171st District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 37,613).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge challenged his conviction for official misconduct in the form of nepotism entered by the 171st District Court of El Paso County (Texas). Appellant contended that the indictment should have been quashed since it failed to negate the proviso contained in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5996a (Supp. 1985), and that it should have been dismissed due to bias of the convening judge in the grand jury proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant judge's conviction for official misconduct in the form of nepotism, he challenged the decision. The court affirmed. First, the court held that appellant's motion to quash the indictment was properly denied because the proviso in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5996a was a defense, not an exception, and therefore did not need to be negated in the state's pleadings. Second, the evidence at trial did not support the defense because the uncle that appellant appointed to represent an indigent defendant was not a public defender, and appellant erroneously interpreted the base point for the two-year computation of the defense. Third, even though the convening judge in the grand jury proceedings testified as a grand jury witness, appellant's due process rights were adequately safeguarded by the ensuing deliberation of the grand jury, the rulings of the trial court and the assessment of the evidence by the trial jury. Moreover, because the stipulated evidence, coupled with the testimony of appellant and his uncle, was tantamount to a confession, the judge's testimony before the grand jury could hardly be said to have deprived appellant of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant judge's conviction for official misconduct in the form of nepotism holding that the statutory proviso was a defense, not an exception, and thus did not need to be negated by the indictment. Appellant was not deprived of due process based on the testimony of the convening judge in the grand jury proceeding because adequate safeguards existed and appellant's testimony was tantamount to a confession.

Taylor v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit rape, burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft, and aggravated rape in the lower court in Montgomery County, (Texas), alleged that the lower court committed reversible errors as to in-court identification of appellant by the victim, insufficiency of the indictment, multiple sentences could not be obtained on separate counts in one indictment, and double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: The victim had been raped by the same man once before, and made a tentative, but not positive photo identification of appellant. Subsequently, she positively identified appellant in a lineup. Once convicted, he sought to challenge the lineup as illegal, but the appellate court held that his face could not be the suppressible fruit of an illegal lineup. Further, because count I of the indictment alleged burglary of a habitation with intent to commit rape while count II of the indictment alleged burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft, appellant could not be sentenced on both counts. Therefore, the court ordered a judgment of acquittal on burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft. As reformed, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The court vacated the burglary with intent to commit theft and aggravated rape convictions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reformed the judgment, acquitting appellant of burglary of a habitation with intent to commit theft because the indictment was duplicitous of the burglary with intent to commit rape, and otherwise affirmed appellant's convictions. On rehearing, the court set aside and vacated the burglary with intent to commit theft and aggravated rape convictions.

 

1350 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Holliman v. State


No. 10-84-052-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


692 S.W.2d 120; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6569



April 25, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 184th Judicial District Court Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 184th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of the offense of delivery of a simulated controlled substance. Appellant sought reversal on grounds that the statute underlying his conviction violated principles of due process and equal protection and that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment convicting appellant of the offense of delivery of a simulated controlled substance proscribed in the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15b. The court rejected appellant's contention that the statute underlying his conviction violated principles of due process and equal protection, that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, and that the indictment was fundamentally defective for failing to state an offense. The court held that art. 4476-15b, § 3 set forth several factors in addition to all other logically relevant factors which a court could consider in determining whether a person had represented a simulated controlled substance to be a controlled substance in a manner that would lead a reasonable person to believe the substance was a controlled substance. These factors were met in appellant's case. The testimony of an officer and a chemist established that the physical appearance of the substance was substantially identical to a controlled substance, marihuana. The Act did not require that the court find proof of all or even one of the factors in order to support a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for the offense of delivery of a simulated controlled substance because there was no constitutional defect in the application of the statute in question to appellant and the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.

Miller v. Providence Memorial Hospital


No. 11-85-013-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


690 S.W.2d 335; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6570



April 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from El Paso County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate sought review of an order from El Paso County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital and doctor on the basis of the two-year statute limitation. Appellant filed suit against appellees, alleging a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant estate filed suit against appellee hospital and doctor alleging a wrongful death action when the decedent died after being sent home upon completion of an emergency room examination. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees on the basis of limitation. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in granting appellees' motion for summary judgment on the basis of limitation. Appellant argued that limitation was tolled because of the discovery rule and fraudulent concealment. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that it was undisputed that the instant lawsuit was filed two years and one week from the date of the medical treatment. There was no proof that decedent's injuries were not immediately discoverable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital and doctor on the basis of limitation. The court found that there was no showing that appellant did not, or reasonably could not, discover the alleged injury within the two-year limitation period.

Retail Merchants Asso. v. Handy Dan Hardware, Inc.


No. 01-84-0798-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


696 S.W.2d 44; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7585



April 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 8, 1985, Reported at: 696 S.W.2d 44 at 54.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 280th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 83-70032.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retail trade association sought review of a judgment from the 280th District Court, Harris County (Texas) which held that the Texas Blue Law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001, violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and refused appellant's application to permanently enjoin appellee chain retailer from violating the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant retail trade association sought to permanently enjoin appellee chain retailer from violating the Texas Blue Law, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 9001, which prohibited the sale of various items on weekends. Appellee launched a constitutional attack. The trial court held in appellee's favor, concluding that art. 9001 violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for entry of a permanent injunction. Finding that appellee had failed to demonstrate the absence of any rational relationship between art. 9001 and its goals, the court held that the statute did not violate the substantive due process or equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or similar provisions of the Texas Constitution. While acknowledging that art. 9001 was not without imperfection, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or indefinite. Concluding that art. 9001 passed due process scrutiny as a valid exercise of the state's police power, the court further held that the statute's private enforcement scheme, as applied to appellee, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Holding that appellee chain retailer's evidence failed to establish the unconstitutionality of Texas' Blue Law, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for entry of an order permanently enjoining appellee from violating the statute.

 

1353 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Herndon Marine Products, Inc. v. San Patricio County Appraisal Review Bd.


No. 13-84-338-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


695 S.W.2d 29; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6573



April 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 343rd District Court of San Particio County, TX.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged decisions of the 343rd District Court of San Particio County (Texas), which denied their motion for summary judgment and granted the motion of appellee tax assessors for summary judgment. The issues were whether appellees' summary judgment proof showed that they had complied with Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 41.47(d) (1982) and whether appellants' constitutional claims barred appellees' summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: After an administrative protest of their property tax assessments, appellant taxpayers sued in the district court. Summary judgment was granted for appellee tax assessors and denied appellants. On appeal, the court described the tax assessment administrative and judicial review procedure. Appellees' summary judgment was granted based upon appellants' alleged failure to comply with Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.06 (1982). The court noted that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 41.47(d) (1982) required the tax appraisal review board to send appellants a notice of its issuance of the order determining the validity of their administrative protest and a copy of the order. Appellees' affidavits in support of its motion for summary judgment merely raised the inference that they had complied with § 41.47(d), so their summary judgment proof was insufficient, as a matter of law, to prove that they were entitled to summary judgment under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.06(a) (1982). Appellants' constitutional claims had no merit, because their legal remedy lay under Tex. Tax Code Ann. chs. 41 and 42 (1982). The court overruled other points of error raised by appellants. The court reversed and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for trial. The tax appraisal review board was required to send a statutory notice to appellant taxpayers of its decision on their administrative protest. Appellee tax assessors' affidavits in support of its motion for summary judgment raised only an inference that notice was sent, so their summary judgment proof was insufficient. Appellants' constitutional claims had no merit, because they had a statutory remedy.

 

1354 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Outlet Co. v. International Sec. Group


No. 04-83-00602-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


693 S.W.2d 621; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6800



April 24, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 12, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 79-CI-10293 Honorable Carolyn Spears, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant television station sought review of an order of the 224th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court (Texas) that entered a jury verdict that found appellant was responsible for libel arising out of a television news broadcast and awarded appellee general, special, and exemplary damages based upon jury findings of falsity and malice.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sued appellant television station for libel arising out of a television news broadcast that alleged that appellee was engaged in a gun smuggling scheme. After a jury trial, appellee was awarded general, special, and exemplary damages. Appellant sought review. The court found an action for libel could be maintained even though appellee made an affirmative waiver of damages for injury to reputation as an element of actual damages because a false statement that charged appellee with a crime was libelous per se and the law presumed it defamed appellee and injured his reputation. The publication could be defamatory to appellee even though it did not directly reference appellee. The court found sufficient evidence to conclude the statements made in appellant's broadcast were not supported by evidence and appellee was entitled to recover actual damages for mental anguish without proof of other injury. The court found sufficient support for the jury finding that the statements were maliciously made. The award of actual and punitive damages was excessive and the court ordered remittitur because appellee's mental anguish was transitory in nature.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that awarded appellee general, special, and exemplary damages was affirmed because an action for libel could be maintained even though appellee made an affirmative waiver of damages for injury to reputation as an element of actual damages because a false statement that charged appellee with a crime was libelous per se and the law presumed it defamed appellee and injured his reputation.

 

1355 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


DANIELS v. STATE


No. 01-84-0583-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7570



April 18, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 405,199


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 248th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that convicted him for burglary of a motor vehicle. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred in conducting his trial in the absence of a waiver of his right to compulsory process and in proceeding in the absence of an effective waiver of this right to trial by jury because he was not aware that the court could not consider his evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for burglary of a motor vehicle. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred when it conducted his trial in the absence of a waiver of his right to compulsory process and when it proceeded in the absence of an effective waiver of his right to trial by jury because he was not aware that the court could not consider his evidence. These grounds for appeal were based upon his reading of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15. Appellant maintained that the statute required that the trial court's judgment be based solely upon appellee's evidence--an unconstitutional end. The court deferred to applicable rules of statutory construction and determined that the text of the statute did not carry the meaning ascribed by appellant. The statute's statement that the trial court's judgment was to be based upon appellee's evidence was a holdover from the old statute. The court in turn determined that there was no requirement that the trial court be limited to consideration of only appellee's evidence in non-jury trials where the plea was not guilty. As the trial court did not in effect misconstrue the statute, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Texas law did not require a trial court to limit its consideration of only appellee's evidence in bench trial of appellant for burglary offense.

 

1356 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Scherlie v. State


No. 01-84-0529-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


689 S.W.2d 294; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7004



April 4, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 768104.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8 of Harris County (Texas), in which he was convicted of driving while intoxicated pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(a) (2)(A), (B) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for driving while intoxicated. Pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(a)(2)(B) (1985), the judge instructed the jury that if they found that appellant had an alcohol concentration of at least 0.10 percent in his body while he drove or operated a motor vehicle in a public place, he was guilty. Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated and sought review. The court held that the definition of intoxication in art. 67011-1(a)(2)(B) of having a blood alcohol content of 0.10 percent or greater did not give rise to a presumption of intoxication, but constituted intoxication standing alone. It was a separate, independent, additional way in which the crime of driving while intoxicated could be committed. The court also held that art. 67011-1(a)(2)(B) did not deprive appellant of due process and did not require a limiting instruction to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated because an alcohol concentration of 0.10 percent constituted intoxication standing alone and was the ultimate fact to be determined in the litigation. It was not an irrebuttable presumption and did not require a limiting instruction to the jury.

Rose v. Rubenstein


No. B14-84-838-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


693 S.W.2d 580; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7565



April 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 308th District Court of Harris County, Texas Cause No. 1,602,559-AA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order of the 308th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied his request to modify child support ordered to be paid for his adult child when appellant was divorced from appellee mother.


OVERVIEW: When appellant father and appellee mother were divorced, appellant was ordered to pay child support for their younger son until that son's eighteenth birthday and for their older, mildly-retarded son past that son's eighteenth birthday. When both sons were past age eighteen, appellant filed a request to modify the support for the older son. The trial court denied the request, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed. The court found that the son still required continuous care and supervision under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 14.05(b) (1975) and that although he had a job, he did not earn sufficient income to be self-supporting. Considering appellant's substantial discretionary income and the son's income from a job that paid slightly more than the minimum wage, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to at least reduce appellant's support payments. Weighing appellee's emotional and financial support of the son, the court found that appellant was not unconstitutionally deprived of equal protection under the law even though the son's age precluded entry of a court-ordered support obligation against appellee.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant father's request to modify child support was affirmed because appellant's mildly-retarded son, although in his twenties, still required continuous care and supervision and did not earn sufficient income to be self-supporting.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court Court at Law No. 2 of Travis County no. 200-811, Honorable Bob Perkins, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 2 of Travis County (Texas), which convicted him for operating a massage establishment without having a valid massage parlor license issued by the sheriff.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for operating a massage establishment without a valid massage parlor license issued by the sheriff. The complaint and information had not alleged that the operation of the massage establishment occurred in an unincorporated area of the county. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372v, § 2 (1985), and Travis County, Tex., Regulations § 3, promulgated pursuant thereto, made the operation of a massage establishment an offense only if the establishment was operated in an unincorporated area. The court reversed the appellant's conviction, and reformed the judgment to show an acquittal, because the state had failed to allege and prove an element of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for operating a massage establishment without a license and reformed the judgment to show that appellant was acquitted. The state failed to allege and prove that appellant operated the establishment in an unincorporated area, an element of the offense.
