Haug v. Franklin


No. 14,273


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


690 S.W.2d 646; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6400



April 3, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 261st Judicial District no. 330,293, Honorable Pete Lowry, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law student challenged an order of the 261st District Court of Travis County (Texas), which entered a take-nothing judgment against him in his suit for injunctive and declaratory relief against appellee university. Appellant alleged that the parking tickets levied against him by appellee violated law school regulations, state and federal due process, and exceeded the statutory powers delegated to the school.


OVERVIEW: Appellant law student accumulated traffic or parking citations issued by appellee university pursuant to Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 51.203 (1972). When he failed to pay the charges, appellee refused to issue his diploma. The trial court issued a take-nothing judgment. The court affirmed. The court held that appellant was not denied due process of law because the regulations provided for a hearing, the private interest at stake was only a few dollars, while appellee had a great interest in controlling traffic on the campus. The court further found that appellant waived any due process claims by requesting and using the privilege of driving and parking on campus under a permit issued by appellee and under the regulations. The court also held that the withholding of his diploma was an authorized sanction where the citations listed that as a possible sanction. The court determined that the charges imposed for violations were within the statutory powers of appellee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing judgment against appellant law student because appellee university's withholding of his diploma as a sanction for unpaid university traffic violations was proper under the regulations and he waived any due process claims by using a university driving permit.

Johnson v. State


No. 04-84-00374-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


693 S.W.2d 559; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6810



March 27, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Court at Law No. 1 of Bexar County Trial Court No. 84-MH 01025 Honorable T. Armour Ball, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, allegedly a mentally ill person, challenged a judgment from County Court at Law No. 1 of Bexar County (Texas), which committed her to a state hospital for observation and treatment for a period not to exceed ninety days, pursuant to the Texas Mental Health Code, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5547-50 (1985). Appellant contended that her due process rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: In disputing the evidence, appellant, allegedly a mentally ill person, challenged the constitutional requirements of due process in the mental health code. The court asserted that a careful reading indicated that the clear and convincing evidence standard, a specific legal term of art, was in the primary paragraph and that the use of the term "likely" was only in subordinate paragraphs. The court found no ambiguity involved in not requiring imminent harm since, as the court pointed out, there were no Texas decisions requiring imminent harm. The jury finding that appellant was dangerous to herself was sufficient to commit her involuntarily, but appellant argued that the trial court applied an overly broad standard of commitment. The court explained that even though the language of an earlier statute was broader than the current one, it incorporated a dangerousness standard that was precise enough to meet due process requirements, and it followed that the current statute was sufficiently narrow to meet due process requirements. The court opined that legislative enactments would not be found unconstitutional and invalid unless it was absolutely necessary. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. Appellant, allegedly a mentally ill person, was not deprived of her due process rights when she was involuntarily committed to a state hospital for observation and treatment.

Commissioners Court of Caldwell County v. Criminal Dist. Attorney


No. 14,253


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


690 S.W.2d 932; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6949



March 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for rehearing overruled April 17, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Caldwell County, 274th Judicial District, no. 17,096, Honorable Paul Huser, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county, its judge, and its commissioners, sought review of an order from the District Court of Caldwell County, 247th Judicial District (Texas), which entered judgment in favor of appellee district attorney requiring appellants to amend or adopt a budget with appropriations for appellee's office under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 332a, § 5 (Supp. 1985) and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 689a-11 (Supp. 1985).


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered appellants, county, its judge, and its commissioners, to amend or adopt a budget with appropriations for appellee district attorney's office. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the legislature intended that the ordinary budget-making process of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 689a-11 (Supp. 1985) be followed in reference to the salaries of appellee's employees. The court held that appellee, not appellant county judge, was to specify amounts to be included in a proposed budget under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 332a, § 5 (Supp. 1985), but appellant commissioners had the power to change those salaries before approving and filing the county's budget.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment in favor of appellee district attorney requiring appellants, county, its judge, and its commissioners, to amend or adopt a budget with appropriations for appellee's office. Appellee, not appellant county judge, was to specify salary amounts of his employees to be included in a proposed budget, but appellant commissioners had the power to change those salaries before approving and filing the county's budget.

DOCKERY v. STATE


NO. A14-84-474CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7420



March 7, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 85th District County of Brazos District Trial Court No. 15,504


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 85th District Court of Brazos County (Texas) convicting him of delivery of a simulated controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of delivery of a simulated controlled substance, sought relief. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court to convict appellant and denied appellant's motion to quash the indictment for failing to describe the simulated substance delivered. Under Tex. Crim. Proc. Code § 21.03 (1966), the state had no duty to show what the delivered substance was other than the controlled substance it purported to be. Appellant had testified that he was selling methamphetamine when the substance was really nasal decongestant. Neither was the state required to prove the substance was chemically different from the purported substance when the jury could conclude the differences logically. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of a mistrial upon admission of appellant's parole status as the issue went to appellant's past crime. Appellant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally vague in its use of the words "reasonable person" was unfounded as the phrase was clarified by examples set forth in the statute. The error in the admission of pen packets containing a void judgment was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant by the trial court because the charging indictment properly set forth the charges against appellant, gave him adequate notice, and was not unconstitutionally vague. The admission of appellant's prior parole sentence was not grounds for a mistrial as it went to the issue of a prior conviction. The error alleged in the admission of pen packets containing a void judgment was not preserved for review.

 

1366 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Ready v. Hughes


NO. 10-84-112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


846 S.W.2d 1; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 12935



March 7, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From 249th Judicial District Court. Johnson County, Texas. Trial Court # 5876-82



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural parents challenged the decision of the 249th Judicial District Court, Johnson County (Texas), which terminated their parental rights and granted adoption to appellee prospective adoptive parents. Appellants contended that appellees lacked standing to file suit under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 11.03, .09.


OVERVIEW: Appellee prospective adoptive parents filed suit against appellant natural parents seeking to terminate appellants' parent-child relationship. The trial court terminated appellants' rights and granted adoption of the child to appellees. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. It found appellees lacked standing to bring the suit because they were not interested parties as defined by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 11.03, .09(a) at the time they filed suit. The court reasoned that because it had been impossible for appellees to show jurisdictional facts when their petition was filed, the only jurisdiction the trial court had had was to dismiss their suit for want of jurisdiction. It further found that the amendment of § 11.09(a) subsequent to the filing of the suit did not give appellees a factual basis for standing to bring the suit where none had existed before. The court also held that appellees' interest in adoption did not give them standing to bring the termination suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which terminated appellant natural parents' parent-child relationship and granted adoption to appellee prospective adoptive parents. The court held that appellees lacked standing to bring suit because they were not interested parties within the definition of the relevant statutes. The court remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to dismiss appellees' suit.

 

1367 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. United States Trust Co.


No. 05-83-00623-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


690 S.W.2d 300; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6865



March 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 18, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a District Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem sought review of the decision of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which rendered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of an estate. On special issue, the jury found that a certificate of trust was delivered as a part payment of a note to the estate and not as a pledge to secure the payment of the note. Appellant contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Almost 100 years earlier, a certificate of a trust was issued. Appellant guardian ad litem contended that title to the certificate was vested in the assignee for the benefit of creditors of the original estate, which had been determined as owner of the certificate by a New York judicial proceeding in 1899. At trial, the trial court submitted the issue of whether the certificate was delivered as part payment of a note to the estate or as a pledge to secure the payment of the note. The jury found that the certificate was partial payment. The court determined that it was not at liberty to substitute its view for that of the jury, unless the evidence was so against the great weight and preponderance as to be manifestly unjust. The court found that, although weak, there was more than a scintilla of evidence from which the jury could have concluded that it was a partial payment. The New York judicial proceeding did not collaterally estop appellee trust company from contesting that the certificate was not a partial payment because the issues were not identical and there was no final judgment. The court found that a broad jury instruction did not cause rendition of an improper verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the estate of the original owners of the certificate as against appellant guardian ad litem, who represented those who asserted interests in the certificate as creditors of the original estate. The court found that there was more than a scintilla of evidence from which the jury could have concluded that the certificate was delivered to the estate as a partial payment of a note to the estate.

 

1368 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Forte v. State


No. 2-84-012-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


686 S.W.2d 744; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6246



February 21, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 5 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of County Criminal Court No. 5 of Tarrant County, Texas, which convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of driving while intoxicated. Defendant appealed his conviction on the ground that he was improperly denied a right to counsel prior to making a decision as to whether to take an intoxilyzer examination. The court reversed, holding that defendant had a right to counsel prior to making a decision regarding whether to submit to the chemical test referred to in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 6701L-1, 5. The court found the decision of whether to submit to the test was a critical pretrial stage because defendant had been taken into custody, informed of his constitutional rights, and informed that his operator's license could be suspended if he refused to take the test. Under those circumstances, counsel's absence might have derogated defendant's right to a fair trial. The court, cognizant that the passage of time would skew the test results, held that a person required to submit to a chemical test of the alcohol content of his blood, breath, or urine would have the right to consult with a lawyer of his choosing before making that decision, provided that such consultation did not unreasonably delay the administration of the test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated, holding that the decision of whether to take a chemical test was a critical pretrial stage to which defendant had the right to counsel before making any decision.

Fitts v. Beaumont

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person appealed grant of summary judgment entered by a trial court (Texas) in favor of defendant City of Beaumont, Texas, dismissing plaintiff's civil action for failure to file a notice of claim within 60 days after her injury occurred.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured person was injured as a result of a fall she alleged was the result of a hole in the roadway which constituted a dangerous condition. Defendant City of Beaumont moved for summary judgment because plaintiff had not filed a notice of claim within 60 days after her injury allegedly occurred. Plaintiff appealed, contending the 60-day period for filing claims contained in the city charter was not reasonable and just. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the 60-day period for filing notice of claims in the city charter was not logical and reasonable and that the court should hear the case. The court remanded for the trial court to hear the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of summary judgment in favor of defendant City of Beaumont and remanded the case because the 60-day period for filing notice of claim of personal injury contained in the city charter was not logical and reasonable.

 

1370 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Lampson v. Beaumont


No. 09-84-324 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


687 S.W.2d 788; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6429



February 21, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxing agencies sought review of an order of the trial court (Texas), which, after appellee city filed a declaratory judgment action, determined that the "tax increment base" for the reinvestment zone under the Texas Tax Increment Financing Act of 1981, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1066e (1985), was to be figured on the total appraised value of all taxable real property for 1982.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city filed a declaratory judgment action against appellant taxing agencies seeking judicial determination as to whether, under the Texas Tax Increment Financing Act of 1981, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1066e (1985) (Act), the "tax increment base" for the reinvestment zone was to be figured on the total appraised value of all taxable real property for the year 1982 or for the year 1983. The trial court declared that 1982 values were to be used. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly determined that 1982 values were to be used. The court found it "glaringly clear" that the legislature mandated that the ordinance designating a reinvestment zone would necessarily be adopted in a year prior to the zone taking effect and noted that the original Act directed cities to commence collecting taxes with the first levy after the zone took effect, which was an acknowledgement of a difference between the year of designation and the year a zone took effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that under the Texas Tax Increment Financing Act of 1981 the "tax increment base" for the reinvestment zone meant the total appraised value of all taxable real property for the year 1982.

Harper v. State

686 S.W.2d 738; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6451



February 20, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 83-184-K, HONORABLE WILLIAM S. LOTT, JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the 26th Judicial District Court of Williamson County (Texas) for involuntary manslaughter in violation of Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 19.02(a)(2) and his enhancement for previous convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of involuntary manslaughter in violation of Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(2) (1974) and entered a plea of true to enhancements alleging two previous felony convictions for driving while intoxicated. The jury assessed punishment at imprisonment for life under Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1985). Defendant contended on appeal that he did not recklessly disregard the safety of another and that the blood test results at the hospital were barred by the physician-patient privilege. Affirming the conviction, the court held that an exception to the physician-patient privilege had gone into effect for blood-alcohol test results and that defendant had recklessly disregarded the safety of others by driving while intoxicated, knowing of the risk that he could have caused the death of another by doing so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because the physician-patient privilege did not apply to the blood-alcohol test results and because defendant's driving under the influence was in reckless disregard of the fact that he might cause the death of another.

Kelly v. State


No. 3-84-038-CR(T)


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


686 S.W.2d 742; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6452



February 20, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, 194TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. F-81-30376-HM, HONORABLE ED KINKEADE, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment by the 194th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to confinement for his guilty plea to the charge of burglary of a building, which was entered before the magistrate's court of Dallas County. Defendant contended that his conviction, heard by the magistrate, was void, and therefore, the subsequent revocation was also void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to burglary of a building, a second degree felony, before the magistrate's court. The plea was accepted, and the punishment was set at four years' confinement, probated. Defendant made no complaint at that time about being brought before the magistrate rather than the district court. Thereafter, the state petitioned to revoke defendant's probation, and the motion was granted after a hearing before the district court. Defendant appealed the revocation of his probation on the ground that his initial conviction was void, therefore, the subsequent revocation was void. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's revocation of probation because his initial conviction was valid, pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1918c, which provided for the appointment of magistrates in Dallas County by the district judges of that county, to perform the functions authorized by the act, and the district court could refer to the magistrate any criminal case. Such referral was proper pursuant to Tex. Const. Ann. art. V, § 1, where the legislature could establish such other courts as it deemed necessary and prescribe the jurisdiction and organization thereof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of defendant's probation and sentenced him to confinement for his guilty plea to burglary of a building because his plea before a magistrate was authorized pursuant to that was authorized to create and organize courts as deemed necessary. Because his initial conviction was valid, there was no remaining point on appeal and revocation of probation was affirmed.

No. 14,215


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin

February 20, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the District Court of Travis County, 250TH Judicial District No. 350,669, Honorable Harley Clark, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, supplier and others, appealed the decision of the 250th District Court, Travis County, Texas, which affirmed the decision of appellee Public Utility Commission of Texas that found in favor of a public utility. Appellants claimed that appellee erred under the Public Utility Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, §§ 38, 45, 47 (1985), when it denied an amendment of the public utility's tariffs and business policies.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, supplier and others, filed a complaint with appellee Public Utility Commission of Texas against a public utility. Appellant charged that the combined effects of the utility's tariff charges and certain of its business policies were discriminatory and anticompetitive, and requested that appellee amend the utility's tariffs and business policies, as necessary, to prevent the violations alleged. Appellee denied appellant's relief, and sued for judicial review. While the court was dissatisfied with the commission's findings, it was required to review the order solely on the grounds invoked by the agency and affirmed appellee's order. The court affirmed that appellants did not suffer unlawful or unreasonable discrimination or competitive disadvantage under the Public Utility Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, §§ 38, 45, 47 (1985). The court found that appellee's final order was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellee Public Utility Commission of Texas's order because the grounds for its decision were based on substantial evidence. The court affirmed the denial of a change in a public utility's tariffs and business polices to appellants, supplier and others, because the tariffs and policies were not illegally or unreasonably discriminatory or disadvantageous.

Leonard v. State


No. 01-84-0238-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


685 S.W.2d 786; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6193



February 14, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 7 of Harris County Trial Court Cause No. 704,439


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the County Criminal Court At Law No. 7 of Harris County (Texas), finding appellant guilty of evading arrest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for evading arrest. After posting bond, he failed to appear on his court date and was eventually rearrested and tried almost one year after the original arrest date. At trial, appellant brought a motion to dismiss, contending that the state failed to comply with the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.02 (Supp. 1984). The trial court denied the motion and, following his sentencing, appellant sought review of his conviction, contending that the trial court erred in overruling the motion to dismiss the information. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, finding that the trial court properly excluded the period during which appellant's location was unknown and he was attempting to avoid apprehension or prosecution from calculations of the pertinent time under the Speedy Trial Act. The court held that the state, therefore, was not required to show diligence or establish an exception to the Speedy Trial Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding appellant guilty of evading arrest because the evidence was clear that appellant was avoiding apprehension, and thus the trial court properly excluded the period during which appellant avoided capture from the time limit of the Speedy Trial Act. The court held that the state was not required to show diligence or establish an exception to the Speedy Trial Act.

DOBBS v. STATE


NO. C14-83-588-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7036



February 7, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 357,607


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for delivery of cocaine and sentence from the 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the indictment drafted under unconstitutional amendments to the Controlled Substances Act.


OVERVIEW: Upon a jury verdict, the trial court convicted appellant of the offense of delivery of cocaine, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03, and assessed punishment of imprisonment. Appellant sought review, challenging the validity of his indictment and the statute under which he was convicted. The court rejected appellant's arguments and affirmed the decision based on its holding that the trial court did not err in overruling appellant's motion to quash the indictment. Although amendments to the Controlled Substances Act were held to be constitutionally infirm and ineffectual, the prior law remained in effect. Therefore, appellant's indictment that was drafted under the amendments was not subject to a motion to quash because it alleged the offense of delivery of cocaine under the pre-amendment statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence, holding that the trial court did not err in overruling appellant's motion to quash the indictment that was drafted under amendments to the Controlled Substances Act which were held to be unconstitutional and ineffectual because the indictment alleged an offense, delivery of cocaine, under the prior law that remained in effect.

CRUZ VIERA v. STATE


NO. C14-84-201-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 7037



February 7, 1985 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 248th District Court of Harris County Cause No. 397,788


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by jury in the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, cocaine, under the Controlled Substance Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03 and contended that the 1981 amendments to the statute were unconstitutional and that the trial court erred when it admitted certain reputation evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, cocaine, under the Controlled Substance Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 4.03. He challenged the constitutionality of the 1981 amendments to the Act and the admission of certain reputation evidence. The court affirmed the conviction. The indictment alleged an offense under the pre-1981 act; therefore, there was no error. The court also overruled appellant's contention that the evidence of appellant's reputation in the community was improper. Such testimony was admissible even if it was partially based upon discussion concerning the primary offense. There was no showing that it was based exclusively upon the primary offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, cocaine, under the Controlled Substance Act because appellant was indicted under the pre-1981 Act. Thus, his challenge to the 1981 amendments was overruled. Testimony regarding his reputation in the community was proper because there was no showing that it was based entirely upon the primary offense.

Ex parte Seymour


No. 09-84-383 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


688 S.W.2d 139; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6431



January 31, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator father filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus in which he claimed that he was illegally confined in jail. The district court found relator in contempt for failing to make child support payments and placed him on probation for five years. Relator's ex-wife filed a sworn motion to revoke his probation for noncompliance with the probation order. The district court issued a warrant for his arrest and relator was incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: Relator father was required to make periodic child support payments. The district court found relator in contempt for failing to make the child support payments that were previously ordered and placed him on probation for five years. Relator's ex-wife filed a sworn motion alleging non-compliance with the probation order and sought revocation of probation. The district court ordered a warrant issued for relator's arrest. Relator was arrested and incarcerated in jail. Relator had been in jail for eight days when he filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus. The court issued the writ and held that relator had been illegally confined. The court ordered his discharge and release from any bond liability. The court concluded that relator was not promptly brought before the district court as required by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 14.12(d). The court ruled that a reasonable definition of "promptly" was 72 hours from the time an arrested probationer arrived in the county jail of the court causing the arrest, excluding weekends and holiday periods. The hearing required by § 14.12(d) did not have to occur within 72 hours, but a court appearance must have been held within that time period.


OUTCOME: The court held that relator father was not promptly brought before the trial court causing his arrest as required by statute. The court held that an arrested probationer should be brought before the trial court within 72 hours of his arrest. The court concluded that relator was illegally confined and was entitled to habeas corpus relief. The court ordered relator's discharge from confinement and release from any liability on his bond.

Russell v. State


Appeal No. 04-83-00499-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


685 S.W.2d 413; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6538



January 30, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 175th District Court of Bexar County

Trial Court No. 83-CR-827 Honorable Phil Chavarria, Jr., Judge Presiding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 175th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which revoked his probation for violation of a condition. Appellant asserted that he was denied due process, that the probation condition was invalid, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove the violation by a preponderance of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of aggravated promotion of prostitution and was placed on probation with conditions. The probation was revoked and sentence was imposed after the trial court found that appellant had violated a condition of his probation. Appellant sought review asserting that he was denied due process, that the probation condition was vague and indefinite and therefore invalid, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove the violation by a preponderance of the evidence. On review, the court examined the condition and the deferred adjudication of guilt. The court found that a condition regarding the promotion of prostitution was not vague and that sufficient notice of the type of conduct prohibited was given. The court next found that appellant was shown to have violated the condition by a preponderance of the evidence. Other procedural and substantive arguments were overruled as well. The decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The revocation of probation for violation of condition of probation was affirmed because probationary conditions were not limited statutorily, reasonable conditions of probation were within the discretion of the trial court, and there was no denial of due process. Also, the probation condition was not vague where sufficient notice of the type of conduct prohibited was given and sufficient evidence was presented of the violation.

Jones v. State


Nos. 01-83-713-CR, 01-83-714-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


684 S.W.2d 223; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6068



January 17, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 185th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Numbers 359,685 and 359,686.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pharmacist sought review of a judgment of the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, that convicted him of violating the Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pharmacist, while working, sold large amounts of controlled substances at excessive prices to an undercover investigator. Appellant was convicted of violating the Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, and he appealed. The court affirmed. Appellant contended that he was not a practitioner as that term was defined under the Act at Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 1.02(24)(A). The court disagreed and held that a pharmacist fell within the definition of "practitioner" because a pharmacist clearly was someone licensed to distribute or dispense a controlled substance. The court also found no merit to appellant's argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague. Appellant further argued that the state did not prove he dispensed the substances, as alleged in the indictment, but that he merely delivered them. Evidence establishing an unlawful delivery did not fatally differ from an indictment alleging unlawful dispensing.


OUTCOME: Appellant pharmacist's conviction for violating the Controlled Substances Act (Act) was affirmed. Appellant, as a pharmacist, was a practitioner under the Act because he was someone licensed to distribute or dispense a controlled substance. Evidence that appellant delivered a controlled substance was sufficient to show that a controlled substance was dispensed.

Hoffart v. State


No. B14-84-361-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


686 S.W.2d 259; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6095



January 17, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 10 of Harris County Cause No. 753,985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pro-life activist appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court At Law No. 10 of Harris County (Texas) which convicted him of criminal trespass. After defendant pled not guilty, the jury found him guilty and assessed his punishment at 30 days in jail, probated for six months, and a fine of $ 500.00.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pro-life activist was arrested after he entered an abortion clinic, which he was picketing. After the trial court convicted appellant of criminal trespass, appellant challenged the conviction. In affirming, the court held that the trial court did not err when it denied appellant's pre-trial motion to compel the abortion clinic to produce names, addresses, and telephone numbers of all females who were in the waiting room when appellant entered because their testimony was irrelevant. Moreover, the court found that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's requested jury instruction on the defense of free speech because such a charge mistakenly suggested that the jury should have interpreted the law. Finally, the trial court did not prohibit appellant's right to free speech when it required, as a condition of probation, that appellant not enter upon the premises of any establishment of which he was picketing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant pro-life activist of criminal trespass because the trial court did not err in denying appellant's pre-trial motion to compel the names of certain witnesses or in excluding certain medical evidence because neither the witnesses' testimony nor the medical evidence was relevant to the criminal trespass charge.

 

1384 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Massachusetts Indem. & Life Ins. Co. v. Texas State Bd. of Ins.


No. 14,153


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


685 S.W.2d 104; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6231



January 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 351,774, HONORABLE PETE LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant life insurance company sought review of a judgment of the 147th District Court, Travis County, Texas, which rendered judgment for appellee insurance board and its commissioner in appellant's claim alleging that the Texas Agents Qualification and License Law for Agents of Legal Reserve Life Insurance Companies, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.07-1, § 10 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant life insurance company filed a claim against appellee insurance board and its commissioner, challenging the constitutionality of the Texas Agents Qualification and License Law for Agents of Legal Reserve Life Insurance Companies, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.07-1, § 10. Appellant contends that the statute, which dealt with the licensing of temporary life insurance agents, violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States and Texas Constitutions. The trial court denied appellant's claim, finding the statute constitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was not unduly vague and bore a rational relationship to legitimate state interests. The statute's limit as to the temporary licenses issued each year, the provision forbidding licensees from selling or soliciting policies in replacement of existing policies held by prospective purchasers, and the statute's classifications based on full and part-time agents furthered the legitimate state interest in assuring the competence and training of agents while simultaneously protecting the public from the ill effect of licensees' lack of training and competence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that the life insurance licensing statute was constitutional because the statute furthered the legitimate state interest in assuring the competence and training of agents while simultaneously protecting the public from the ill effects of licensees' lack of training and competence.

 

1385 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Saldana v. State


Appeal No. 04-82-00262-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


685 S.W.2d 399; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6531



January 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 289th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 80-SF-0102 Honorable Tom Rickhoff, Judge Presiding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, surety on a bail bond, challenged a decision from the 289th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court (Texas), which allowed only a 50 percent remittitur of the amount of the bond after the principal was returned to custody.


OVERVIEW: After the principal failed to appear in court, a bail bond was declared forfeited and a judgment nisi was signed. The principal was rearrested, and a summary judgment on the bond was rendered against appellant, surety on the bail bond. The trial court granted appellant a 50 percent remittitur of the bond. At the time of the judgment nisi, the applicable statute limited the amount of remittitur to 50 percent of the amount of the bond. Appellant argued on appeal that, because he procured the return of the principal within two years of the judgment nisi and after the effective date of the amendment mandating a remittitur of 95 percent, the trial court erred in limiting the remittitur to 50 percent. The reviewing court previously held that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3 § 13(b), which required a 95 percent remittitur, was unconstitutional. As appellant's claim was based solely on the provisions of an unconstitutional legislative act, it was rejected and there was no need to consider whether the enacted 1981 amendment was applicable to a declaration of forfeiture and a judgment nisi entered prior to the effective date of such amendment. The trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court held that the statute that appellant, surety on a bail bond, relied upon to support his argument that he was entitled to a 95 percent remittitur on a bail bond was unconstitutional. Therefore, appellant's claim was rejected and the judgment from the trial court granted appellant 50 percent remittitur on the bond was affirmed.

Malone & Hyde, Inc. v. Hobrecht


Appeal No. 04-83-00086-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


685 S.W.2d 739; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6533



January 16, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeals from the 45th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 81-CI-10367 Honorable Carol Haberman, Judge Presiding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pharmacy appealed the judgment of the 45th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court (Texas), which awarded damages to plaintiff estate, plaintiff wife, and plaintiff adult children for a pharmacist's mistake in filling a prescription for insulin syringes, which resulted in death from overdose. In a separate appeal, plaintiff wife appealed the trial court's disregard of the jury's award for loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: Decedent suffered an insulin overdose, which caused his death. Plaintiff estate, plaintiff wife, and plaintiff adult children filed a wrongful death and survivor action against defendant pharmacy, which had mistakenly filled decedent's prescription for insulin syringes with non-insulin syringes, causing the overdose. At trial, the jury returned a verdict that awarded damages to all plaintiffs. The trial court disregarded the jury's answer that awarded damages to plaintiff wife for loss of consortium following her husband's death. On appeal, the court upheld the award of damages for pain and suffering and pecuniary loss with respect to plaintiff wife and two of plaintiff adult children. The court reversed the pecuniary loss claim of the third adult child. The court found that the trial court correctly refused to order remittitur or otherwise limit recovery. However, the court found the amount awarded for loss of consortium prior to death was excessive. On plaintiff wife's separate appeal, the court reinstated the jury award for loss of consortium after death.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the award of damages to one of the three plaintiff adult children, severed that claim, and remanded it for a new trial. The court also remanded for remittitur the award to plaintiff wife for loss of consortium prior to her husband's death. On plaintiff wife's separate appeal, the court reinstated the jury's award for loss of consortium after the death of her husband.

 

1387 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Palmer v. State


No. 05-84-00557-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


686 S.W.2d 645; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6341



January 14, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of burglary of a habitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for burglary of a habitation. Defendant's first contention was that because the indictment failed to set out how consent in the cause was ineffective, it was fundamentally defective. The court held that it was well-settled that when an indictment alleged "without effective consent," the defendant was given sufficient notice that consent was lacking for any of the reasons set out in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 1.07(12). The court reiterated the rule that an indictment need not plead evidence relied on by the state, only the facts essential to give notice. Hence, the reviewing court found no merit to defendant's point of error, and overruled it. Next, defendant argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. The court held that a statute was vested with a presumption of validity, and that the presumption remained until the contrary was shown beyond a reasonable doubt. The presumption of validity was not overcome. Defendant's second point of error was also overruled, and his conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for burglary of a habitation was affirmed, as both his points of error were overruled. The indictment was not fundamentally defective because defendant was given sufficient notice that consent was lacking for any reasons set out in the applicable statute. Furthermore, the presumption of validity for the statute in question had not been overcome.

 

1388 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Baum v. State


Nos. B14-84-583CR, B14-84-584CR, B14-84-585CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


686 S.W.2d 258; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6048



January 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 180th District Court of Harris County Cause Nos. 409,174, 409,175, and 409,176.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged orders of the 180th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied his applications for writs of habeas corpus in three causes of action for which he was charged each with the offense of theft of receiving stolen property, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was accused in three indictments for the offense of theft by receiving under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(c)(3). Prior to trial, appellant filed applications for writs of habeas corpus in each cause; the trial court denied all applications. Appellant challenged those denials, arguing that § 31.03(c)(3) created a mandatory presumption that was unconstitutional; the provision at issue stated that a person in the business of buying or selling secondhand property was presumptively guilty of theft by receiving if he possessed stolen property valued at 25 dollars or more and failed to have proper records concerning it. The court found that the elements of the offense of theft by receiving stolen property had been correctly alleged in the indictment. Furthermore, whether or not the presumption was applied and how it was applied were fact questions that could only be decided at trial. The presumption had nothing to do with the indictments by which appellant was charged; thus, constitutionality of the presumption was prematurely before the court. The court also found that § 31.03(c)(3) was not unconstitutionally vague or ambiguous. The orders below were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Denial of applications for writs of habeas corpus in three causes of action charging appellant with the offense of theft of receiving stolen property was affirmed, as a presumption created by the applicable statute had nothing to do with the indictments by which appellant was charged, and the issue of its constitutionality was thus prematurely before the court. Moreover, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or ambiguous.

Preston Tower Condominium Asso. v. S.B. Realty, Inc.


No. 05-83-01243-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


685 S.W.2d 98; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6251



January 9, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM A DISTRICT COURT OF DALLAS COUNTY, TEXAS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condominium association sought review of the judgment of a District Court of Dallas County (Texas), granting summary judgment to appellee leasing family on the ground that appellant's age restriction was illegal and unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant condominium association filed suit seeking a permanent injunction enjoining appellees, a family who leased a condominium, from violating an age restriction contained in the bylaws, which prevented those under 16 from living in the complex. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees on the ground that the age restriction was illegal. The court reversed and remanded, finding that the age restriction was permissible because it was a reasonable means of achieving legitimate goals, and exceptions to the restriction were a reasonable way to do so without undue hardship and required that reasonable criteria be used. Further, the court found that appellees had notice of the restriction. The court also concluded that there were genuine questions of fact as to whether the application of the restriction against appellees was discriminatory, arbitrary, or oppressive where there was conflicting and inconclusive evidence and as to whether appellees' claims of waiver, estoppel, and laches had merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's grant of summary disposition because questions of fact existed as to whether the age restriction was discriminatorily or arbitrarily applied and whether laches, estoppel, or waiver barred suit.

 

1390 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Pollard v. State


No. 05-83-01161-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


687 S.W.2d 373; 1985 Tex. App. LEXIS 6347



January 2, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 13, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: From a County Court of Dallas County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him in a trial de novo on his plea of guilty to a charge of sleeping and dozing in a public place in violation of Dallas, Tex., Rev. Code of Civ. and Crim. Ordinances § 31-13 (1960).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury in a trial de novo to a charge of sleeping and dozing in a public place in violation of Dallas, Tex., Rev. Code of Civ. and Crim. Ordinances § 31-13 (1960). Appellant challenged the conviction, contending that the complaint should have been quashed for failure to allege a culpable mental state, and that such defect rendered the complaint fundamentally defective. The court noted that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.02(b) (1974) supplied a required mental state by providing that unless the definition of the offense plainly dispensed with any mental element, a culpable mental state was required. As the definition of sleeping in public did not plainly dispense with any culpable mental state by not mentioning any mental state at all, § 6.02(b) consequently applied, and added the requirement of culpable mental state to the definition of the offense. Because a culpable mental state was thus an element of the offense of sleeping in public, the failure of the complaint to allege that element rendered it fundamentally defective. The complaint was therefore void, the judgment was reversed, and the complaint was ordered dismissed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for sleeping and dozing in a public place, in violation of a local ordinance, was reversed. The court found that a culpable mental state was an element of the charged offense under a penal statute, which had not been alleged in the complaint against appellant. As such, the complaint was thus void, and it was ordered dismissed.

 

1391 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


Melendez v. Beal


No. 01-84-00379-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


683 S.W.2d 869; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6848



December 27, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 24, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 165th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 82-41032.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the summary judgment entered by the 165th District Court of Harris County (Texas) in favor of appellee hospital and nurses in a medical malpractice case. Appellant argued the court erred in ruling that her claim was barred by the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01, because she did not discover the claim until one year before filing suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a medical malpractice action against appellee hospital, doctor, and nurses after discovering that a sponge was left inside her abdominal area during a surgery performed 13 years earlier. Appellees filed motions for summary judgment, which the trial court granted based on the two-year statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01. Appellant argued that the court erred in ruling that her claim was barred by the Act, because she did not discover the claim until one year before filing suit. The appeals court reversed and remanded. The court reasoned that appellant had no way of discovering the negligent act within two years from the date of the medical treatment because she was asymptomatic for 13 years. Thus, the limitation was unreasonable when applied to appellant because it denied her a cause of action before she knew she was injured. The court established the rule that in situations where there was no showing that the patient knew or could have known of the negligent treatment, the limitation should not be applied. The filing of suit within two years of discovery was timely.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed and remanded the summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital, doctor and nurses in appellant's medical malpractice case. The court ruled that the limitations provision was unreasonable when applied to appellant because it denied her a cause of action before she knew, or could have known, she was injured.

Reed v. Campbell


No. 08-83-00022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


682 S.W.2d 697; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6839



December 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 83rd District Court of Reagan County, Texas. (TC# 2567)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant illegitimate child challenged an order of the 83rd District Court of Reagan County (Texas), which entered a take-nothing judgment against her in her suit against appellee administratrix to establish a share in the estate of her natural father because she did not meet the requirements of Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 42(b) (1979).


OVERVIEW: Appellant illegitimate child was born to her natural father and mother, who were never married, and appellant was subsequently adopted by another man. After her natural father's death, appellant filed an action against appellee administratrix to establish a share in the estate of her natural father. The trial court entered a take-nothing judgment against her, and appellant challenged the judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 42(b) (1979) provided the only means by which illegitimate children could share in their natural fathers' estates. The court found that appellant did not meet the requirements that she was born or conceived before or during the marriage of her mother and natural father; that she was legitimized, or that her natural father executed a statement of paternity. The court found that such denial did not violate appellant's equal protection rights because the state had a rational basis for the legislation. The court found that the evidence supported the finding that appellant's mother and natural father were never married.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, finding that appellant illegitimate child was not entitled to share in her natural father's estate because the requirements set forth in the Probate Code for illegitimate children to inherit from their fathers had not been met. The court found that such exclusion did not violate appellant's rights to equal protection because the state had a rational basis for the legislation.

Brooks v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


682 S.W.2d 437; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6824

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 176th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Case No. 353,285.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment by the 176th District Court of Harris County, Texas, which revoked his probation for the offense of aggravated robbery after he was placed on shock probation when he violated the conditions of his probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty of robbery and was placed on shock probation after he served 91 days of confinement. After he violated terms of his probation it was revoked and he appealed. Appellant alleged that his conviction should have been reversed because the indictment was fundamentally defective, in that it failed to describe the property he intended to steal. The court affirmed finding that robbery was an assaultive offense rather than an offense against property, and therefore the property he intended to steal did not have to be described.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's probation after he violated the conditions of probation for his conviction for robbery because robbery was an assaultive offense not an offense against property. The indictment was valid, as the property he intended to steal need not have been described in the indictment.

Pinkston v. State

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 43rd District Court of Parker County.

The court found sufficient evidence to support the enhancement of appellant's sentence based on his prior felony convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance, holding that the evidence was sufficient to connect him to the manufacture of the controlled substance even though the title to the property was in his wife's name. The court held that there was probable cause to issue the search warrant based on the totality of the circumstances.

GAINES v. STATE


NO. 01-84-0070-CR.

1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4799

NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 263rd District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 393,357


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for robbery by the 263rd District Court of Harris County(Texas) on grounds of alleged Speedy Trial Act violations, improper argument, and improper jury charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of aggravated robbery after robbing a bank using a gun. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment for violation of the Speedy Trial Act. The court concluded that the time that elapsed due to continuances requested by appellant's counsel did not count toward the time limit, and as a result, appellant's trial took place within the time permitted. NORTON v. STATE


No. 01-83-00749-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4804



December 6, 1984 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 212th District Court of Galveston County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 39,690


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the 212th District Court of Galveston County (Texas) finding defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, namely, phenylacetone and methylamine, with intent to manufacture methamphetamine and assessing defendant's punishment at seven years' confinement, in accordance with a plea bargain agreement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of possession of a controlled substance, namely, phenylacetone and methylamine, with intent to manufacture methamphetamine. After finding defendant guilty, the trial judge assessed punishment at seven years confinement, in accordance with the plea bargain agreement. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction because defendant waived his motions for severance, discovery, and suppression prior to entering his plea by failing to present them to the trial judge for a ruling. The court stated that defendant's motions were never presented to the trial court, but were apparently abandoned. The court also stated that it was true that the trial judge, in giving the admonishment required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(a)(3) (1984), did tell defendant that he could have appealed for motions previously filed. However, the mere filing of a motion was insufficient to raise a matter on appeal, unless the motion was ruled upon. The court noted that the judge's incorrect admonishment and the defense attorney's silent acquiescence deprived defendant of the correct information he needed to make an informed choice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of possession of a controlled substance, namely, phenylacetone and methylamine, with intent to manufacture methamphetamine because defendant waived his motions for severance, discovery, and suppression prior to entering his plea by failing to present them to the trial judge for a ruling, and the mere filing of a motion was insufficient to raise a matter on appeal, unless the motion was ruled upon.

Ex parte Mattox


No. 3-84-201-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


683 S.W.2d 93; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6900



December 5, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 74,873, HONORABLE MACE B. THURMAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governmental lawyer challenged an order from the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas) that denied appellant's pretrial petition for writ of habeas corpus in which appellant contended that he was unlawfully restrained pursuant to indictments that alleged commercial bribery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(3) (1974).


OVERVIEW: Appellant governmental lawyer solicited an attorney representing a private corporation to breach the attorney's fiduciary duty to that attorney's client. Appellant was indicted for commercial bribery under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(3) (1974). The denial of appellant's pretrial petition for habeas corpus relief was affirmed because, as a general rule, when there was a valid penal statute under which a prosecution could be brought, habeas corpus was not available to test the sufficiency of the charging instrument prior to trial. Further, appellant's claim was not within the narrow exception to that rule which permitted pretrial habeas corpus to challenge the legal authority of state to prosecute. The court rejected claims that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(c), and the definitions of fiduciary and beneficiary contained in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 32.43(a) were unconstitutionally vague because it must be proved that appellant acted with the requisite culpable mental state, which mitigated any vagueness especially when the statute provided adequate notice of the proscribed conduct. Also, the reasonableness requirement within the definition of benefit narrowed the scope of § 32.43(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied appellant governmental lawyer's pretrial petition for habeas corpus relief because a habeas corpus proceeding could not be used to challenge the sufficiency of the charging instrument before trial. Also, the statute that criminalized commercial bribery was not vague because its required proof of scienter and provided adequate notice that the conduct was proscribed.

 

1398 of 1887 DOCUMENTS


PADGETT v. STATE


Appeal No. 04-82-00026-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6960



November 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 226th District Court of Bexar County Trial Court No. 80-CR-3371 Honorable Ted Butler, Judge Presiding


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 226th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated kidnapping after finding that he had terrorized his victim.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of aggravated kidnapping. The court overruled a motion for rehearing on appeal. The court reasoned that although the kidnapping statutes did not define the term terrorize, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 2207(1)(2) (1974) categorized a threat to commit any offense that involved violence with the intent to place any person in fear of imminent serious bodily injury as a terroristic threat. The court also concluded that § 2207(1)(2) afforded ample support for the finding that appellant's threat to kill his victim if she attempted to escape constituted a threat to use deadly force that reasonably created a feeling of terror in her mind.


OUTCOME: The court overruled a motion for rehearing as to appellant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping. The court held that a statute that categorized a threat to commit a violent offense with the intent to create fear of imminent serious bodily injury as a terroristic threat adequately supported a finding that appellant's threat to kill his victim if she tried to escape was a threat of deadly force that reasonably created a feeling of terror.

HENDERSON v. STATE


No. 01-84-0079-CR.


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 4766



November 21, 1984 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 374,649.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 228 Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), which revoked appellant's probation, adjudicated appellant's guilt for possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, and sentenced him to 10 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered a guilty plea to possession of a controlled substance. The trial court deferred adjudication and placed appellant on probation. Subsequently, the court revoked probation, adjudicated appellant guilty, and sentenced appellant to 10 years confinement. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 3d(b) was constitutional despite giving trial courts absolute discretion to revoke probation and adjudicate guilt, that appellant's constitutional right to due process was satisfied when the trial court heard evidence substantiating his guilt before deferring the proceedings without an adjudication, that there was no constitutional right to appeal in criminal cases, as that right was purely statutory, and that there was no appellate review of adjudication of guilt under art. 42.12 or the sufficiency of evidence supporting the adjudication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment of the trial court, because the trial court had absolute discretion to revoke appellant's probation and adjudicate his guilt for possession of a controlled substance, and the appellate court had no jurisdiction to review the adjudication.

Webster v. Signad, Inc.


No. 01-84-0354-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


682 S.W.2d 644; 1984 Tex. App. LEXIS 6719



November 21, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 157th District Court of Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 83-59245.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and city engineer, sought review of an order of the 157th Judicial District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellee sign company, declaring a portion of a city sign ordinance unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, city and city engineer, refused to allow appellee sign company to repair six hurricane-damaged billboards, which were erected prior to the passage of appellants' sign ordinance; and appellee filed suit. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, finding pertinent portions of the ordinance unconstitutionally vague and void. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the ordinance was violative of due process and fatally vague because the portion of the ordinance appellants relied on to refuse repairs to a sign that a substantial part thereof had been blown down or destroyed did not set out a definition of "substantial parts" or an objective standard by which damage to "substantial parts thereof" could be measured; therefore, the terms of the regulation were so vague, indefinite, and uncertain that men of common intelligence must guess at their meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee sign company because persons of common intelligence were left to guess at the meaning of the portion of the city sign ordinance in question; thus, that portion was unconstitutionally vague and unenforceable by appellants, city and city engineer.
